Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introduction to Mirk al-Masih: Navigating Hanafi Usul Through Commentaries
Introductory front matter and table of contents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three key works related to Mirk al-Masih and explain their hierarchical relationship in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
Commentary chains reveal the living tradition of Hanafi usul: al-Tawdih, al-Talwih, and Mirk al-Masih form a single intellectual conversation.

This first lesson orients you to the book you are studying: Mirk al-Masih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It is not a standalone treatise but a super-commentary that resolves disputes between two earlier works on Hanafi usul al-fiqh. By understanding the structure of this volume, you will learn how to navigate the layered commentaries that define the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three works
Locate the three titles mentioned: al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah, al-Talwih by al-Taftazani, and Mirk al-Masih by the author/compiler.
These are all works of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
2
Understand the hierarchy
Recognize that al-Tawdih is the base text, al-Talwih is a commentary on al-Tawdih, and Mirk al-Masih is a super-commentary that resolves differences between them.
This layered structure is typical in the Hanafi madrasa tradition.
3
Parse the table of contents
Scan the list of topics: vocabulary, rhetorical devices, definitions, objections and answers, and specific usul debates.
The page numbers correspond to the original pagination used in citations.
4
Note the dialectical style
Observe the frequent mention of 'objections and answers' (i'tiradat wa ajwiba). This indicates that the work engages critically with previous scholars.
Dialectic (munazara) is a core method in Hanafi usul.

Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the book, consisting of the title page (page 5) and the table of contents (page 6). The title page gives the book's name as 'Mirk al-Masih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' (The Celestial Ascent for Solving al-Tawdih and al-Talwih). This indicates that the work is a commentary (sharh) on two famous texts of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: 'al-Tawdih' by Sadr al-Shariah and 'al-Talwih' by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The author is described as Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami (but this is likely a later compiler/editor, as the classical author of the original commentary is actually Mulla Khusraw? However, the text says 'afadat Hadrat Mawlana al-Shaykh Abd al-Rahman Jami' — so it may be a collection of his teachings. The table of contents lists over fifty topics, covering vocabulary explanations, rhetorical devices, definitions of key usul terms, objections and answers, and the famous debate between the author (presumably Sadr al-Shariah) and Taftazani. The page numbers refer to the original pagination of the volume. This is typical of classical Islamic scholarly works where the table of contents is placed at the beginning for quick reference.

Key Terms
توضيح (al-Tawdih): Short title of the work 'Al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih' by Sadr al-Shariah al-Mahbubi, a foundational text of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
تلويح (al-Talwih): Short title of the work 'Al-Talwih ila Kashf Asrar al-Tanqih' by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, a commentary on al-Tawdih that often critiques Sadr al-Shariah.
مرك المسيح (Mirk al-Masih): The title of the present volume, meaning 'The Celestial Ascent' (or 'The Ladder of the Messiah') - a super-commentary resolving differences between al-Tawdih and al-Talwih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between al-Tawdih and al-Talwih?
A) Both are by the same author.
B) al-Talwih is a commentary on al-Tawdih.
C) They are unrelated works on different subjects.
D) al-Tawdih is a commentary on al-Talwih.

Key Takeaway
Mirk al-Masih is a super-commentary that harmonizes the Hanafi usul works of Sadr al-Shariah and al-Taftazani.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Miskulmaleeh: Structure of a Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh Commentary
Table of contents listing topics and page numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major sections and key topics of the Miskulmaleeh commentary and use its table of contents to locate specific discussions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A classical usul commentary’s table of contents is the map of its argument — knowing the structure is the first step to mastery.

Tables of contents (faharis) in classical texts are not mere lists; they reveal the author’s pedagogical design and the logical sequence of topics. This lesson unpacks the index of Miskulmaleeh, a major Hanafi commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, so you can navigate its discussions on definitions, sources of law, and dialectical objections with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Scan the major headings
Look at the first few topics: opening words, definitions, and the structure of the book. Notice how the author begins with introductory matters and then moves to substantive usul topics.
The index lists topics in order of appearance; the page numbers indicate the relative depth of coverage.
2
Identify the four primary sources
Locate where the four sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) are mentioned. In this index, they appear around pages 143-148 under 'Statement of the four evidences'.
These sources are the core of usul al-fiqh.
3
Recognize the dialectical sections
Find entries that mention 'objections' or 'answers' — e.g., pages 25, 26, 35, 36, 55, 67, 80, 85, 97, 99, 102, 103. These indicate the author's engagement with opposing views.
Dialectical sections are crucial for understanding rasm al-mufti and tarjih.
4
Note the Hanafi-specific content
Search for 'Imam Abu Hanifa' or specific Hanafi positions. At page 109, there is a clarification of the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa.
This helps in tracing the school's distinctive rulings.
5
Plan your study using page numbers
Choose a topic (e.g., 'hukm') and note the pages: 60 (definition), 72 (shar'i vs. non-shar'i), 67-71 (objections and answers). This sequence guides a systematic reading.
The index is a study tool for the five maqamat: hifz, fahm, naqd, taqyim, tatbiq.

۷۲ حکم کی تعریف (متن)
۶ خطاب کا معنی و سوال و جواب
حکم کے معنی پر معتزلہ کے تین اعتراضات و جوابات
۲۵ خطاب تکلیفی خطاب وضعی کی تحقیق حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ پر اعتراضات
۶۷ پہلے اعتراض کے جوابات دوسرے اعتراض کے جوابات تیسرے اعتراض کے جواب
چوتھے اور پانچویں اعتراضات کے جوابات
اء الشرعیہ کا معنی (متن)
۷۲ حسن و فتح کے شرعی اور عقلی ہونے میں اختلاف
مصنف کی امام رازی کی تردید اس پر اشکال
احکام سے کل بعض مراد ہیں اس کی تحقیق ۷۵ شارح کی وضاحت (متن) دیکھنا بحث سے اشکالات ۷۷ تھیو کی تفسیر اس پر سوالات علم فقہ کی تیسری تعریف از مصنف مسائل قیاسیہ کا علم مجتہد کے لئے ضروری نہیں
۸۰ پچھنا ابحاث سے اعتراضات

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents (fihrist) for the book Miskulmaleehurdusharhaltaozeehwattalweeh, which is a commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It lists the topics covered in the book along with their page numbers. The table reveals the structure of the work: it begins with introductory matters, such as the preface and opening sermon (khutbah), proceeds to definitions of key terms like 'ilm, hukm, and fiqh, and then delves into the four sources of Islamic law (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas). The index also indicates sections on objections and answers, indicating the dialectical style of the text. The last part of the index shows a detailed discussion on the definition of the Quran and the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. The table spans pages 6-7 of the book.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Dedication: Acknowledging the Chain of Knowledge
Author's dedication to Prophet, imams, and teachers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's chain of gratitude and explain its significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Knowledge is a sacred trust received from the Prophet, through the imams, to our teachers.

Dedications in classical texts are not mere formalities; they reveal the author's understanding of the chain of transmission (sanad). This dedication honors the ultimate source of guidance, the intermediaries who codified it, and the personal teachers who imparted it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels of dedication
The author dedicates to the Prophet, then to the mujtahid imams, then to his own teachers. Each level represents a link in the chain of knowledge transmission.
The Prophet is the source, the imams are the interpreters, and the teachers are the direct transmitters.
2
Explain the significance of each level
The Prophet is the ultimate guide. The mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa and his successors) extracted rulings from the Quran and Sunnah. The teachers personally trained the author, passing on the tradition.
The imams are described as extracting pearls, showing their role in deriving law.
3
Connect to the Hanafi emphasis on sanad
The Hanafi school places great importance on the chain of transmission (sanad) for both hadith and fiqh. This dedication mirrors that principle by tracing the author's own lineage.
Understanding this chain helps appreciate the authority of rulings.

besturdubooks.wordpress.com Dedication: I dedicate this book to the benefactor of the universe, the leader of both worlds, the crown of the prophets, Muhammad Mustafa (peace be upon him), and to those great mujtahid imams (may Allah have mercy on them) who extracted pearls from the Quran and Hadith and presented them for the guidance of the Ummah in the form of usul al-fiqh and fiqh. May Allah enlighten their graves and grant them the abode of peace. And also to my great respected teachers (may Allah perpetuate their bounties), under whose special attention and training and through the blessings of their kindness, I received the light of knowledge and was granted the grace of teaching, learning, and authorship. May Allah grant us the ability to walk on the straight path. Amen.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This page contains the author's dedication. He begins by dedicating the book to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), acknowledging him as the ultimate source of guidance. He then dedicates it to the great mujtahid imams, highlighting their role in deriving legal rulings from the primary sources. Finally, he dedicates it to his own teachers, expressing gratitude for their tutelage. This dedication reflects the author's deep respect for the chain of knowledge transmission in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
انتساب (intisāb): Dedication of a book to someone in honor or gratitude.
مجتهدین (mujtahidīn): Scholars qualified to perform ijtihad, specifically the founders of the schools.
ائمہ متبوعین (a'immat mutbū‘īn): The followed imams, i.e., the founders of the four schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The Prophet, the mujtahid imams, and his teachers

Key Takeaway
The dedication reveals the author's recognition of the chain of knowledge from the Prophet through the imams to his own teachers.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Dedication of the Book to the Prophet, Imams, and Teachers
Author dedicates his work to his scholarly lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three levels of dedication in Islamic scholarly works and explain their significance for the transmission of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The dedication traces the chain of knowledge from the Prophet through the imams to the teachers — a living isnad.

This opening dedication (intisab) is not merely a formality; it anchors the work in the living tradition of Islamic scholarship. The author explicitly traces his intellectual lineage, acknowledging the Prophet as the ultimate source, the mujtahid imams as codifiers of usul al-fiqh, and his own teachers as the direct transmitters. Understanding this chain is essential for appreciating the authority and continuity of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recipients
List the three groups mentioned: the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), the mujtahid imams, and the author's teachers.
Note the hierarchical order: Prophet first, then imams, then teachers.
2
Understand the role of each
The Prophet is the source of revelation; the imams extracted rulings from Quran and Hadith; the teachers transmitted this knowledge to the author.
3
Reflect on the author's position
The author places himself as a student receiving from teachers, and as an author passing on the tradition. This highlights the continuity of knowledge transmission.
The author prays for guidance to the straight path, showing humility.

Dedication: I dedicate this book to the Benefactor of the Universe, the Master of Both Worlds, the Crown of the Prophets, Hadrat Muhammad Mustafa (peace be upon him), and to those great mujtahid imams, the followed leaders (may Allah have mercy on them), who extracted pearls from the Quran and Hadith and presented them in the form of usul al-fiqh and fiqh for the guidance of the Muslim ummah; may Allah illuminate their graves and grant them paradise; and to my great respected teachers (may Allah perpetuate their blessings), through whose special attention, training, and shadow of kindness I attained the light of knowledge and was blessed with the grace of teaching, learning, and authorship. May Allah grant me the ability to walk on the straight path. Amen.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the author's dedication (intisab) of his work. It opens by dedicating the book first to the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), the ultimate source of guidance. Then to the great mujtahid imams of the Hanafi school and others, who formulated the sciences of usul al-fiqh and fiqh from the Qur'an and Sunnah. Finally, to his own teachers, through whom he received knowledge. This tripartite dedication reflects the traditional Islamic scholarly chain: the Prophet (primary source), the founding imams (codifiers), and the personal teachers (transmitters). The author acknowledges that his ability to teach, write, and understand is due to their blessings. He ends with a prayer for tawfiq (divine assistance).

Key Terms
انتساب (intisab): Dedication; attributing a work to someone, acknowledging scholarly lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To whom does the author primarily dedicate this book?
A) The Prophet Muhammad only
B) The mujtahid imams only
C) His teachers only
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The dedication of a scholarly work is a critical marker of its place in the chain of transmission, highlighting the Prophet, the imams, and the teachers.

Rationale for Urdu Commentaries in Hanafi Usul Studies
Author explains rationale for an Urdu commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical shift from exclusive reliance on Arabic commentaries to the use of Urdu commentaries as a pedagogical necessity in Hanafi usul studies.

Core Idea
When Arabic proficiency declines, Urdu commentaries become necessary bridges to preserve classical texts.

This lesson examines the author's rationale for producing an Urdu commentary on the foundational Hanafi usul work 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. The author reflects on a time when scholars discouraged Urdu translations, yet the contemporary decline in Arabic fluency now makes them indispensable. Understanding this methodological shift is key to appreciating how classical Hanafi texts remain accessible across generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classical ideal
Note the earlier emphasis on direct engagement with Arabic commentaries for building academic competence and confidence.
This reflects the traditional madrasa pedagogy.
2
Recognize the contemporary problem
Observe the author's assessment that both students and teachers now avoid Arabic commentaries, relying on notes and summaries.
The decline is attributed to lack of Arabic mastery and a preference for ease.
3
Analyze the proposed solution
Understand how the author justifies Urdu commentaries as a necessary bridge, citing the maxim 'what cannot be fully attained should not be entirely abandoned.'
The goal is not to replace Arabic but to provide an entry point.
4
Appreciate the work's pedigree
Recognize the stature of 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' as a core Hanafi usul text, and the credentials of the Urdu commentator.
This establishes the authority and reliability of the present commentary.

اپنی مقبولیت پر شاہد صدیوں سے متداول کبار علمائے امت کے زیر درس رہنے والی علم اصول فقہ کی پلند پایہ جلیل المرتبت توضیح و تلویح کی شرح زیر نظر کتاب مسک الملیح اسی سلسلہ کی ایک کڑی ہے. گرامی قدر حضرت محترم جناب مولانا عبد الرحمن جامی زیدت معالیہم ایک قدیم کہنہ مشق ، حضرات اساتذہ کرام کے معتمد اور طلباء کرام میں مسند محبوبیت پر فائز : عظیم استاذ و مدارس ہیں ذوق تدریس کے ساتھ الکریم ابن الکریم کی فضیلت کے بھی حامل ہیں... دار العام کبیر والا کے زمانہ تدریس میں ہزاروں طلباء کرام میں مشکل ترین اسباق سھل ترین انداز میں پڑھانے کے ماہر مانے جاتے تھے۔ ملکہ تفہیم کے
Misk al-Maleeh. Dark opening. From Muhammad and our honored, a model of predecessors, Sheikh al-Qurra Hadrat Maulana Qari Muhammad Uralis Sahib Hoshyarpuri (may his shadow continue), manager of Jamia Darul Uloom Rahimiya Multan. Completed with Misk. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah? and prayers be upon His? ... Commentary on al-[?]. There was a time when our respected elders considered an Urdu commentary extremely harmful and unbeneficial for academic competence. Students were advised not to keep an Urdu commentary under study but to benefit from Arabic commentaries, which not only solidify competence but also create a taste for study and develop breadth and self-confidence in the heart and mind. Without this, the idea of becoming a teacher was not conceived. In this era, with a lack of competence and capability, natures have also become easygoing. Not only students, but teachers also directly rely on dictations, notes, and memory, and avoid studying Arabic commentaries. Except what my Lord wills. This era of scientific decline has ultimately brought us to the point that things previously avoided with gusto are now considered necessary. Consequently, Urdu commentaries of Arabic books are appearing in the public view from the pens of many scholars, so that due to lack of mastery in Arabic, the ancient sciences may not be lost. Therefore, this matter has come to be considered a boon: if a student, after studying an Urdu commentary, can apply it to the Arabic books. According to the maxim 'What cannot be fully attained should not be entirely abandoned,' it is much better; otherwise, there is fear that today's student will become unfamiliar with the terminology of the early scholars, and thus the relationship with the heritage of the fathers (those books) will be severed. The popularity of this book witnesses that the commentary of Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a lofty and exalted book on usul al-fiqh that has been taught under great scholars of the ummah for centuries, is now presented in this Urdu commentary 'Misk al-Maleeh'. The honorable, respected Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jami (may his excellencies increase) is an old experienced, trustworthy of the respected teachers, and seated on the throne of love among students; he is a great teacher and educator, possessing the virtue of the 'noble son of the noble' along with teaching zeal... In his teaching period at Dar al-Ulum Kabeer Wala, he was considered an expert in teaching the most difficult lessons in the easiest way among thousands of students. The faculty of understanding...
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his Urdu commentary 'Misk al-Maleeh' on the classical usul al-fiqh work 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. The author opens by recalling that earlier scholars discouraged Urdu commentaries, advocating direct study of Arabic commentaries to build competence. However, due to a decline in Arabic proficiency, both students and teachers now rely on paraphrases and notes, avoiding Arabic commentaries. The author argues that this decline necessitates Urdu commentaries as a bridge, following the maxim 'what cannot be fully attained should not be entirely abandoned.' He presents his commentary as a response to this need, enabling students to eventually apply it to the original Arabic texts. He then praises the original work 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' and its author (the commentator). Finally, he introduces the author of this Urdu commentary, Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jami, highlighting his teaching experience and skill. The passage thus establishes the rationale, methodology, and credentials behind the present work.

Key Terms
اردو شرح (Urdu sharh): A commentary written in Urdu language on an Arabic original work.
توضیح و تلویح (al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih): A famous Hanafi usul al-fiqh work: al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Talwih by al-Taftazani.
مالا یدرک کله لا یترک کله (Ma la yudraku kulluhu la yutraku kulluhu): A maxim meaning 'What cannot be fully attained should not be entirely abandoned.' It justifies partial acquisition when full attainment is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author believe Urdu commentaries have become necessary?
A) Arabic commentaries are not available
B) Students and teachers lack Arabic proficiency
C) Urdu is now the international language of Islam
D) The original Arabic books are lost

Key Takeaway
Urdu commentaries on classical Hanafi works are a pragmatic response to declining Arabic proficiency, intended as bridges to, not replacements for, the original Arabic texts.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Necessity of Urdu Commentaries for Usul al-Fiqh
Prefatory remarks on the need for Urdu commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why later Hanafi scholars produced Urdu commentaries on classical usul al-fiqh works and identify the key figure involved.

Core Idea
When Arabic proficiency declined, Urdu commentaries became necessary to preserve access to classical Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

This passage from the introduction to Misk al-Malih describes the historical shift in scholarly attitudes toward Urdu commentaries. It explains that while elders once considered Urdu commentaries harmful, declining Arabic skills forced a pragmatic approach to keep classical texts accessible. The author then introduces his teacher, Maulana Abdur Rahman Jami, as the commentator who undertook this vital task.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical problem
The passage states that in earlier times, scholars considered Urdu commentaries harmful for developing academic aptitude. Students were urged to use Arabic commentaries. However, a decline in Arabic proficiency has made it difficult for students to engage directly with Arabic texts.
This reflects a tension between ideal and reality in Islamic education.
2
Understand the solution
The author argues that producing Urdu commentaries has become necessary to prevent the loss of classical knowledge. He cites the principle 'ma la yudrak kulluh la yutrak kulluh' (what cannot be fully achieved should not be entirely abandoned).
This is a common legal maxim applied to educational necessity.
3
Recognize the scholar and his credentials
The passage introduces Maulana Abdur Rahman Jami as a veteran teacher with decades of experience, trusted by senior scholars and beloved by students. He is praised for his ability to simplify difficult texts, such as Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih.
His lineage is also noted as 'al-Karim ibn al-Karim', indicating noble descent.

Misk al-Malih. Dark openings by Muhammad and our honored one, the model of predecessors, Shaykh al-Qurra Hadhrat Maulana Qari Muhammad Uwais Sahab Hoshiarpuri (may his shadow prolong) manager of Jami'a Darul Uloom Rahimiya Multan. Concluded by Misk. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah and prayers be upon His family and companions. Explanation of al-... There was a time when our elders considered Urdu commentary extremely harmful and unbeneficial for academic aptitude. Students were urged to benefit from Arabic commentaries instead of studying Urdu commentary, because that not only strengthens aptitude but also creates a taste for study and develops breadth and self-confidence in the heart and mind. Without this, becoming a teacher was inconceivable. In this era, with the lack of aptitude and ability, people's natures have become ease-loving. Not only students, but even teachers directly rely on dictation, notes, and memory, and shy away from studying Arabic commentaries. Except what my Lord wills. This era of decline has ultimately brought us to the point that things previously avoided by taste are now considered necessary. Consequently, many elders have started publishing Urdu commentaries of Arabic books, lest ancient knowledge perish due to lack of mastery of Arabic. Hence, it began to be considered a boon if a student, after studying Urdu commentary, could apply it to Arabic books. In accordance with 'what cannot be fully achieved should not be entirely abandoned', it is much better; otherwise, there is fear that today's student will become unfamiliar with the terminology of the early scholars and thus lose connection with the heritage of the fathers (those books). The book under view, Misk al-Malih, a commentary of Tawdih and Talwih – lofty and majestic works on usul al-fiqh that have been taught for centuries by great scholars – is a link in this chain. The honored respected Hadhrat Maulana Abdur Rahman Jami (may their excellences be prolonged) is an ancient veteran, trusted by the senior teachers, and seated on the throne of love among students: a great teacher of madrasas. Along with a taste for teaching, he is also possessor of the virtue of al-Karim ibn al-Karim. During his teaching period at Dar al-Ilm Kabir Wala, he was considered expert in teaching the most difficult lessons in the easiest manner to thousands of students. Due to his ability to explain, students were eager that our lesson be with Hadhrat Ustadh. After his long teaching career, since he honored Jami'a Darul Uloom Rahimiya (Multan) with his association, his personality is introduced through this reference. Students are eager to study difficult books with him. He is first and last a teacher, and in the field of teaching, he is not intimidated by any book, and the example of 'kneading and feeding' applies to him. The academic status and position of Tawdih and Talwih in their field is undisputed. And the annotations of Allama Taftazani (may Allah have mercy on him) make the book more subtle rather than easier. Our master's father (may his blessings continue) said in one sentence considering his lofty rank and lifelong teaching experience: 'Taftazani's commentary is fit for criticism'. At the beginning of the year, when the stage of lesson distribution comes in madrasas and universities, teachers have to consider which teacher should be given such type of books. Teachers are not voluntarily ready to bear this burden. In this declining academic atmosphere, it can be seen that students also consider it a heavy lesson. It is the incomplete thought of this incapable one that if the curriculum binding under the system of Wifaq al-Madaris al-Arabiyya Pakistan were not mandatory, perhaps many madrasas would have removed it from the curriculum. Hadhrat Jami (may his glory increase), feeling this, introduced it in Urdu garb, and thus not only brought his academic benefits out of the four walls of the lecture hall into the academic world, which is evidence of his confidence in teaching, but also created a good means for those students who cannot benefit directly from him to also enjoy his great invaluable academic gift. Along with adorning the chair of hadith at Jami'a Darul Uloom Rahimiya, he is currently benefiting students in rational sciences with his expert command. Also, three years after his arrival, the department of Ifta and Specialization in Fiqh was established, in which he has a notable share. This is from Allah a sign of his acceptance and benefit, that his pure breaths, instead of being limited to the classroom, through the pen, as a compassionate teacher, for the imperfect the perfect, for the perfect a guide, are proving to be a correct path for the respected teachers and students. The beneficiaries hope that they will reach the conclusion: 'Musk is that which emits its own fragrance, not what the perfumer says.'
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is the front matter (introduction) of the Urdu commentary Misk al-Malih on the classical usul al-fiqh works Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. The author begins by lamenting the decline in academic standards, where even teachers rely on notes rather than study Arabic commentaries. He explains that Urdu commentaries, once discouraged, have become necessary to preserve Islamic knowledge for students who lack strong Arabic. He then praises the author of this commentary, Maulana Abdur Rahman Jami, extolling his teaching expertise and his noble lineage. The introduction notes the difficulty of Taftazani's Al-Talwih, quoting Jami's father who said it is more a work of criticism than explanation. The passage ends with a Persian couplet emphasizing that true value is intrinsic, not proclaimed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the introduction, why did the author produce an Urdu commentary of Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih?
A) Because Arabic commentaries are too expensive.
B) Because students' Arabic proficiency has declined, making Urdu explanation necessary.
C) Because the original Arabic texts are lost.
D) Because the author wanted to replace Arabic with Urdu in all subjects.

Key Takeaway
The production of Urdu commentaries reflects a pragmatic adaptation by Hanafi scholars to ensure the survival of usul al-fiqh education in the face of declining Arabic fluency.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Introduction to Al-Tawdih, Al-Talwih, and the Need for Accessible Commentaries
Author's preface praising the need and merit of this Urdu commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the respective roles of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih in Hanafi usul and explain the pedagogical motivation behind the Urdu commentary Misk al-Malih.

Core Idea
Al-Tawdih and al-Talwih are core but difficult; accessible commentaries bridge the gap for students.

This lesson introduces two foundational texts of Hanafi usul al-fiqh — al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Talwih by al-Taftazani. The preface to Misk al-Malih describes the challenges students face and the need for a clear Urdu commentary. Understanding this context helps you appreciate the scholarly effort behind making complex usul principles accessible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual context
What are the two books being commented upon? Who authored them? What is their status in Hanafi usul?
This sets the stage for understanding the commentary.
2
Recognize the problem stated
According to the preface, what difficulties do teachers and students face with these texts? Why was there a need for an Urdu explanation?
The preface explicitly mentions that al-Talwih increases difficulty and that many would drop the book.
3
Understand the commentator's approach
How does the commentary Misk al-Malih address the difficulty? What features does it include (e.g., grammatical analysis, easy style)?
The commentary aims to be clear, with resolutions of difficulties.
4
Appreciate the scholarly chain
Who is the teacher (Hazrat Jami) and his role? How does this commentary fit into the tradition of sharh?
The commentary is based on the teacher's lectures and experience.

لحاظ سے طلباء کرام کا اشتیاق ہوتا تھا کہ ہمارا سبق حضرت استاذ کے پاس ہو ۔ اپنے میں سالہ دور تدریس کے بعد جب سے جامعہ دار العلوم رحیمیہ (ملتان) کو اپنی وابستگی کا شرف بخشا ہے ان کی شخصیت کا تعارف اسی حوالہ سے ہورہا ہے۔ طلباء کرام ادق کتب ان کے پاس پڑھنے کے خواہاں ہوتے ہیں۔ وہ اول و آخر مدرس ہیں اور میدان تدریس میں محمد و تعالی وہ کتاب سے مرعوب نہیں ہوتے اور گھول کر پلانے کے کی تمثیل ان پر صادق آتی ہے۔ توضیح و تویخ کی اپنے فن میں علمی حیثیت و مقام مسلّم البوت ہے ۔ اور حضرت علامہ تفتازانی مرحوم کی جولانیاں کتاب کو سہل کرنے کی بجائے مزید دقت نظر کی حامل بنادیتی ہیں۔ جس کو ہمارے مخدوم حضرت جامی صاحب دامت بر کاتہم کے والد گرامی نے اپنے بزرگانہ مقام و عظمت اور زندگی بھر کے تدریسی تجربہ کے لحاظ سے ایک جملہ میں ارشاد فرمایا ہے کہ تفتازانی کی شرح تو " جرح کا مقام رکھتی ہے۔ ابتداء سال میں جب مدارس و جامعات میں تقسیم اسباق کا مرحلہ آتا ہے تو اساتذہ کرام پر نظر دوڑانی پڑتی ہے کہ ایسی نوعیت کی کتب کس استاذ کو دی جائیں۔ اساتذہ کرام اس بوجھ کو اٹھانے کے لئے از خود تیار نہیں ہوتے اسی گرتی ہوئی علمی فضا کے تناظر میں دیکھا جا سکتا ہے کہ طلباء کرام بھی اس کو بوجھل سبق تصور کرتے ہیں . اس نا کارہ کا ناقص خیال ہے اگر وفاق المدارس العربیہ
پاکستان کے نظام کے تحت نصاب کی پابندی لازمی نہ ہوتی تو شاید بہت سے مدارس اس کو نصاب سے ہی خارج کر دیں۔ حضرت اقدس جامی صاحب زید مجدہم نے اس چیز کو محسوس کرتے ہوئے اس کو اردو کے لباس میں متعارف کرا کر نہ صرف یہ کہ اپنے فیوض علمیہ کو درس گاہ کی چاردیواری سے نکال کر علمی دنیا میں پیش کیا ، جو ان کے ذوق تدریس کے اعتماد کی دلیل ہے۔ بلکہ وہ طلباء کرام جو ان سے براور است استفادہ نہیں کر سکتے وہ بھی ان کے عظیم بیش بہا علمی تحفہ سے بہرہ مند ہو سکیں گے ان کے لئے بھی اچھی صورت پیدا کر دی۔
جامعہ دار العلوم رحیمیہ کی مسند حدیث کو رونق بخشنے کے ساتھ اس وقت وہ علوم عقلیہ میں بھی اپنی ماہرانہ دسترس سے طلباء کرام کو فائدہ پہنچارہے ہیں نیز جامعہ میں ان کے آنے کے تین سال بعد افتاء وتخص فی الفقہ کا جو شعبہ قائم ہوا اس میں بھی ان کا قابل ذکر حصہ ہے۔ یہ منجانب اللہ انکی قبولیت ونافعیت کی دلیل ہے کہ ان کے انفاس طیبہ درس گاہ تک محدود رہنے کی بجائے قلم کے ذریعہ ایک مشفق استاذ کی حیثیت سے

Misk al-Malih
Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
From the perspective, students used to desire that our lesson be with the teacher. After his many years of teaching, since he honored Jamia Darul Uloom Rahimiya (Multan) with his affiliation, his personality is being introduced in this context. Students wish to read precise books with him. He is a teacher first and last, and in the field of teaching, he is not intimidated by any book, and the example of 'dissolving and feeding' applies to him. Al-Tawdih and al-Talwih have an acknowledged scholarly status and rank in their field. And the annotations of the late Allama Taftazani make the book more profound rather than easier. Regarding this, our honored master, Hazrat Jami Sahib (may his blessings endure), his noble father said in one sentence based on his high station and lifelong teaching experience that Taftazani's commentary is 'worthy of criticism.' At the beginning of the year, when the stage of lesson distribution comes in madrasas and universities, teachers have to look around to see which teacher should be given such books. Teachers are not ready to bear this burden themselves. In the context of this declining academic atmosphere, it can be seen that students also consider it a heavy lesson. This incompetence's flawed opinion is that if it were not for the mandatory curriculum under the system of Wifaq al-Madaris al-Arabiyya Pakistan, perhaps many madrasas would have removed it from the curriculum. Hazrat Aqdas Jami Sahib (may his glory increase), feeling this, introduced it in the garb of Urdu, thereby not only bringing his scholarly bounties out of the classroom and presenting them to the academic world, which is evidence of his confidence in teaching, but also those students who cannot directly benefit from him can also benefit from his great invaluable scholarly gift, and a good means was created for them.
Along with adorning the hadith chair of Jamia Darul Uloom Rahimiya, he is currently benefiting students with his expert command in rational sciences. Also, after three years of his arrival at the university, he had a notable share in the department of Ifta and Takhassus in Fiqh that was established. This is a sign from Allah of his acceptance and benefit, that his blessed breathings, instead of being confined to the classroom, through the pen, as a kind teacher, as 'the imperfect for the perfect, the perfect for the guide', are proving to be a correct path for teachers and students. It is hoped that the beneficiaries will reach the conclusion:
'Musk is that which smells by itself, not what the perfumer says.'

Misk al-Malih
Sharh al-Tawdih
There are other Urdu commentaries of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, but with eloquent expression, continuity of text, easy-to-understand style, resolution of vocabulary along with grammatical constructions, besturduboo
text difficult, student-like questions and answers, and beneficial benefits, this commentary containing such distinguishing qualities desires that it be called the 'seal' (Misk): 'And for that let the competitors compete.' (Quran 83:26)
Considering the noble command of respected brother Hazrat Jami Sahib (may his glory increase), and keeping in view 'al-Amr fawq al-Adab' (the matter is above courtesy), I have penned a few disorganized letters, otherwise, the writing of someone like me without means has no rank for a commentary that has such high status and grandeur.
Prayer: May it be accepted in the pure court of Allah Almighty and cause an increase of love in his heart, and may the students get a abundant share in the ongoing charities. Ameen.
If accepted, it is honor and nobility.
Wa al-Salaam
Muhammad Idris
Servant of Jamia Darul Uloom Rahimiya, Multan
31 December 1862 [2004-11-25?]
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the preface to 'Misk al-Malih', an Urdu commentary on the classical works 'Al-Tawdih' by Sadr al-Shari'ah and 'Al-Talwih' by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, which are core texts in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, Muhammad Idris, introduces the context and necessity of this work. He describes the high scholarly status of the original books and acknowledges that Taftazani's annotations, while profound, increase the difficulty. The preface notes that both teachers and students find these texts challenging, to the point that many would drop them from the curriculum if not mandatory. The commentator, Hazrat Jami Sahib (referring to the teacher and scholar whose father also commented on Taftazani), aimed to make these works accessible by producing an Urdu explanation. This commentary is characterized by clear expression, grammatical analysis, and student-friendly explanations, including resolutions of difficulties. The author expresses humility, stating that he is merely writing at the behest of his teacher. The preface concludes with a prayer for acceptance and benefit. This front matter sets the stage for the technical usul discussions to follow, emphasizing the pedagogical purpose of the work.

Key Terms
التوضيح (al-Tawdih): A foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh text by Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Mahbubi, known for its concise yet precise exposition of usul principles.
التلويح (al-Talwih): A gloss by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on al-Tawdih, which critically engages with and expands upon the source text, often adding depth and complexity.
مسک الملیح (Misk al-Malih): The title of this Urdu commentary, meaning 'The Pleasant Musk', alluding to the Quranic verse 'مِسْكٌ وَفِي ذَٰلِكَ فَلْيَتَنَافَسِ الْمُتَنَافِسُونَ' (83:26).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the author of the preface highlights the difficulty of al-Talwih?
A) To criticize al-Taftazani for poor scholarship.
B) To justify the need for an accessible Urdu commentary.
C) To discourage students from studying the text.
D) To demonstrate his own mastery of the subject.

Key Takeaway
The preface establishes that Misk al-Malih is a necessary tool for students to grasp the complex usul discussions in al-Tawdih and al-Talwih.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of Taqriz and Core Texts in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Three scholars praise the Urdu commentary on Tawdih and Talwih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two core Hanafi usul texts (al-Tawdih and al-Talwih) and explain the function of scholarly endorsements (taqriz) in establishing a commentary's credibility.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements and mastery of core texts ensure reliable transmission of Hanafi usul.

This lesson examines the front matter of an Urdu commentary on the advanced Hanafi usul texts al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Such endorsements (taqriz) are a traditional feature of Islamic scholarly works, serving to authenticate the author and guide students. Understanding this context prepares you to appreciate the authority of the commentary and the texts it explains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the endorsers
Read the endorsements and note the names and credentials of each scholar. They are described as teachers of hadith and directors of Islamic seminaries, indicating their high standing.
The endorsers are Mawlana Ghulam Yasin, Mawlana Muhammad Yasin Sabir, and Mawlana Abdul Majeed.
2
Identify the core texts
The commentary is on al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'a and its supercommentary al-Talwih by al-Taftazani. Both are foundational in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
Al-Tawdih is the matn (core text), al-Talwih is its sharh (commentary).
3
Understand the need for the commentary
The endorsers note that students found these texts difficult, and the author’s long teaching experience qualified him to write a clear Urdu explanation.
The commentary is praised for being 'easy and comprehensive'.
4
Recognize the function of taqriz
Taqriz (endorsements) serve to recommend the work, establish the author’s credibility, and encourage students to study it. They also indicate the scholarly network behind the publication.
These endorsements are typical for traditional madrasa curricula.

۲۵ رمضان المبارک ۱۴۲۵ھ
Misk al-Maleeh (The Fragrant Musk) – 413 – Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Qalam [sic]. Esteemed opinion of the teacher of scholars and students, master of scholars, Hadrat Mawlana Ghulam Yasin Sahib (may his shade be prolonged), teacher of Hadith and director of Jamia Islamiya Lilbanat, Tunsa Sharif. Praising and sending blessings. It is a matter of utmost joy and happiness that dear Mawlana Jami Sahib (may his honor increase) has taken up his pen on the most difficult and problematic book of the higher level, al-Tawdih with al-Talwih. Before this, such an easy and comprehensive commentary has not passed before the eyes. My dear Jami Sahib is among my worthy and reliable students, and he taught for sixteen years under my supervision at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala. Allah Almighty has granted him a powerful ability for explanation and acceptance among students. Previously, his commentaries 'Abr al-Yam and Tuhfa Ilmiyya have gained fame in scholarly circles. My prayer is that Allah, whose glory is great, may grant full acceptance in His court to the work of resolving [the difficulties of] al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, and make it a means of progress and success in both worlds for the author (Amin). Your servant Ghulam Yasin, forgiven, servant of Jamia Islamiya Lilbanat Tunsa Sharif. Esteemed opinion of the teacher of scholars, Hadrat Mawlana Muhammad Yasin Sahib Sabir (may his shade be prolonged), teacher of Hadith at Jamia Umar ibn al-Khattab Multan. In the name of Allah, the Most High. It became known with pleasure that my brother Hadrat Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Sahib Jami has written a commentary in Urdu on al-Tawdih with al-Talwih. MashaAllah, it is a very good commentary; the style of elucidation and explanation seems unique. In every era, scholarly works have continued and will continue. Fortunate are those scholars who were granted the ability for such great works, and among them is the aforementioned brother. Along with teaching, he has abundant enthusiasm for authorship and compilation; he is famous among students. May Allah, exalted is His glory, grant him further progress in knowledge and perfection (Amin). Your humble servant Muhammad Yasin Sabir, may you be forgiven, teacher at Jamia Umar ibn al-Khattab Multan. [PAGE_015] Misk al-Maleeh – Commentary on al-Tawdih and – Esteemed opinion of the shaykh of shaykhs, Hadrat Mawlana Abdul Majeed Sahib (may his shade be prolonged), teacher of Hadith and director of Jamia Qasimiyya Sharaf al-Islam Chowk Sarwar Shahid. besturdubooks.w.com In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Allah is Muhammad with all His attributes, and Muhammad is Allah, may peace be upon him despite the loftiness of His essence. To proceed: The principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh) is among the most important of the higher sciences, through which the principles, rules, and realities of jurisprudence and understanding are perceived. Pious scholars in every era have paid attention to this science. Allama Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud (d. 747 AH) and Allama Sa'd al-Din Mas'ud ibn Umar al-Taftazani (d. 792 AH) are both mountains of knowledge and shining lights among the researchers of the eighth century. The former's al-Tawdih and the latter's commentary al-Talwih are standard foundational books of usul al-fiqh. In every era they have been part of the curriculum, and now too they are included in the syllabus of Wifaq al-Madaris. Because of these books being the most abstruse in usul al-fiqh, students of the Arabic sciences felt great difficulty in understanding them. There was a need for a researching scholar to write a commentary in Urdu. Allah the Generous granted the honor to dear respected Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jati, principal of Jamia Hafsah Lilbanat Muzaffargarh and teacher of Hadith at Jamia Dar al-Ulum Rahimiya Multan, that he authored an excellent Urdu commentary in a scholarly style on the mentioned book, thus solving the difficulty of the students. In the center of learning, Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, for a long time the mentioned book remained under Mawlana's teaching, therefore he appears to be well aware of the book's ins and outs, and explains matters with full research. From the depth of the heart, prayer is made that Allah the Generous may grant this commentary general acceptance, and make it a means of raising the ranks of the author. Amin, then Amin. This prayer from me and from the whole world, may it be accepted. Muhammad Abdul Majeed, may Allah forgive him, servant of the sciences, Jamia Qasimiyya Chowk Sarwar Shahid, District Muzaffargarh. 25 Ramadan al-Mubarak 1425 AH.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage comprises the front matter of the book 'Misk al-Maleeh', containing endorsements (taqriz) from three scholars: Mawlana Ghulam Yasin, Mawlana Muhammad Yasin Sabir, and Mawlana Abdul Majeed. Each praises the author, Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami, for his Urdu commentary on the difficult usul al-fiqh texts 'al-Tawdih' by Sadr al-Shari'a and 'al-Talwih' by Taftazani. They highlight the commentary's clarity and scholarly value, noting that the author taught these texts for sixteen years at Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, giving him deep expertise. The endorsements are typical of traditional Islamic scholarly works, serving to establish the book's credibility and recommend it to students. There is no legal content; this is purely introductory.

Key Terms
توضیح (al-Tawdih): The matn (core text) on usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud (d. 747 AH).
تلویح (al-Talwih): The commentary on al-Tawdih by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani (d. 792 AH).
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): The science of the principles of Islamic jurisprudence, by which rulings are derived from their sources.
تقریظ (taqriz): A scholarly endorsement or commendation, typically found at the beginning of a book, written by respected scholars to recommend the work and establish its credibility.

The Significance of Usul al-Fiqh and the Role of Commentaries
Endorsement promoting a commentary on usul al-fiqh texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why usul al-fiqh is considered a foundational science in the Hanafi tradition and identify the key texts and scholars mentioned in the endorsement.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the key to unlocking the principles and rules of fiqh.

This endorsement from Muhammad Abdul Majeed introduces an Urdu commentary on the classical usul al-fiqh works al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. It underscores the central role of usul al-fiqh in Islamic scholarship and the need for accessible explanations for students. Understanding this context helps appreciate the continuity of Hanafi learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Purpose of an Endorsement
Recognize that a taqriz is a scholarly recommendation used to introduce and validate a new work, often highlighting its utility and the author's credentials.
Classical endorsements serve as a form of scholarly peer review.
2
Locate the Key Texts and Their Authors
Note that al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar and al-Talwih by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani are two foundational texts of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
Both authors are highly respected 8th-century Hanafi scholars.
3
Understand the Need for the Commentary
The endorsement states that students found these texts difficult, and Maulana Abdur Rahman Jati wrote an Urdu commentary to make them accessible.
This reflects the ongoing tradition of producing commentaries to facilitate learning.
4
Appreciate the Commentator’s Qualifications
The endorser praises Maulana’s long teaching experience with the texts, ensuring his commentary is based on deep understanding.
Teaching experience is a mark of authority in the Hanafi tradition.
5
Reflect on the Broader Significance
Usul al-fiqh is described as one of the most important sciences, essential for deriving legal rulings from primary sources. The commentary helps students master these principles.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on systematic reasoning.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Allah (is described) by all His attributes, and Muhammad (peace be upon him) with elevation of his essence. As to what follows: The principles of jurisprudence (Usul al-Fiqh) is one of the most important among the lofty sciences, through which one gains understanding of the principles, rules and realities of fiqh and jurisprudence. The pious scholars in every era have paid attention to this science. Allamah Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar 'Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud (d. 747 AH) and Allamah Sa'd al-Din Mas'ud ibn 'Umar al-Taftazani (d. 792 AH) are both mountains of knowledge and brilliant lights among the researchers of the eighth century. The former's al-Tawdih and the latter's al-Talwih are standard foundational books of usul al-fiqh. They have been part of the curriculum in every era, and are still included in the syllabus of Wafaq al-Madaris. Because these are the most abstruse books of usul al-fiqh, students of Arabic sciences found great difficulty in understanding them. There was a need for a researcher scholar to write a commentary in Urdu. Allah the Generous granted success to the dear respected Maulana Abdur Rahman Jati, the chief of Jamia Hafsah Lilbanat Muzaffargarh and teacher of Hadith at Jamia Darul Uloom Rahimiya Multan, that he authored an excellent Urdu commentary of the mentioned book in a scholarly style, solving the students' difficulty. At the center of knowledge, Darul Uloom Kabirwala, the mentioned book was taught by Maulana for a long time, so he seems well acquainted with its ins and outs, and explains matters with full research. From the depths of the heart, a prayer that Allah the Generous grants this commentary general acceptance and makes it a means of elevation for the author. Ameen, Thumma Ameen. This prayer is from me and from all the world. Ameen.
Muhammad Abdul Majeed, may Allah forgive him

He explains the need for an Urdu commentary and praises the author's qualifications, noting his long teaching experience with the text. The endorsement ends with a prayer for acceptance.

Contextualizing al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: The Commentary's Value
Third endorsement highlighting the difficulty and commentary's role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of the commentary and state why al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih are considered difficult texts in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih are abstruse usul texts; this commentary makes them accessible.

This lesson introduces the third endorsement by Muhammad Ashraf Shad, which emphasizes the difficulty of the core texts al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih and the value of the commentary Misk al-Malih. Understanding the nature of these source texts helps appreciate the need for careful study in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of an endorsement
Recognize that a taqriz (endorsement) authenticates the work, recommends it to readers, and often highlights its unique benefits.
Endorsements are common in classical texts to establish scholarly credibility.
2
Locate the description of the original texts
Find the phrases that describe al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih as 'extremely abstruse' and 'difficult', requiring 'deep study'.
This sets the expectation for the student.
3
Note the role of the commentary
The commentary is presented as a 'great favor' that makes the difficult original accessible to 'comfort-seeking students'.
The commentary does not replace the original but explains it.
4
Recognize prior works of the author
The author's earlier successful commentaries (e.g., Tuhfah 'Ilmiyah, 'Anbar al-Yam) attest to his expertise in writing beneficial explications.
This builds confidence in the commentary's quality.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. As to what follows: al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih are extremely abstruse and difficult books in usul al-fiqh, requiring deep study to understand them. The esteemed Maulana Abdur Rahman Jami has done a great favor upon the comfort-seeking students of this era by writing its Urdu commentary named 'Misk al-Malih fi Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. It is hoped that the students will appreciate it. The respected author has previously also written some very beneficial commentaries, which students have eagerly accepted, for example Tuhfah 'Ilmiyah li al-Tarkib and in tafsir 'Anbar al-Yam fi Tafsir 'Am. Prayer that Allah Almighty grants this commentary general acceptance like the original, and grants the author and all concerned success in both worlds. Ameen, O Lord of the worlds.
The weak servant Muhammad Ashraf, Jamia Mazahir al-Ulum Kot Addu
Jumada al-Ula 1425 AH corresponding to 25 June 2004

Key Terms

التلويح (al-Talwih): A commentary on al-Tawdih by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, itself a standard text in usul.
مسك المليح (Misk al-Malih): The Urdu commentary being endorsed, written by Maulana Abdur Rahman Jami.

Introducing Misk al-Malih: A Commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
Endorsements introducing a new commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose and significance of the commentary Misk al-Malih and identify its place in the Hanafi usul al-fiqh curriculum.

Core Idea
A balanced commentary on a difficult usul text, tailored for student accessibility.

This front matter introduces the Urdu commentary 'Misk al-Malih' on 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih', a standard Hanafi usul text. The endorsements explain why a new commentary was needed and what makes this one valuable. Understanding the context helps appreciate the pedagogical role of commentary literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' is a foundational Hanafi usul work, consisting of Sadr al-Sharia's matn and Taftazani's supercommentary.
This text is part of the Dars Nizami curriculum.
2
Recognize the problem with previous commentaries
According to Munir Ahmad, earlier commentaries were either too lengthy or too concise, causing difficulty for teachers and students.
The commentary addresses this by being 'moderate'.
3
Note the key features of this commentary
It is written in simple Urdu, includes responses to Taftazani's objections, and aims for clarity and balance.
Both endorsers emphasize its accessibility and comprehensiveness.

اما بعد : " التوضيح والتلويح وفاق المدارس الاسلامیہ کے نصاب کے مطابق اصول فقہ کی آخری کتاب ہے جو صل عبارت اور مقاصد کتاب کے اعتبار سے متعلق ترین ہے۔ ابتک اس کے متعدد حواشی لکھے جاچکے ہیں جن میں سے بعض میں بہت طوالت ہے ، بعض میں بہت اختصار ہے۔ جس کی وجہ سے اساتذہ کرام کو تو ضیح وتلویح کے پڑھانے میں بہت وقت و مشقت کا سامنا کرنا پڑتا تھا۔ الحمد اللہ رب العالمین۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے حضرت العلام شیخ الحدیث حضرت مولانا عبد الرحمن صاحب جامی کو تو فیق خاص سے نوازا۔ انہوں نے توضیح و تلویح کے ایک معتد بہ حصہ کی نہایت عمدہ، عام فہم ۔ آسان ترین ایسی شرح تحریر فرمائی ہے جو معتدل ہے اور طوالت عمل اختصار محل سے پاک ہے جس میں تنقیح عبارت ،حل عبارت، توضیح اغراض ۔ اور حل مقاصد کا حق ادا کیا ہے۔ علامہ تفتازانی کی طرف سے جگہ بہ جگہ ماتن پر دارد کئے گئے اعتراضات کے جوابات کا التزام بھی کیا گیا ہے۔ دعا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ اس شرح کو عند اللہ وعند الناس قبولیت تامہ عطا فرما کر اس کے فیض کو ہمیشہ ہمیشہ کیلئے عام تام کرے۔ فقط والسلام عليكم ورحمة الله و بركاته
منیر احمد غفرلہ استاذ الحدیث والتفسیر جامہ اسلامیہ باب العلوم کروڑ پکا
In the name of Allah, the All-Knowing. Praising and praying. In a brief glance in a short time, I have seen the commentary written by respected Mawlana Abdur Rahman Jami Sahib, hadith scholar of Darul Uloom Rahimiya, entitled 'Misk al-Salih hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' at a few places. MashaAllah, he has written it with research and accuracy, and explained it with easy-to-understand and fluent Urdu. He has taught Tawdih and Talwih for many years at Darul Uloom Eidgah Kabirwala; he is a famous teacher. Therefore, this commentary will inshaAllah be very beneficial for students. May Allah accept this effort and deed of his, make it a continuous charity (Ameen), and grant it honor of acceptance among the people of knowledge. Ameen. Bism. Only, the supplicant: Muhammad Ashraf Shad, Ashrafabad, Jamia Ashrafiya Mankot, Tehsil Kabirwala, District Khanewal. Opinion of the esteemed teacher of scholars, Hazrat Mawlana Muhammad Ashraf Sahib (may his shadow be extended), hadith scholar of Madrasa Mazahir-ul-Ulum Kot Adu. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: Tawdih and Talwih is an extremely precise and difficult book in Usul al-Fiqh, requiring deep study to understand. The honored Mawlana Abdur Rahman Jami Sahib has done a great favor on the convenience-loving students of this era by writing its Urdu commentary named 'Misk al-Salih fi Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. It is hoped that the respected students will appreciate it. The author has also written some other very beneficial commentaries before, which students have eagerly received, such as Tuhfah Ilmiyah for grammar and in tafsir 'Anbar al-Yam fi Tafsir Am'. Dua that Allah grants this commentary general acceptance like the original, and grants the author and all concerned success in both worlds. Ameen ya Rabb al-Alameen. The weak servant Muhammad Ashraf, Jamia Mazahir-ul-Ulum Kot Adu. Jumada al-Ula 1425 AH / 25 June 2004 CE. Misk al-Malih Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Opinion of the esteemed monazir of Islam, Hazrat Mawlana Munir Ahmad Sahib (may his shadow be extended), teacher of hadith and tafsir at Jamia Islamia Bab al-Ulum Kahror Pakka. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' is the final book of Usul al-Fiqh according to the syllabus of the Union of Islamic Seminaries, and it is the most intricate in terms of expression and the objectives of the book. Until now, many footnotes have been written on it, among which some are very lengthy, some very concise. Because of this, the honorable teachers faced a lot of time and difficulty in teaching Tawdih and Talwih. All praise is due to Allah, Lord of the worlds. Allah has blessed the eminent scholar, hadith teacher Hazrat Mawlana Abdur Rahman Jami Sahib with special divine grace. He has written an excellent, easy-to-understand, and extremely simple commentary on a considerable portion of Tawdih and Talwih, which is moderate and free from excessive length and excessive brevity. In it, due justice has been done to the refinement of expression, solving of expression, clarification of objectives, and resolution of purposes. It has also committed to answering the objections leveled by Allama Taftazani at various places against the text author. Dua that Allah grants this commentary complete acceptance with Allah and among the people, and makes its benefit universally perpetual forever. Only, and peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Munir Ahmad (forgiven), teacher of hadith and tafsir, Jamia Islamia Bab al-Ulum Kahror Pakka.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the commentary 'Misk al-Malih' on 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih', consisting of two short endorsements/recommendations. The first is by Muhammad Ashraf Shad, who commends the author Mawlana Abdur Rahman Jami for his teaching experience and accessible Urdu style. The second is by Munir Ahmad, who explains that previous commentaries on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih were either too long or too short, causing difficulty for teachers. The present commentary is praised for being moderate, clear, and for addressing the critiques of Allama Taftazani against the matn (Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Sharia). Both writers pray for its acceptance and benefit. This introduction sets the stage for a commentary designed to meet the needs of students in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
التوضيح والتلويح (Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih): A famous work in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh, consisting of Al-Tawdih (by Sadr al-Sharia) and its supercommentary Al-Talwih (by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani).
مسک الملیح (Misk al-Malih): The title of the Urdu commentary being introduced, meaning 'The Pleasant Musk'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What problem did previous commentaries on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih have according to Munir Ahmad?
A) They were all too short.
B) Some were too long and some too short, causing difficulty for teachers.
C) They were not in Urdu.
D) They did not address the objections of Taftazani.

Key Takeaway
A well-balanced commentary on a difficult usul text can greatly facilitate learning and teaching.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Role of Commentaries in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Introductions praise Urdu commentary on Tawdih wa Talwih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and significance of the Urdu commentary Misk al-Malih on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih within the Hanafi usul curriculum.

Core Idea
A balanced commentary bridges the gap between an intricate classical text and the student's comprehension.

The endorsements (taqriz) for Misk al-Malih reveal the challenges faced by teachers and students of Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih due to its difficulty and lack of accessible resources. This lesson examines how this commentary addresses those challenges and why it matters for the study of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original text and its components
Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is a composite work: Sadr al-Shari'ah wrote Al-Tanqih, then his own commentary Al-Tawdih, and then al-Taftazani wrote Al-Talwih. Recognize that this layered structure adds to the complexity.
The endorsements mention this three-book origin.
2
Analyze the need for a new commentary
Previous commentaries were either too long or too short. Teachers struggled to explain the text. Note that the endorsers emphasize the lack of a moderate, easy Urdu explanation.
The author aimed for balance between detail and brevity.
3
Examine the features of Misk al-Malih
It refines wording, solves expressions, clarifies objectives, and answers Taftazani's objections against Sadr al-Shari'ah. These features make it a comprehensive teaching aid.
Responding to objections is a key feature for advanced study.
4
Consider the impact on the curriculum
The commentary meets a long-standing academic need, making usul al-fiqh accessible to advanced students. Its acceptance in seminaries is predicted by the endorsers.
The endorsements come from teachers at various institutions.
5
Reflect on the broader significance
This example shows how classical Hanafi texts are kept alive through well-crafted commentaries, preserving the tradition while adapting to linguistic and pedagogical needs.
Urdu commentaries like this one are vital in the Indian subcontinent.

برادر محترم حضرت مولانا عبد الرحمن جامی صاحب زید مجدہم نے اصول فقہ کی ادق اور مشکل ترین کتاب التوضیح مع التلویح کی اردو میں مفصل اور آسان شرح لکھ کر اس کتاب کے سمجھنے اور سمجھانے کو سہل الحصول بنا دیا ہے؟ یہ شرح معلمین اور متعلمین کیلئے گراں قدر علمی خزانہ اور تحفہ ہے فاضل محترم زید مجدہم نے اس شرح کے ذریعہ دور حاضر کی ایک بہت بڑی علمی ضرورت کو پورا کر دیا ہے۔ فجزاہ اللہ تعالیٰ خیر الجزاء بنی وعن جميع المستفیدین۔ ورحم الله عبدا قال آمینا؟

مدرس جامعہ خیر المدارس ملتان
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is the last book of usul al-fiqh according to the curriculum of Islamic seminaries, most relevant in terms of its wording and objectives. Many commentaries have been written on it, some lengthy, some brief, causing teachers difficulty in teaching it. Praise be to Allah, the Lord of the worlds. Allah the Exalted granted special success to the great scholar, hadith master, Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami. He wrote a very excellent, easily understandable, and simple commentary on a substantial portion of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, which is moderate and free from length and undesirable brevity, fulfilling the rights of refining wording, solving expressions, clarifying purposes, and resolving objectives. He also undertook to answer the objections raised by al-Taftazani against the author in various places. I pray that Allah the Exalted grants this commentary complete acceptance with Him and among the people, and makes its benefit ever- enduring. Only peace be upon you. Munir Ahmad, teacher of hadith and tafsir, Jamia Islamia Bab al-Uloom, Kahror Pakka. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: Like other sciences and arts, usul al-fiqh was not compiled and arranged in the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Companions because Arabic was their mother tongue. When Islam spread beyond Arabia to non-Arabs and intermixing occurred, and non-Arabs began making mistakes in Arabic, then the sciences of grammar, literature, etc. were compiled. Among these sciences is the science of usul al-fiqh, in which principles and rules are explained for understanding fiqh. This science is extremely subtle. Scholars of every era have authored very useful books on it. Among these books is al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, which is actually a collection of three books: Allamah Sadr al-Shari'ah first wrote al-Tanqih, then its commentary al-Tawdih, then Allamah al-Taftazani wrote its commentary al-Talwih. This book has been part of the curriculum of Arabic seminaries for a long time. It is taught to advanced-level students and is considered extremely intricate. Due to the lack of an Urdu commentary, students faced great difficulty. My brother, Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami, has written its Urdu commentary and removed the students' confusion to a great extent. May Allah make this commentary beneficial for teachers and students and accept the effort of Mawlana. Amin. Muhammad Nawaz, servant of Jamia Hanafiyya Qadiriyya Sadiqabad, Multan. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: The respected brother, Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami (may Allah prolong his benefit) has written a detailed and easy Urdu commentary on the most intricate and difficult book of usul al-fiqh, al-Tawdih with al-Talwih, making it easy to understand and teach. This commentary is a valuable scholarly treasure and gift for teachers and students. The respected author (may Allah prolong his benefit) has fulfilled a great academic need of the present age through this commentary. May Allah reward him with the best reward for me and for all beneficiaries. May Allah have mercy on the one who says Amin. Written by the weak servant, Shabbir al-Haqq Kashmiri, forgive him O Allah, teacher at Jamia Khair al-Madaris, Multan.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage contains three endorsements (taqriz) for the Urdu commentary 'Misk al-Malih' on the classical Hanafi usul al-fiqh work 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. The first endorsement is by Mawlana Munir Ahmad, a teacher of hadith and tafsir. He describes the difficulty teachers faced due to the lack of a moderate commentary and praises Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami for producing a balanced commentary that addresses objections by al-Taftazani. The second endorsement is by Muhammad Nawaz, who provides a brief history of usul al-fiqh and explains that the book 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' is a collection of three books: Al-Tanqih by Sadr al-Shari'ah, Al-Tawdih as its commentary, and Al-Talwih by al-Taftazani. He notes the book's difficulty and the need for an Urdu commentary, which Mawlana Jami provided. The third endorsement is by Shabbir al-Haqq Kashmiri, who emphasizes the intricacy of the original text and praises the commentary for making it easy. Together, these endorsements highlight the commentary's significance in the Hanafi curriculum and its utility for students and teachers.

B) They were either too long or too brief
C) They did not include responses to objections
D) They omitted the historical background

Key Takeaway
The Misk al-Malih commentary exemplifies how a balanced, user-friendly commentary can revitalize the study of a foundational Hanafi usul text.

Introduction and Front Matter

Introduction and Historical Context of Usul al-Fiqh and al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
Prefatory note introducing the book and its importance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the historical reason for the development of usul al-fiqh and identify the authors of the three layers of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh was compiled after non-Arabs entered Islam and faced linguistic errors.

This prefatory note by Muhammad Nawaz sets the stage for Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami's Urdu commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It explains why usul al-fiqh was not needed in the earliest period and highlights the composite structure of the book. Understanding this historical context is crucial for appreciating the later scholarly efforts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
What is Muhammad Nawaz trying to accomplish in this note? Recognize it as an introduction praising the commentary and explaining the need for it.
2
Locate the historical reason for usul al-fiqh's compilation
Find the specific line that states why usul al-fiqh was not compiled earlier and what prompted its compilation.
Look for the mention of Arabic being the mother tongue and non-Arabs making errors.
3
Recognize the three-book structure
Identify the three component texts: al-Tanqih by Sadr al-Shari'ah, its commentary al-Tawdih, and the super-commentary al-Talwih by al-Taftazani.
Note that the composite work is called al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih.
4
Understand the value of the Urdu commentary
Why was this commentary needed? What problem does it solve according to the author?
The text states students faced difficulty due to the lack of an Urdu commentary.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم نحمده ونصلى على رسوله الكريم ) اما بعد: دوسرے علوم وفنون کی طرح اصول فقہ بھی حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور صحابہ کے دور میں مدون دمرتب نہیں تھا کیونکہ عربی زبان انکی " مادری زبان تھی جب اسلام عرب سے نکل کر عجم میں پہنچا اور عرب وعجم کا اختلاط ہوا اور عجم حضرات عربی میں غلطیوں کا ارتکاب کرنے لگے تو پھر علم صرف نخوادب وغیر ہ مدون کئے گئے انہیں علوم میں سے ایک علم اصول فقہ ہے جس میں فقہ کو سمجھنے کیلئے اصول وضوابط بیان کئے گئے ہیں یہ علم انتہائی مخدوم علم ہے ہر دور کے علماء نے اس میں بڑی مفید کتب تصنیف کیں انہیں کتب میں سے ایک کتاب توضیح تلویح ہے جو دراصل تین کتب کا مجموعہ ہے علامہ صدر الشریعت نے اول تنقیح لکھی پھر اس کی شرح توضیح لکھی پھر علامہ تفتازانی نے اسکی شرح تلویح لکھی یہ کتاب عرصہ دراز سے مدارس عربیہ کے نصاب میں داخل ہے اس وقت درجہ عالیہ کے طلبہ کو پڑھائی جاتی ہے اور انتہائی ادق . سمجھی جاتی ہے اردو شرح نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے طلبہ کو بہت مشکل پیش آتی تھی برادرم حضرت مولانا عبدالرحمن صاحب جامی نے اسکی اردو شرح لکھ کر کافی حد تک طلبہ کی الجھن دور کر دی ہے مولا با افہام وتقسیم کے اعتبار سے طلبہ میں مقبول ہیں اسکی جھلک شرح میں بھی نمایاں ہے۔ دعاء ہے اللہ تعالی اس شرح کو معلمین و معلین کیلئے نافع بنائے اور مولانا کی کاوش کو قبول فرمائے۔ آمین۔ فقط السلام محمد نواز خادم جامعہ حنفیہ قادریہ صادق آباد ملز۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: Like other sciences and arts, usul al-fiqh was not compiled in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Companions, because Arabic was their mother tongue. When Islam spread from Arabia to non-Arab lands and Arabs mixed with non-Arabs, and non-Arabs began to make errors in Arabic, then the sciences of grammar, syntax, and literature were compiled. Among these sciences is the science of usul al-fiqh, in which principles and rules are stated for understanding fiqh. This science is extremely beneficial; scholars of every era have authored many useful books on it. Among these books is al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, which is actually a compilation of three books: Allamah Sadr al-Shari'ah first wrote al-Tanqih, then its commentary al-Tawdih, then Allamah al-Taftazani wrote its commentary al-Talwih. This book has been included in the curriculum of Arabic madrasas for a long time; it is taught to advanced students and is considered extremely difficult. Due to the lack of an Urdu commentary, students faced great difficulty. My brother, Hazrat Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami, wrote an Urdu commentary, alleviating much of the students' confusion. He is popular among students for his eloquent explanations and divisions; this is evident from his commentary. I pray that Allah makes this commentary beneficial for teachers and students, and accepts Mawlana's effort. Amen. Only, peace, Muhammad Nawaz, servant of Jami'ah Hanafiyyah Qadiriyyah Sadiq Abad, Multan.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This is a prefatory note by Muhammad Nawaz, a teacher at Jami'ah Hanafiyyah Qadiriyyah, introducing the context of usul al-fiqh and praising Mawlana Abd al-Rahman Jami's Urdu commentary on the difficult book al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. He explains that usul al-fiqh was developed later due to non-Arabs' errors in Arabic, and highlights the importance of this commentary in making the subject accessible.

Key Terms
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): The science of principles for deriving legal rulings from Islamic sources.
توضیح تلویح (al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih): A composite work consisting of al-Tanqih by Sadr al-Shari'ah, its commentary al-Tawdih, and the super-commentary al-Talwih by al-Taftazani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say usul al-fiqh had to be compiled later?
A) Because the Prophet ordered its compilation
B) Because Arabs forgot the language
C) Because non-Arabs started making errors in Arabic after mixing with Arabs
D) Because it was not needed earlier

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh was a later science, compiled due to non-Arab Muslims' errors in Arabic, and al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is a composite work that remains central in Hanafi usul studies.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Interpreting Scholarly Endorsements in the Hanafi Tradition
Scholarly endorsements establishing author and work significance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract from a taqriz the author's scholarly authority, the difficulty of the source text, and the commentary's intended pedagogical role.

Core Idea
A taqriz is a scholarly testimony that situates a work within the tradition and attests to its necessity.

Scholarly endorsements (taqriz) are not mere formalities. In the Hanafi tradition, they serve as a chain of attestation, linking the author to the wider scholarly community. This lesson guides you through reading three endorsements for 'Misk al-Maleeh', extracting the key claims about the commentary's value and the author's credentials.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Book and Author
From the endorsements, determine the title of the commentary (Misk al-Maleeh), the original work (Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih), and the author (Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jami).
The author's name appears in the third endorsement.
2
Analyze the Endorsers' Credentials
Note the titles and positions of each endorser: Maulana Irshad Ahmad (Director, Dar al-Ulum), Maulana Mufti Muhammad Owais (Administrator), Maulana Daud Ahmad (Hadith teacher). Their positions establish their authority to evaluate scholarly works.
The endorsers are themselves respected scholars; their testimony carries weight.
3
Extract the Perceived Difficulty of the Source Text
All endorsements describe 'Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih' as extremely difficult, even intimidating. Identify the metaphors used: 'sharp stone', 'most difficult book', 'teachers avoid it'.
This difficulty creates the need for the commentary.
4
Identify the Commentary's Claimed Solution
The endorsements claim the commentary 'turns hard stone into wax', provides a 'comprehensive Urdu explanation', and makes the text accessible. Highlight these claims.
The commentary is presented as a pedagogical breakthrough.
5
Assess the Pedagogical Context
The endorsements mention the Dars Nizami curriculum, the lack of adequate Urdu commentaries, and the target audience (teachers and students). This contextualizes the work within the South Asian madrasa system.
Understanding the context helps evaluate the commentary's relevance.
