Misk al-Maleeh. 4185. Commentary on Al-Tawdih [wa al-Talwih]. 

Words of honor from the emperor of teaching, Hadrat Maulana Irshad Ahmad Sahib (may his shadow be prolonged), Director and Shaykh al-Hadith of Dar al-Ulum Eidgah Kabirwala. 
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: 
The abilities with which Allah, the Exalted, has endowed my dearest, beneficent, and nurturing teacher, the teacher of scholars, the scholar of scholars, the ascetic, the investigator of his time, the refuge of creation, the emperor of teaching, Hadrat Mufti Muhammad Siddiq Sahib (may his blessings be perpetual) in the fields of scholarship, research, and teaching are not hidden from anyone in the world. Who knew that this promising child nurtured in that lap of scholarship and research would, in the future, brighten his father's name and how much. Under the principle 'the child is the secret of his father,' this prince, upon entering the teaching field, left scholars and students astonished. With God-given intelligence, competence, and a gift for explanation, he gained immense popularity. In Dar al-Ulum Eidgah Kabirwala, he quenched the thirst of students thirsty for knowledge and research in the most difficult lessons such as Hidayah Thalith, Tawdih Talwih, Sharh Jami, etc. When he entered the field of authorship, the acceptance that his famous work 'Abar al-Yam' received in boys' and girls' madrasas can be gauged by the fact that it is talked about in every library in Pakistan. Another scholarly and research gift from this emperor of teaching is Misk al-Sahih. Several places in it are seen to be extremely eloquent, flowing prose, easy to understand, with solution of vocabulary, syntactic analysis, and 
: 
Along with resolving difficulties, this scholarly and research treasure contains beneficial points and is a royal gift for teachers. 'Tawdih Talwih' is that book in the Dars Nizami which teachers consider a sharp stone; even teachers with ten to fifteen years of experience do not dare to teach it, saying 'touching this stone is beyond us.' My brother (the author) has turned this hard stone into wax. God willing, now every intelligent, capable teacher will benefit from the fragrance of Misk al-Sahih and perfume the minds of the noble students. From the depths of the heart, I pray that Allah, the Exalted, by His grace, grants acceptance to this arduous effort. Grant this book a place of acceptance and benefit among scholars and students. (Amin, then Amin, O Lord of the worlds). 
Written by Irshad Ahmad, pardoned, resident of Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, 8 Jumada al-Ula 1425 AH. 

Misk al-Maleeh.

And Al-Talwih. Commentary on [the text]. 

Words of honor from the master of students, Hadrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Owais Sahib (may his glory be increased), Administrator of Dar al-Ulum Jaleel Town Gujranwala. 
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. All praise is due to Allah and sufficient, and peace be upon His chosen servants. To proceed: The people of knowledge know well that Tawdih Talwih is the most difficult book of the higher level. Not to mention the students, even most junior teachers shy away from teaching it with understanding. Moreover, there is no comprehensive Urdu commentary available to explain it. The respected teacher, Hadrat Nu'mani Sahib (may Allah have mercy on him), his Urdu commentary 'al-Ta'liq al-Fasih' was extremely concise, like his teaching style, and was like confining something in a bottle. Students with lesser ability could not benefit from it. Therefore, there was an urgent need for a comprehensive Urdu commentary to explain this book. My brother Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jami (may his glory be increased), a distinguished teacher from the center of knowledge Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala, has taught the most subtle lessons like Abu Dawud, Hidayah Thalith, Tawdih, Sharh Jami. Currently he is Shaykh al-Hadith at Dar al-Ulum Rahmiyya Multan, and he is my classmate and companion in the completion class. Allah has bestowed upon him excellent teaching ability. He has written an excellent Urdu commentary on Tawdih Talwih, creating ease for students. God willing, this commentary will prove beneficial for students and make them independent of all other commentaries. I pray that the Exalted and Majestic Lord accepts this commentary in His lofty court and makes it beneficial for students. Amin. 
The humble Abu Idris Muhammad Owais, forgiven, 
Servant of Jamia Yakeya Aimanabad, Gujranwala. 

Words of honor from the pride of teachers, Hadrat Maulana Daud Ahmad Sahib (may his glory be increased), Hadith teacher at Jamia Mazahir al-Ulum Gujranwala. 
The respected teacher, Hadrat Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jami (may their shadows be prolonged) is a pride-worthy teacher of Dars Nizami. He possesses an unparalleled gift of teaching and explanation. During my teaching of Talwih, I benefited from his lecture on Tawdih and Talwih. Masha Allah, it is a very useful thing for explaining the book. It is the graciousness of Hadrat that he asked me to write an endorsement; otherwise, this work of Hadrat is independent of words of praise and description. May Allah make this scholarly gift of the teacher most beneficial for all those connected to teaching and learning, and grant him success for more such scholarly services. Amin, O Lord of the worlds. 
The humblest of creatures, Daud Ahmad, Jamia Mazahir al-Ulum Gujranwala, currently residing at Jamia Yakeya Aimanabad, District Gujranwala.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is front matter for the book 'Misk al-Maleeh', consisting of two scholarly endorsements (taqriz) and an introduction. The first endorsement is by Maulana Irshad Ahmad, who praises the author Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jami as a gifted teacher and scholar. He vividly describes the difficulty of the classical text 'Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih' in the Dars Nizami curriculum, comparing it to a sharp stone that even experienced teachers avoid. He claims that the author's commentary has turned this hard stone into wax, making it accessible. The second endorsement is by Maulana Mufti Muhammad Owais, who emphasizes the urgent need for a comprehensive Urdu commentary on this difficult work, noting that existing commentaries were too concise for average students. He confirms that the author has fulfilled this need. The third endorsement by Maulana Daud Ahmad further commends the author's teaching abilities and the utility of the commentary. Together, these texts establish the scholarly credentials of the author and the significance of his work in the Hanafi usul al-fiqh tradition, particularly in the South Asian madrasa system. They provide context for why this commentary was written and its intended audience: teachers and students struggling with the original Arabic text.

Key Terms
تقریظ (taqriz): A scholarly endorsement or foreword written by a respected figure to commend a book and its author.
توضیح تلویح (Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih): A classical text on usul al-fiqh, authored by Sadr al-Shari'ah, known for its depth and difficulty in the Dars Nizami curriculum.
درس نظامی (Dars Nizami): The traditional curriculum of South Asian madrasas, developed by Mulla Nizam al-Din Sahlawi, including texts like Al-Hidayah, Al-Tawdih, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary function of a taqriz as seen in this passage?
A) To summarize the book's content
B) To attest to the author's scholarly credentials and the work's necessity
C) To provide a legal ruling on the book's permissibility
D) To critique the author's methodology

Key Takeaway
Scholarly endorsements (taqriz) are testimonies that establish an author's authority and the pedagogical significance of a commentary within the Hanafi tradition.

Understanding the Role of Urdu Commentaries in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh: The Example of Misk al-Maleeh
Introductory endorsements (taqariz) for an Urdu commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of an Urdu commentary on a classical usul text and explain how scholarly endorsements establish a work's credibility.

Core Idea
A comprehensive Urdu commentary transforms a difficult classical text into an accessible tool for students.

This passage presents the endorsements (taqariz) for Misk al-Maleeh, a recent Urdu commentary on the Hanafi usul al-fiqh classic al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The endorsers, all respected scholars, highlight the challenges students face with the original text and praise the author, Maulana Abdul Rahman Jami, for his clarity and pedagogical skill. Understanding the function of such commentaries is crucial for appreciating how the Hanafi tradition remains accessible across generations and languages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of Misk al-Maleeh
From the endorsements, determine what the book aims to do. Is it a new legal work, a summary, or a commentary? Note the specific references to al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih.
All three endorsers agree it is a sharh (commentary) designed to simplify the difficult text.
2
Assess the credentials of the endorsers
Look at the academic titles and positions of the endorsers (e.g., rector, Shaykh al-Hadith, teacher). Consider why their endorsement adds credibility.
Endorsers include Mufti Muhammad Owais (rector), Maulana Dawood Ahmad (hadith teacher), and Maulana Allah Bakhsh Zafar (teacher).
3
Understand the problem the commentary solves
The endorsements mention the difficulty of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih and the inadequacy of previous commentaries like al-Ta'liq al-Faseeh. Identify the specific shortcomings noted.
Al-Ta'liq al-Faseeh was extremely brief, like 'confining the ocean in a jug', leaving low-capacity students unable to benefit.
4
Recognize the role of Urdu in transmitting Hanafi usul
The endorsements highlight the use of Urdu to make complex Arabic texts accessible. Consider the broader context of Urdu commentaries in the Hanafi tradition.
Urdu serves as a bridge language, preserving the content while lowering the barrier to entry.
5
Evaluate the claims of the endorsements
One endorser claims the commentary will 'dispense with all other commentaries'. Assess whether this is hyperbole or a realistic expectation based on the text.
Consider that the endorser is praising the work, but the claim may be rhetorical.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله وكفى وسلام علی عبادہ الذین اصطفیٰ اما بعد: اہل علم بخوبی جانتے ہیں کہ توضیح تلویح درجہ عالیہ کی مشکل ترین کتاب ہے طلبہ کرام تو اپنی جگہ اکثر ابتدائی اساتذہ بھی اسکو پھر سمجھتے ہوئے پڑھانے سے کتراتے ہیں نیز اسکو حل کرنے کیلئے کوئی جامع اردو شرح موجود نہیں ہے استاذ المکرم حضرت نعمانی صاحب رحمۃ اللہ تعالیٰ کی اردو شرح التعلیق الفسیح آپ کے تدریسی انداز کی طرح انتہائی مختصر تھی اور یا کو کوزے میں بند کر دینے کا مصداق تھی۔ جس سے ادنی استعداد والے طلبہ استفادہ نہیں کر سکتے تھے اس لئے اس کتاب کو حل کرنے کیلئے ایک جامع اردو شرح کی شدید ضرورت تھی۔ برادرم مولانا عبد الرحمن جامی زید مجدۀ مرکز علم دار العلوم کبیر والا کے مایہ ناز استا ذرہ چکے ہیں ابو داؤد ہدایہ ثالث توضیح شرح جامی جیسے ادق اسباق پڑھاتے رہے ہیں اس وقت دار العلوم رحمیہ ملتان کے شیخ الحدیث ہیں اور درجہ تکمیل کے میرے ہم سبق و ساتھی نہیں اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان کو بہترین تدریسی صلاحیت سے نوازا ہے آپ نے توضیح تلویح کی بہترین اردو شرح لکھ کر طلبہ کیلئے سہولت پیدا کر دی ہے انشاء اللہ یہ شرح طلبہ کیلئے مفید ثابت ہو کر تمام شروحات سے مستغنی کر دیگی۔ دعا ہے کہ حق جل وعلی اس شرح کو اپنی درگاہ عالیہ میں قبول فرما کر طلبہ کیلئے نافع بنائے آمین۔
احقر ابو ادریس محمد اویس غفرلہ
خادم جامعه یکیه ایمن آباد مور گوجرانولہ
رائے گرامی فخر المدرسین حضرت مولانا داؤ د احمد صاحب زید مجدہ استاذ الحدیث جامعہ مظاہر العلوم گوجرانوالہ
استاد محترم حضرت مولانا عبد الرحمن جامی مدظلہم العالی درس نظامی کے قابل فخر مدرس ہیں افہام و تفہیم کا بے مثال ملکہ رکھتے ہیں ۔ حضرت والا کی توضیح و تلویح کی درسی تقریر سے بندہ نے تکویح کی تدریس کے دوران استفادہ کیا تھا ما شاء اللہ حل کتاب کیلئے بڑی کام کی چیز ہے حضرت والا کی ذرہ نوازی ہے کہ بندہ سے تقریظ کے لئے فرمایا وگرنہ حضرت والا کی یہ تصنیف تعریف و توصیف کے رسی کلمات سے بے نیاز ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ حضرت الاستاد کی اس علمی سوغات کو تعلیم و تعلیم سے تعلق رکھنے والے تمام حضرات کیلئے مفید سے مفید تر فرمائے اور اس قسم کی مزید علمی خدمات کیلئے موفق فرمائے۔ آمین یا رب العالمین۔
احقر الا نام داؤ داحمد جامعہ مظاہر العلوم گوجرانوالہ
حال نزیل جامعه یکیہ ایمن آباد، ضلع گوجرانوالا

بسم ا
اما بعد ترقی کے اس دور میں جس طرح عصری علوم کو فروغ دینے کیلئے جدید آلات ( کمپیوٹر وغیرہ) کا استعمال مستحسن قرار دیا گیا ہے بلکہ وقت کی ایک ضرورت سمجھ لیا گیا ہے اسی طرح عربی دینی و اسلامی کتب میں وداعیت رکھے ہوئے اسلامی علوم کے اسرار ورموز کو سمجھنے کی خاطر ان کی اردو شروحات کی ضرورت بھی محسوس ہو رہی ہے تاکہ عربی کتب کی مغلق اور مشکل ترین عبارت کو آسان الفاظ اور مانوس زبان کے ذریعے حل کیا جا سکے۔ اس سلسلہ میں تو ضیح اور اسکی شرح تلویح اصول فقہ میں اعلیٰ معیار کی کتب ہیں اور اسلامی مدارس میں داخل نصاب ہیں۔ لیکن مغلق ہونے کے باعث طلباء کرام کیلئے سمجھنا باعث دشوار اور کٹھن مرحلہ تھا برادر کبیر حضرت مولانا عبد الرحمن صاحب جاتی ، ظلہم شیخ الحدیث جامعہ رحیمیہ ملتان نے اسکی اردو شرح لکھ کر طلباء کرام پر بہت بڑا احسان کیا ہے کتاب مذکور کے بعض مقامات دیکھنے سے محسوس ہوا کہ جس قدر یہ شرح طلباء کیلئے مفید ہے اس قدر اساتذہ کرام کیلئے بھی علمی معلومات بڑھانے کا بہترین ذریعہ ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ موصوف کی اس کاوش کو بار آور فرمائے اور قبولیت سے سرفراز فرماتے ہوئے آخروی نجات کیلئے ذریعہ بنائے آمین۔ العبد الضعيف افقر الی اللہ ابوسعید اللہ بخش ظفر عفی عنہ

۵۱۴۲۵/۱۰/۱۱
Misk al-Maleeh... and al-Talwih, commentary on al-Fiqh [besturdubooks.war] Endorsement of the respected teacher, Mufti Muhammad Owais Sahib, may his benefit increase, rector of Dar al-Ulum Jaleel Town, Gujranwala. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, and peace be upon His chosen servants. To proceed: The people of knowledge know well that al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih is among the most difficult books. Students, and even many beginners among teachers, are reluctant to teach it after understanding it. And no comprehensive Urdu commentary exists for it. The Urdu commentary of the respected teacher Naumani, may Allah have mercy on him, al-Ta'liq al-Faseeh, was extremely brief like his teaching style, and was like confining the ocean in a jug. Hence students of low capacity could not benefit. Therefore, there was a dire need for a comprehensive Urdu commentary to solve this book. My brother Maulana Abdul Rahman Jami, may his benefit increase, is a distinguished teacher from Dar al-Ulum Kabirwala. He has taught intricate subjects like Abu Dawood, Hidayah, Thalith, Tawdih, and Sharh Jami. Currently he is the Shaykh al-Hadith of Dar al-Ulum Rahmiyya Multan. He is not my classmate in the completion class, but Allah has bestowed him with excellent teaching ability. He has written an excellent Urdu commentary of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, making it easy for students. In sha Allah, this commentary will prove beneficial for students and dispense with all other commentaries. I pray that Allah the Exalted accepts this commentary in His lofty court and makes it beneficial for students. Ameen.
The humble Abu Idris Muhammad Owais, forgiven, servant of Jami'a Yakiya Aimanabad, near Gujranwala.
Endorsement of the pride of teachers, Maulana Dawood Ahmad Sahib, may his benefit increase, teacher of Hadith at Jami'a Mazahir al-Ulum Gujranwala. Respected teacher Maulana Abdul Rahman Jami, may his shadow be lofty, is a proud teacher of the Dars Nizami curriculum. He has an unparalleled talent for explanation and comprehension. I benefited from his class lecture on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih during my teaching of al-Talwih. Masha Allah, it is a very useful thing for solving the book. It is his graciousness that he asked me for this endorsement; otherwise, his work is needless of words of praise. May Allah make this academic gift of the respected teacher most beneficial for all those involved in teaching and learning, and grant him success for more such academic services. Ameen, O Lord of the worlds. The most humble, Dawood Ahmad, Jami'a Mazahir al-Ulum Gujranwala, currently residing in Jami'a Yakiya Aimanabad, district Gujranwala.

Misk al-Maleeh, commentary on al-Tawdih [besturdubooks.wa] Endorsement of the pillar of teachers, Maulana Allah Bakhsh Zafar, may his shadow be lofty, teacher at Jami'a Khair al-Madaris Multan. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, and blessings upon His family. To proceed: In this age of progress, just as the use of modern tools (computers, etc.) for promoting worldly sciences has been deemed commendable and considered a necessity of the time, similarly, for understanding the secrets and mysteries of Islamic sciences contained in Arabic religious and Islamic books, the need for their Urdu commentaries is being felt, so that the complex and difficult expressions of Arabic books can be solved through simple words and familiar language. In this regard, al-Tawdih and its commentary al-Talwih are high-quality books in Usul al-Fiqh and are part of the curriculum in Islamic seminaries. But due to their complexity, understanding them was a difficult and arduous stage for students. My elder brother, Maulana Abdul Rahman Sahib Jami, may his shadow be lofty, Shaykh al-Hadith of Jami'a Rahimiya Multan, has done a great favor to the students by writing an Urdu commentary of it. After seeing some parts of the mentioned book, I felt that as much as this commentary is beneficial for students, it is also an excellent means of increasing academic knowledge for teachers. May Allah make this endeavor of the mentioned person fruitful and honor it with acceptance, and make it a means of salvation in the hereafter. Ameen. The weak servant, most needy of Allah, Abu Saeed Allah Bakhsh Zafar, pardoned, Jami'a Khair al-Madaris Multan. 11/10/1425 AH.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage comprises the front matter of Misk al-Maleeh, an Urdu commentary on the classical Hanafi usul al-fiqh text al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. It contains three endorsements (taqariz) from prominent scholars: Mufti Muhammad Owais, Maulana Dawood Ahmad, and Maulana Allah Bakhsh Zafar. Each scholar praises the author, Maulana Abdul Rahman Jami, for his teaching ability and for producing a much-needed Urdu commentary that simplifies the difficult text. They note that previous commentaries were too brief or lacked comprehensiveness. The endorsements highlight the importance of making advanced usul works accessible to students through clear Urdu explanations. The passage also includes the author's own opening remarks, explaining the need for such a commentary. There is no legal ruling or usul analysis here; it is purely introductory and biographical.

Key Terms
تقریظ (taqriz): A scholarly endorsement or review written by a respected academic to attest to the quality and usefulness of a new work.
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the book Misk al-Maleeh according to the endorsements?
A) To present a new legal ruling in Hanafi fiqh
B) To provide a comprehensive Urdu commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
C) To critique the Shafi'i school of jurisprudence
D) To compile the fatwas of later Hanafi scholars

Key Takeaway
Scholarly endorsements and accessible commentaries are vital for transmitting Hanafi usul al-fiqh to new generations, ensuring that even the most difficult texts can be studied by students of varying abilities.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Importance of Usul al-Fiqh and the Role of Tawdih and Talwih
Prefatory remarks on usul al-fiqh and the Tawdih/Talwih works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why usul al-fiqh is considered the key to deriving rulings and describe the composition and significance of Tawdih and Talwih in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the master key to Islamic law; Tawdih and Talwih are its most profound yet challenging Hanafi expositions.

This preface opens the door to the world of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, explaining why this science is indispensable and why the works of Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Taftazani are both revered and feared by students. The author, a seasoned teacher, shares his motivation for writing a commentary, revealing the timeless struggle to make complex legal theory accessible. This lesson will orient you to the foundational role of usul and the specific texts you are about to study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author's Purpose
Read the first part of the preface to understand why the author wrote this Urdu commentary. He notes the need for accessible explanations of difficult Arabic texts in modern times.
The author explicitly states that Urdu commentaries help unlock the 'secrets' of Islamic sciences.
2
Recognize the Importance of Usul al-Fiqh
The preface describes usul al-fiqh as the science containing principles and rules that lead to fiqh rulings. Understand that it is considered 'key and fundamental' after the Quran and Sunnah.
This science is taught every year in seminaries, reflecting its centrality.
3
Trace the Compilation History
The preface reports two opinions on the first compiler of usul al-fiqh: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i. Note that this shows the early origins of the discipline.
This debate itself is a matter of ikhtilaf; the Hanafi school often credits Imam Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the Composition of Tawdih and Talwih
The preface reveals that 'Tawdih Talwih' is actually a collection of four books: Usul al-Bazdawi, Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih. Identify each component and its author.
Sadr al-Shari'ah wrote Tawdih as a commentary on Tanqih, and Taftazani wrote Talwih as a super-commentary on Tawdih.
5
Appreciate the Pedagogical Challenge
The preface highlights that Tawdih contains rare and difficult topics, and Talwih adds complexity and critique. Understand why this book is considered one of the most difficult in Dars-e-Nizami.
The author mentions he needed 'a strong heart and courage' to teach it.

عزیز طلبہ کرام ! قرآن وسنت کے بعد جن علوم شرعیہ فرعیہ کو کلیدی و بنیادی اہمیت حاصل ہے ان میں اصول فقہ سرفہرست ہے کیونکہ یہی وہ علم ہے جس میں وہ اصول و قواعد بیان کئے گئے جن سے آشنا ہو کر انسان فقہ کے احکام تک رسائی حاصل کرتا ہے جیسا کہ اس علم کی تعریف سے ظاہر ہے۔ اور فقہ کو اسلامی و معاشرتی زندگی میں جو اہمیت حاصل ہے وہ کسی سے پوشیدہ نہیں ہے. اس لئے یہ علوم انتہائی مخدوم علوم میں حضرات ائمہ مجتہدین متبوعین رحمہم اللہ کے دور میں ہی ان کی تدوین و تہذیب شروع ہو گئی۔ ایک قول کے مطابق اصول فقہ کے مدون اول حضرت امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ اور ایک قول کے مطابق حضرت امام شافعی ہیں۔ ہر دور کے علماء کرام نے اس علم کو اپنی خصوصی توجہ کا موز بنایا اور اس میں تصنیفات کیں اس علم کی اہمیت کا اندازہ اس بات سے لگایا جا سکتا ہے کہ درجہ ثالثہ سے لے کر موقوف علیہ تک ہر سال کے طلبہ کو اصول فقہ کی کوئی کتاب سبقاً پڑھائی جاتی ہے ان کتب میں سے اہم ترین اور مشکل ترین کتاب درجہ عالیہ کو پڑھائی جانی والی اصول فقہ کی آخری کتاب" توضیح تلویح ہے جو کہ درحقیقت چار کتابوں کا مجموعہ ہے (۱) اصول بزدوی (۲) تنقیح (۳) توضيح (۴) تلویح بلاشک وشبہ علامہ صدر الشریعہ کی توضیح انتہائی قیمتی اور نادر مشکل ترین مباحث پر مشتمل ہے جو دوسری کتب میں نایاب یا وشبہ کمیاب ہیں جس کا اظہار علامہ صدر " و هذا مما تفردت بہ کیساتھ جابجا فرماتے رہتے ہیں۔
پھر نابغہ روزگار شخصیت محقق و مدقق علامہ تفتازانی جو علوم نقلیہ و عقلیہ کے آفتاب عالمتاب ہیں کی تدقیقات غامضہ پر مشتمل شرح تلویح نے کتاب کو مزید پیچیدہ بنادیا اور جابج علامہ تفتازانی کے اعتراضات نے شرح کو جرح میں بدل دیا۔ اس لئے علماء و معلمین کے ہاں تو ضیح تلویح درس نظامی کے ان مشکل ترین اسباق سے شمار ہوتی ہے جس کی تدریس کے لئے مضبوط دل گردہ چاہئیے ۔ اللہ کے فضل وکرم اور حضرات اساتذہ کرام کی شفقتوں اور دعاؤں سے اپنے مادر علمی مرکز علوم دار العلوم عیدگاہ اسا کبیر والا میں بندہ عاجز کو کتاب مذکور آٹھ دس مرتبہ پڑھانے کی توفیق میسر ہوئی اور تاہنوز دار العلوم رحیمیہ ملتان میں بھی چار سال سے بندہ کے زیر تدریس ہے دوران تدریس بندہ کو اس وقت کے توضیح پڑھانے والے چند جید اور مشہور اساتذہ کرام میری مراد ولی کامل حضرت مولانا علی محمد (۲) محقق عصر حضرت مولانا محمد موسی خان صاحب رحمۃ اللہ شیخ الحدیث جامعہ
Misk al-Malih. Opinion of the noble teacher, the dean of teachers, Hadrat Maulana Allah Bakhsh Zafar Sahib (may his shadow be prolonged), teacher of Jamia Khair al-Madaris Multan. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, and blessings upon His family. To proceed: In this age of progress, just as the use of modern tools (computers, etc.) to promote contemporary sciences has been deemed commendable, indeed considered a necessity of the time, similarly, for understanding the secrets and mysteries of Islamic sciences contained in Arabic religious and Islamic books, the need for their Urdu commentaries is felt, so that the obscure and most difficult expressions of Arabic books may be solved through easy words and familiar language. In this regard, Tawdih and its commentary Talwih are high-quality books in usul al-fiqh and are included in the curriculum of Islamic seminaries. But due to their obscurity, understanding them was difficult and arduous for students. The elder brother, Hadrat Maulana Abd al-Rahman Sahib Jati, (may his shadow be lengthened?), teacher of Hadith at Jamia Rahimia Multan, has done a great favor to the students by writing its Urdu commentary. From examining certain passages of the mentioned book, it was felt that as much as this commentary is beneficial for students, it is also an excellent means of increasing academic knowledge for teachers. May Allah the Almighty make this effort of his fruitful and grant it acceptance, making it a means of salvation in the hereafter. Amen. The weak servant, the most needy of Allah, Abu Sa'id Allah Bakhsh Zafar, pardoned by Him. Jamia Khair al-Madaris Multan. 11/10/1425 AH.

Misk al-Malih. Preface. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, and blessings upon His family ... to proceed! Dear students! Among the subsidiary religious sciences after the Quran and Sunnah, that which holds key and fundamental importance is usul al-fiqh, because it is this science in which those principles and rules are set forth, by becoming acquainted with which a person gains access to the rulings of fiqh, as is evident from the definition of this science. And the importance that fiqh holds in Islamic and social life is not hidden from anyone. Therefore, these sciences began to be compiled and refined in the era of the great imams and authoritative mujtahids (may Allah have mercy on them). According to one opinion, the first compiler of usul al-fiqh is Hadrat Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa, and according to another opinion, Hadrat Imam Shafi'i. Scholars of every era have made this science the object of their special attention and authored works in it. The importance of this science can be gauged from the fact that from the third level to the final level, students every year study some book of usul al-fiqh as a lesson. Among these books, the most important and most difficult book taught at the highest level is the final book of usul al-fiqh, 'Tawdih Talwih', which is actually a collection of four books: (1) Usul al-Bazdawi, (2) Tanqih, (3) Tawdih, (4) Talwih. Without doubt, the Tawdih of 'Allama Sadr al-Shari'ah is extremely valuable and contains rare and most difficult discussions that are scarce in other books. 'Allama Sadr expresses this by repeatedly saying, 'And this is something I have uniquely done.' Then the penetrating investigations of the genius of the age, the researcher and verifier 'Allama Taftazani, who is the radiant sun of transmitted and rational sciences, embodied in the commentary Talwih made the book even more complex, and the objections of 'Allama Taftazani changed the commentary into criticism. Therefore, among scholars and teachers, Tawdih Talwih is counted among the most difficult lessons of the Dars-e-Nizami, for the teaching of which a strong heart and courage are needed. By the grace and favor of Allah and the kindness and prayers of respected teachers, this humble servant was granted the opportunity to teach the said book eight or ten times in his alma mater, Markaz al-Ulum Dar al-Ulum Idgah Asa Kabir Wala, and still at Dar al-Ulum Rahimia Multan, it is under his teaching for four years. During teaching, the humble servant's...
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the preface (پیش لفظ) of the book 'Misk al-Malih', a Urdu commentary on the classical works Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, Abu Sa'id Allah Bakhsh Zafar, begins by praising Allah and invoking blessings, then explains the motivation for writing this commentary. He notes that in modern times, just as tools like computers are used to advance secular sciences, there is a similar need for Urdu commentaries to make the difficult Arabic texts of Islamic sciences accessible. In particular, Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah and its super-commentary Al-Talwih by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani are foundational texts in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, taught in Islamic seminaries. However, these texts are extremely challenging due to their condensed style and deep theoretical discussions. The author praises the earlier Urdu commentary by Maulana Abd al-Rahman Jati but still finds areas that require further clarification. He then provides a brief history of usul al-fiqh, noting that Imam Abu Hanifa is considered by some to be the first to compile this science, while others attribute it to Imam al-Shafi'i. He emphasizes the importance of usul al-fiqh as the key to deriving rulings from the Quran and Sunnah. The author then focuses on the books Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih, describing them as a collection of four works: Usul al-Bazdawi, Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih. He highlights the unique and difficult topics in Tawdih, and how Taftazani's commentary added complexity, sometimes even turning commentary into critique (jarh). Therefore, teaching these texts requires great expertise. The author states that he has taught this book multiple times and continues to do so, emphasizing his qualifications to write this commentary. This preface sets the stage for the detailed explanations that follow in the lesson.

Key Terms
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): The principles and rules by which rulings of fiqh are derived from their detailed evidence; a foundational Islamic science.
توضیح (Tawdih): A well-known work on usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Thani, considered a concise yet comprehensive text in the Hanafi school.
تلویح (Talwih): A super-commentary by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on the Tawdih, known for its critical analysis and depth.
امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ (Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa): The founder of the Hanafi school, known for his use of reason and opinion in jurisprudence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, what is the primary reason for writing an Urdu commentary on Tawdih and Talwih?
A) To simplify the text for students who find it difficult due to its obscurity and complexity
B) To criticize the original authors for their errors
C) To add new rulings that were not present before
D) To replace the original Arabic texts entirely

Key Takeaway
The preface frames usul al-fiqh as the essential key to fiqh, and positions Tawdih and Talwih as the most challenging yet rewarding Hanafi textbooks, whose study requires dedicated effort and accessible commentaries.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Structure and Purpose of 'Misk al-Maleeh'
Author's preface explaining his Urdu commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four component books of Tawdih wa Talwih and explain the author's pedagogical approach in his Urdu commentary.

Core Idea
Tawdih wa Talwih is a challenging composite of four books; this commentary simplifies it for students.

The preface to a scholarly work often sets the stage for what follows. In this preface, the author introduces his Urdu commentary on the famous Hanafi usul text 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. He explains why this text is important, what makes it difficult, and how his own commentary aims to make it accessible. Understanding this preface will help you appreciate the purpose and methodology of the commentary before diving into its content.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main subject of the preface
Read the opening lines of the preface. The author directly addresses students and highlights the importance of Usul al-Fiqh. Note that he places this science after the Quran and Sunnah in importance.
The preface is addressed to students of the Dars-e-Nizami curriculum.
2
Recognize the composition of Tawdih wa Talwih
The author states that Tawdih wa Talwih is actually a collection of four books: Usul al-Bazdawi, Tanqih, Tawdih, and Talwih. Commit these names to memory.
This is a common point of confusion; many think it is a single work.
3
Understand the challenge of Tawdih wa Talwih
The author mentions that Tawdih by Sadr al-Sharia contains unique difficult discussions, and Taftazani's Talwih adds complexity and criticism. This makes teaching and learning the text challenging.
Taftazani's objections are noted as 'nahaq (unjust)' by the author.
4
List the features of the author's commentary
The author lists five features of his commentary: vocabulary explanation, literal translation, segmentation of Talwih, responses to Taftazani's objections, and focus on clarifying the original text.
These features aim to reduce student boredom and provide clarity.
5
Appreciate the author's motivation and acknowledgments
The author shares his personal teaching experience and acknowledges his teachers and supporters. This shows the commentary is based on practical teaching needs.
The title 'Misk al-Maleeh' was suggested by his father.

مسک الملیح
والتلويح

اشرفیه (۳) ولی کامل حضرت اقدس مفتی عبد القادر صاحب شیخ الحدیث دار العلوم کبیر والا کی تقاریر دستیاب ہو گئیں جن سے حل توضیح تلویح میں کافی سہولت ہو گئی۔ بندہ نے انکو اور حواشی کو سامنے رکھ کر ایک کاپی مرتب کر لی جو بعد میں طلبہ کرام اور دوست احباب فوٹوسٹیٹ کرا کر اس سے استفادہ کرتے رہے ہیں تو بندہ کے دل میں داعیہ پیدا ہوا کہ تفسیر عبر الیم اور التحفتہ العلمیہ کی طرح اگر اس کو بھی کتابی شکل دے کر شائع کر دیا جائے تو ان شاء اللہ عزیز طلبہ کے لئے نافع ثابت ہوگی ۔ ایک سال کی تنگ ودو کے بعد الحمد للہ ثم احمد اللہ اب یہ منزل قریب اور آسان ہو گئی ہے۔ خصوصیات ! خطبات ثلاثہ میں حل لغات وصل تراکیب کا التزام کیا گیا ہے (۲) خطبات ثلاثہ میں عبارت کے لفظی ترجمہ کا اہتمام کیا گیا ہے۔ (۳) شرح تلویح کی عبارت کی تقطیع کر کے ہر حصہ کی غرض شارح کی وضاحت کر دی گئی ہے۔ (۴) شارح تفتازائی نے علامہ صدر الشریعہ پر جو ناحق اعتراضات کئے ہیں۔ شروحات اور حواشی کی روشنی میں تبصرہ کے عنوان سے ان کے جوابات عرض کئے گئے ہیں (۵) نفس عبارت کو حل: کرنے کی کوشش کی گئی زیادہ قیل و قال اور خارجی مباحث سے حتی الوسع اجتناب کیا گیا ہے تا کہ طلبہ المہن محسوس نہ کریں۔
خوشی کے ان لمحات کے موقع پر میں ایک بار پھر اپنے انتہائی مشفق و مربی والد گرامی حضرت اقدس مفتی محمد صدیق صاحب ادام اللہ ظلہم علینا کا شکر گزار ہوں جنہوں نے اپنی مصروفیات و پیرانہ سالی کے باوجو داس شرح کے مسودہ کو بالا ستعاب ملاحظہ فرمایا اور اپنے قیتی مشوروں سے نوازا اور کتاب کا نام مک الی خو تجویز فرمایا فجزاهم الله احسن الجزاء ثانیاً اپنے ان عظیم مشفقین اساتذہ کرام اور اکابرین علماء عظام دامت بر کاتہم العالیہ کا بے حد ممنون ہوں جنہوں نے اپنی گوناگوں مصروفیات کے باوجود اپنی قیمتی آراء تحریر فرما کر بندہ کی حوصلہ افزائی فرمائی۔
خصوصاً انتہائی شفیق و پر وقار شخصیت گرامی قدر حضرت قاری محمد ادریس صاحب زید مجدہم (مدیر جامعہ دار العلوم رحیمیہ ملتان کا انتہائی شکر گزار ہوں جنہوں نے افتتاحی کلمات مبار کہ تحریر فرما کر ذرہ نوازی فرمائی فجزاهم الله كلهـم احسن الجزاء - ثالثاً ان مخلص بھائیوں کا شکریہ ادا کرتا ہوں جنہوں نے اپنی دعاؤں سے اور قیمتی مشوروں سے نوازا خصوصاً برادر مکرم گرامی قدر حضرت الشیخ مولانا ارشاد احمد صاحب زید مجدہم مدیر جامعہ دار العلوم کبیر والا اور صاحبزادہ مکرم حضرت مولانا سراج الحق صاحب زید مجدہ استاذ الحدیث دار العلوم کبیر والا اور عزیز مکرم حضرت مولانا مفتی محمد ناصر صاحب رئیس الافتاء دار العلوم رحیمیہ ملتان زید مجدہم رابعاً ان عزیز ان کا شکر گزار ہوں جنہوں نے اس مسودہ کی تسوید و بیض تقطیع و تہذیب کتابت کمپوزنگ میں تعاون فرمایا خصوصاً عزیز القدر مولانا محمد مرسلین سلمہ کا انتہائی شکر گزار ہوں جن کی تحریک
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise belongs to its people and blessings upon its people... To proceed! Dear students! Among the subsidiary Sharia sciences after the Quran and Sunnah, the one with key and fundamental importance is Usul al-Fiqh, because it is the science in which the principles and rules are explained, by becoming familiar with which a person gains access to the rulings of fiqh, as is evident from the definition of this science. And the importance that fiqh holds in Islamic and social life is not hidden from anyone. Therefore, these sciences are among the most served sciences; their compilation and refinement began in the era of the imams, the mujtahidun, the followed ones (may Allah have mercy on them). According to one statement, the first compiler of Usul al-Fiqh was Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to another statement, it was Imam al-Shafi'i. Scholars of every era have given special attention to this science and authored works in it. The importance of this science can be gauged from the fact that from the third grade to the highest level, every year students are taught some book of usul al-fiqh as a lesson. Among these books, the most important and most difficult book taught at the highest level, the final book of usul al-fiqh, is 'Tawdih wa Talwih', which is actually a collection of four books: (1) Usul al-Bazdawi, (2) Tanqih, (3) Tawdih, (4) Talwih. Without doubt, the Tawdih of Allamah Sadr al-Sharia contains extremely valuable and rare, most difficult discussions that are either rare or scarce in other books, the expression of which Allamah Sadr repeatedly makes with 'and this is something unique to me'. Then the genius of the age, the investigator and verifier Allamah Taftazani, who is the shining sun of the transmitted and rational sciences, his commentary Talwih containing his profound investigations made the book even more complex, and at times Allamah Taftazani's objections turned the commentary into a criticism. Therefore, among scholars and teachers, Tawdih wa Talwih is considered among the most difficult lessons of the Dars-e-Nizami curriculum, for teaching which a strong heart is required. By the grace and favor of Allah and the kindness and prayers of respected teachers, this humble servant was granted the opportunity to teach the mentioned book eight or ten times in my alma mater, Markaz-e-Uloom Darul Uloom Eidgah Asa Kabir Wala, and until now I have been teaching it for four years at Darul Uloom Rahimiya Multan. During teaching, I obtained the lectures of several skilled and famous teachers who taught Tawdih at that time, namely (1) the perfect saint Hazrat Maulana Ali Muhammad, (2) the investigator of the age Hazrat Maulana Muhammad Musa Khan Sahib (may Allah have mercy on him), Shaykh al-Hadith of Jami'ah Ashrafiyya, (3) the perfect saint Hazrat Aqdas Mufti Abdul Qadir Sahib, Shaykh al-Hadith of Darul Uloom Kabir Wala, which greatly facilitated the understanding of Tawdih wa Talwih. I prepared a copy by keeping these and the marginal notes in front, which later students and friends used by making photocopies. Then a desire arose in my heart that if this too could be published in book form like Tafsir 'Abr al-Yam and al-Tuhfat al-'Ilmiyya, then Allah willing, it would prove beneficial for dear students. After a year of hardship, praise be to Allah, this milestone has become near and easy. Features: (1) In the three sermons (Khutbat), the explanation of vocabulary and phrases has been committed. (2) In the three sermons, the literal translation of the text has been arranged. (3) The text of the commentary Talwih has been segmented and the purpose of each part from the commentator has been clarified. (4) The unjust objections that the commentator Taftazani made against Allamah Sadr al-Sharia have been answered under the title 'Remarks' in the light of commentaries and marginal notes. (5) An effort has been made to clarify the original text itself; excessive discussion and external debates have been avoided as much as possible so that students do not feel bored. On this joyous occasion, I once again express my gratitude to my most affectionate and nurturing father, Hazrat Aqdas Mufti Muhammad Siddiq Sahib (may Allah prolong his shadow over us), who, despite his busy schedule and old age, reviewed the manuscript of this commentary comprehensively and honored me with his valuable advice, and suggested the name 'Misk al-Maleeh' for this book. May Allah reward him with the best reward. Secondly, I am extremely grateful to those great benefactors, respected teachers, and senior scholars (may their blessings remain high) who, despite their various engagements, encouraged me by writing their valuable opinions. Especially the most affectionate and dignified personality, Hazrat Qari Muhammad Idris Sahib (may his honor increase), the manager of Jami'ah Darul Uloom Rahimiya Multan, I am extremely grateful for his gracious opening words. May Allah reward all of them with the best reward. Thirdly, I thank my sincere brothers who supported me with their prayers and valuable advice, especially the honorable brother, Hazrat al-Shaykh Maulana Irshad Ahmad Sahib (may his honor increase), manager of Jami'ah Darul Uloom Kabir Wala, and his honored son Hazrat Maulana Siraj al-Haq Sahib (may his honor increase), teacher of Hadith at Darul Uloom Kabir Wala, and dear respected Hazrat Maulana Mufti Muhammad Nasir Sahib, chief mufti of Darul Uloom Rahimiya Multan (may his honor increase). Fourthly, I am grateful to those dear ones who assisted in drafting, editing, segmenting, refining, copying, and composing of this manuscript, especially Hazrat Maulana Muhammad Mursalin (may he be protected).
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (peysh lafz) to his Urdu commentary 'Misk al-Maleeh' on the Hanafi usul al-fiqh text 'Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. The author begins by praising Allah and greeting, then addresses the students directly. He highlights the importance of Usul al-Fiqh as the key science for deriving Islamic rulings from the primary sources. He mentions the two opinions about its first compiler: Imam Abu Hanifa or Imam al-Shafi'i. He then introduces the book 'Tawdih wa Talwih', which is a composite of four works: Usul al-Bazdawi (by al-Bazdawi), Tanqih (by Sadr al-Sharia), Tawdih (by Sadr al-Sharia, a commentary on Tanqih), and Talwih (by al-Taftazani, a gloss on Tawdih). The author notes that Sadr al-Sharia's Tawdih contains unique and difficult discussions, and Taftazani's Talwih with its critical objections makes the work even more challenging. He explains that his own commentary aims to simplify the text for students by providing vocabulary explanations, literal translations, segmentation of Talwih, and responses to Taftazani's objections. He also acknowledges his teachers, father, and others who helped in producing this work. The author's method is to focus on clarifying the original text and avoid excessive debate. This preface sets the context for the commentary and explains its pedagogical purpose.

Key Terms
اصول فقہ (usul al-fiqh): The science of the principles and rules by which Islamic legal rulings are derived from the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
توضیح تلویح (Tawdih wa Talwih): A composite Hanafi usul text consisting of Tanqih and Tawdih by Sadr al-Sharia, and Talwih by al-Taftazani.
علامہ صدر الشریعہ (Allamah Sadr al-Sharia): The author of Tawdih, a prominent Hanafi jurist and usuli.
علامہ تفتازانی (Allamah Taftazani): The author of Talwih, a renowned scholar of rational and transmitted sciences.
دروس نظامی (Dars-e-Nizami): The traditional Islamic curriculum used in South Asian madrasas, established by Mulla Nizam al-Din Sahlawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, which four books are combined in 'Tawdih wa Talwih'?
A) Usul al-Bazdawi, Tanqih, Tawdih, Talwih
B) Hidayah, Tanqih, Tawdih, Talwih
C) Usul al-Bazdawi, Tanqih, Talwih, Kanz al-Daqaiq
D) Tanqih, Tawdih, Talwih, Maraqi al-Sa'adat

Key Takeaway
Tawdih wa Talwih is a composite of four Hanafi usul works, and the author's commentary aims to simplify it through vocabulary, translation, segmentation, and rebuttals.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Author's Methodology in Misk al-Malīh: A Preface to Hanafi Usul Commentary
Author introduces his commentary and thanks contributors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of the author's commentary methodology and explain how they serve the student of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A commentary on a commentary – Jāmī’s Misk al-Malīh resolves text, translates, and defends Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a against Taftāzānī.

This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on al-Tawdīh wa al-Talwīh, a central Hanafi usul text. The author outlines his pedagogical approach: simplifying vocabulary, providing translation, segmenting the text, and responding to Taftāzānī's criticisms of Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a. Understanding this preface equips you to navigate the commentary's structure and its role in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose
The author states he compiled this commentary to benefit students, based on lectures from Mufti 'Abd al-Qādir and other sources. This preface sets the context for a student-friendly work.
2
List the five features
The author enumerates five distinct features: resolution of vocabulary and structures, literal translation, segmentation of the commentary text with explanation of purpose, responses to Taftāzānī's objections against Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a, and focus on resolving the text itself while avoiding excessive debate.
These features are pedagogical tools for studying a dense usul text.
3
Analyze the scholarly chain
The author thanks his father, teachers, and various scholars. This reflects the transmission of knowledge in Hanafi usul through direct ijaza and personal connections.
4
Note the critical engagement
Jāmī explicitly addresses Taftāzānī's objections, indicating that the commentary is not merely explanatory but also defensive of Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a. This shows the intra-Hanafi dialectic within usul works.
Such critical engagement is a hallmark of the Hanafi usul tradition.
5
Reflect on the author's humility
The author requests readers to inform him of any mistakes, embodying the adab of a scholar. This reminds us that even commentaries are subject to revision and correction.
This humility aligns with the ethical framework of Islamic scholarship.

اشرفیه (۳) ولی کامل حضرت اقدس مفتی عبد القادر صاحب شیخ الحدیث دار العلوم کبیر والا کی تقاریر دستیاب ہو گئیں جن سے حل توضیح تلویح میں کافی سہولت ہو گئی۔ بندہ نے انکو اور حواشی کو سامنے رکھ کر ایک کاپی مرتب کر لی جو بعد میں طلبہ کرام اور دوست احباب فوٹوسٹیٹ کرا کر اس سے استفادہ کرتے رہے ہیں تو بندہ کے دل میں داعیہ پیدا ہوا کہ تفسیر عبر الیم اور التحفتہ العلمیہ کی طرح اگر اس کو بھی کتابی شکل دے کر شائع کر دیا جائے تو ان شاء اللہ عزیز طلبہ کے لئے نافع ثابت ہوگی ۔ ایک سال کی تنگ ودو کے بعد الحمد للہ ثم احمد اللہ اب یہ منزل قریب اور آسان ہو گئی ہے۔ خصوصیات ! خطبات ثلاثہ میں حل لغات وصل تراکیب کا التزام کیا گیا ہے (۲) خطبات ثلاثہ میں عبارت کے لفظی ترجمہ کا اہتمام کیا گیا ہے۔ (۳) شرح تلویح کی عبارت کی تقطیع کر کے ہر حصہ کی غرض شارح کی وضاحت کر دی گئی ہے۔ (۴) شارح تفتازائی نے علامہ صدر الشریعہ پر جو ناحق اعتراضات کئے ہیں۔ شروحات اور حواشی کی روشنی میں تبصرہ کے عنوان سے ان کے جوابات عرض کئے گئے ہیں (۵) نفس عبارت کو حل: کرنے کی کوشش کی گئی زیادہ قیل و قال اور خارجی مباحث سے حتی الوسع اجتناب کیا گیا ہے تا کہ طلبہ المہن محسوس نہ کریں۔
خوشی کے ان لمحات کے موقع پر میں ایک بار پھر اپنے انتہائی مشفق و مربی والد گرامی حضرت اقدس مفتی محمد صدیق صاحب ادام اللہ ظلہم علینا کا شکر گزار ہوں جنہوں نے اپنی مصروفیات و پیرانہ سالی کے باوجو داس شرح کے مسودہ کو بالا ستیعاب ملاحظہ فرمایا اور اپنے قیتی مشوروں سے نوازا اور کتاب کا نام مک الی خو تجویز فرمایا فجزاهم الله احسن الجزاء ثانیاً اپنے ان عظیم مشفقین اساتذہ کرام اور اکابرین علماء عظام دامت بر کاتہم العالیہ کا بے حد ممنون ہوں جنہوں نے اپنی گوناگوں مصروفیات کے باوجود اپنی قیمتی آراء تحریر فرما کر بندہ کی حوصلہ افزائی فرمائی۔
خصوصاً انتہائی شفیق و پر وقار شخصیت گرامی قدر حضرت قاری محمد ادریس صاحب زید مجدہم (مدیر جامعہ دار العلوم رحیمیہ ملتان کا انتہائی شکر گزار ہوں جنہوں نے افتتاحی کلمات مبار کہ تحریر فرما کر ذرہ نوازی فرمائی فجزاهم الله كلهـم احسن الجزاء - ثالثاً ان مخلص بھائیوں کا شکریہ ادا کرتا ہوں جنہوں نے اپنی دعاؤں سے اور قیمتی مشوروں سے نوازا خصوصاً برادر مکرم گرامی قدر حضرت الشیخ مولانا ارشاد احمد صاحب زید مجدہم مدیر جامعہ دار العلوم کبیر والا اور صاحبزادہ مکرم حضرت مولانا سراج الحق صاحب زید مجدہم استاذ الحدیث دار العلوم کبیر والا اور عزیز مکرم حضرت مولانا مفتی محمد ناصر صاحب رئیس الافتاء دار العلوم رحیمیہ ملتان زید مجدہم رابعاً ان عزیز ان کا شکر گزار ہوں جنہوں نے اس مسودہ کی تسوید و بیض تقطیع و تہذیب کتابت کمپوزنگ میں تعاون فرمایا خصوصاً عزیز القدر مولانا محمد مرسلین سلمہ کا انتہائی شکر گزار ہوں جن کی تحریک

شرح القون التاريخ 
مسک الملیح و تعاون اور دن رات کی تگ و دو کے بعد یہ شرح تکمیل کے مراحل تک پہنچی اور اپنے انتہائی مخلص دوست برادرم ابو میسون اللہ بخش صاحب زید مجدہ کا بے حد ممنون ہوں جنہوں نے شب و روز کمپوزنگ کے لئے تعاون فرمایا اور جناب مولوی عبد الرحمن صاحب متعلم جامعہ دار العلوم رحیمیہ اور جناب رانا ثاقب خاں صاحب اور شیخ منور احمد صاحب کا بھی شکر ادا کرنا ضروری سمجھتا ہوں جنہوں نے دن رات محنت کر کے کتاب کی کمپوزنگ مکمل کی ہے۔ اللہ تعالی ان سب کو جزاء خیر عطا فرمائے اور آخرت میں اس کا صلہ عطا فرمائے۔ آمین .
گزارش
آخر میں گزارش یہ ہے کہ الانسان مركب من الخطا النسيان ... چونکہ کتاب انتہائی دقیق ہے اس لئے قوی امکان ہے کہ بندہ سے تعبیر میں یا سمجھنے میں کہیں غلطی ہوگئی ہو اس لئے قارئین کرام سے التماس ہے کہ بندہ کی لغزشوں سے در گزر کرتے ہوئے مطلع فرما دیں تاکہ ان کی اصلاح کی جاسکے۔ خداوند قدوس سے التجاء ہے کہ اس حقیری کوشش کو قبول فرما کر توشہ آخرت بنائے ۔آمین ثم آمین .
دية عبدالرحمن جامی
مقیم دار العلوم رحیمیہ ملتان
۲۰ ذی قعد و ۱۴۲۵ھ
Misk al-Malīh wa al-Talwīh, commentary on al-‘Awf. Ashrafiyya (3) But the complete lectures of His Eminence Mufti ‘Abd al-Qādir, teacher of Hadith at Dār al-‘Ulūm Kabīrwālā, became available, which greatly facilitated the explanation of al-Tawdīh wa al-Talwīh. I compiled a copy from these and the commentaries, which later students and friends photocopied and benefited from. Then the thought came to my heart to publish this in book form like Tafsīr ‘Abr al-Yam and al-Tuhfat al-‘Ilmiyya, so that, God willing, it would be beneficial for dear students. After a year of effort, praise be to God, this goal has become near and easy. Features: In the three sermons, the resolution of vocabulary and structures is adhered to. (2) In the three sermons, the literal translation of the text is arranged. (3) The text of the commentary on al-Talwīh is segmented, and the purpose of each part by the commentator is explained. (4) The unjust objections made by the commentator al-Taftāzānī against ‘Allāma Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a are answered under the title ‘commentary’ in light of the commentaries and footnotes. (5) Effort was made to resolve the text itself; excessive debate and external discussions were avoided as much as possible so that students do not feel burdened. On this happy occasion, I again thank my extremely kind and nurturing venerable father, His Eminence Muftī Muḥammad Ṣiddīq, may God prolong his shadow over us, who despite his busy schedule and old age reviewed the draft of this commentary comprehensively, gave me precious advice, and suggested the name of the book as Misk al-Malīh. May God reward him with the best reward. Secondly, I am immensely grateful to my great kind teachers and senior scholars, may their blessings endure, who despite their various busy schedules encouraged me by writing their valuable opinions. Especially the extremely affectionate and dignified personality of His Eminence Qārī Muḥammad Idrīs, may his glory increase, director of Jāmi‘a Dār al-‘Ulūm Raḥīmiyya Multan, I am extremely grateful for his writing of blessed opening words and favouring me. May God reward them all with the best reward. Thirdly, I thank those sincere brothers who supported me with their prayers and valuable advice, especially the respected and venerable brother Shaykh Mawlānā Irshād Aḥmad, may his glory increase, director of Jāmi‘a Dār al-‘Ulūm Kabīrwālā, and his honourable son Mawlānā Sirāj al-Ḥaqq, may his glory increase, teacher of Hadith at Dār al-‘Ulūm Kabīrwālā, and dear respected Mawlānā Muftī Muḥammad Nāṣir, chief mufti of Dār al-‘Ulūm Raḥīmiyya Multan, may his glory increase. Fourthly, I thank those dear ones who assisted in the drafting, editing, segmentation, refinement, writing, and typesetting of this manuscript, especially the respected Mawlānā Muḥammad Mursalin, may he be protected, whose motivation and cooperation, along with day and night effort, brought this commentary to completion. And I am extremely grateful to my most sincere friend and brother Abū Maymūn Allāh Bakhsh, may his glory increase, who cooperated day and night for typesetting. And I also consider it necessary to thank Mr. Mawlawī ‘Abd al-Raḥmān, student of Jāmi‘a Dār al-‘Ulūm Raḥīmiyya, Mr. Rana Thāqib Khān, and Shaykh Munawwar Aḥmad, who completed the typesetting of the book with day and night effort. May God Almighty reward them all with good and grant them recompense in the Hereafter. Amen. Statement: Finally, I request that since man is composed of error and forgetfulness... because the book is extremely precise, there is a strong possibility that I may have made a mistake in expression or understanding. Therefore, I request respected readers to overlook my slips and inform me so that they can be corrected. I supplicate to the Holy Lord to accept this humble effort and make it provision for the Hereafter. Amen, then amen. Written by ‘Abd al-Raḥmān Jāmī, resident of Dār al-‘Ulūm Raḥīmiyya Multan, 20 Dhī al-Qa‘da 1425 AH.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface from 'Misk al-Malīh', a commentary on 'Al-Tawdīh wa al-Talwīh' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains how he compiled the commentary, acknowledges his teachers and helpers, and outlines the distinctive features of his work. He emphasizes the resolution of vocabulary, literal translation, segmentation of the text, and responses to Taftāzānī's objections against Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a. The preface is a front matter, not a legal ruling, but it sets the context for a rigorous Hanafi usul text.

Key Terms
توضیح تلویح (al-Tawdīh wa al-Talwīh): A foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh by Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a with a supercommentary by al-Taftāzānī.
مسک الملیح (Misk al-Malīh): The title of this commentary, meaning 'The Fragrant Musk', authored by 'Abd al-Raḥmān Jāmī.
خطبات ثلاثہ (Khutbāt al-Thalāth): The three introductory sermons or chapters of the book.
شرح تلویح (Sharḥ al-Talwīh): The commentary on al-Talwīh, which is the main subject of this book.
شارح تفتازانی (al-Shāriḥ al-Taftāzānī): The commentator Sa‘d al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī, author of al-Talwīh.
علامہ صدر الشریعہ (‘Allāma Ṣadr al-Sharī‘a): The author of al-Tawdīh, a key Hanafi usul text.
تفسیر عبر الیم (Tafsīr ‘Abr al-Yam): A Quranic commentary mentioned as a previous publication of the author.
التحفتہ العلمیہ (al-Tuhfat al-‘Ilmiyya): Another previous publication of the author.

Scholarly Humility and the Pursuit of Correction
Author's preface with thanks and plea for error correction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly norms of seeking correction and acknowledging assistance as demonstrated in the author's preface.

Core Idea
A scholar's work is never final; seeking correction is an act of humility and academic integrity.

This lesson examines the preface of Abdur Rahman Jami to his commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The author's acknowledgments and request for correction reveal the ethical foundations of Hanafi scholarship: collaboration, humility, and the recognition of human fallibility. Understanding these norms is essential for anyone engaged in serious study of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's acknowledgments
List the individuals the author thanks and the specific contributions they made (e.g., composing, proofreading).
This demonstrates the collaborative nature of scholarly production.
2
Recognize the request for correction
Find the exact phrase where the author asks readers to inform him of errors. Note that he attributes potential mistakes to human forgetfulness and the difficulty of the subject.
The phrase 'الانسان مركب من الخطا النسيان' is a key acknowledgment of fallibility.
3
Understand the scholarly rationale
Consider why the author anticipates errors: the book is 'extremely precise' (دقیق), so mistakes are possible in expression or understanding.
This reflects the adab of the scholar: humility before knowledge and concern for accuracy.
4
Connect to the Hanafi tradition
Recall that Hanafi scholars often include such requests in their works, showing that seeking correction is part of the scholarly method. This parallels the concept of 'nasihah' (sincere advice) in ilm.
The author's request is not mere formality; it is an invitation to engage in the collective refinement of knowledge.
5
Apply the lesson to your own study
Reflect on how you, as a student of usul al-fiqh, should approach your own reading and writing: be open to correction, acknowledge helpers, and never consider your understanding infallible.
This attitude safeguards the integrity of the discipline and fosters a spirit of collaboration.

The Five Essential Matters Before Studying Usul al-Fiqh
Author explains why five introductory matters are necessary before studying the science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five essential matters required before studying Usul al-Fiqh and explain the rationale for each one.

Core Idea
Knowing definition, subject, purpose, founder, and author's background ensures focused and motivated study of Usul al-Fiqh.

Before diving into Usul al-Fiqh, scholars traditionally outline preliminary matters to provide orientation and motivation. This passage presents a middle path of five matters, balancing the eight matters of early scholars and the three of later scholars. Understanding these five matters prepares the student to approach the science with clarity and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's approach
The author chooses a middle path between the early scholars (eight matters) and later scholars (three matters), citing the hadith 'The best of affairs is the middle.' This reflects a balanced pedagogical philosophy.
The hadith is commonly 'خير الأمور أوسطها'.
2
List the five matters
The five matters are: definition (تعريف), subject (موضوع), purpose/end (غرض غاية), founder (واضع), and author's background (حالات مصنف).
3
Understand the rationale for each
For each matter, the author gives a reason: definition prevents seeking the unknown, subject distinguishes sciences, purpose prevents wasted effort, founder creates enthusiasm for the discipline, and author's background creates enthusiasm for the book.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical value
These matters are not mere formalities; they ensure that the student begins study with clear goals and motivation, which are essential for deep learning.

شرح التوضيح وا
ہر علم کو شروع کرنے سے قبل متعدد اشیاء کا جاننا ضروری ہے تاکہ علی وجہ البصیرت علم کو شروع کیا جا سکے۔ عند المتقد میں آٹھ چیزوں کا جاننا ضروری ہے جنکو روس ثمانیہ کہا جاتا ہے عند المتاخرین اشیائے ثلاثہ کا جاننا ضروری ہے (۱) تعریف علم (۲) موضوع (۳) غرض وغایت ۔ ہم اس کتاب کے آغاز سے قبل متقدمین و متاخرین سے ہٹ کر درمیانی راہ اختیار کرتے ہوئے امور خمسہ کو بیان کریں گے کیونکہ حضورا کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے خیث الامور اوساطها (۱) تعريف (۲) موضوع (۳) غرض غایت (۴) واضع (۵) حالات مصنف۔
سوال ۔ ان امور خمسہ کا جاننا کیوں ضروری ہے؟ الجواب بتعریف کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہے تاکہ طلب مجہول مطلق کی خرابی لازم نہ آئے ، موضوع کا جانا اس لیے ضروری ہے تا کہ امتیاز بین العلوم ہو سکے ، غرض و غایت کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہے تا کہ طالب علم کی محنت بریکار نہ جائے ، واضع کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہے تا کہ اشتیاق الی الفن ہو، حالات مصنف کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہے تا کہ اشتیاق الی الکتاب ہو کما ھو المشہور کہ بازار میں مصنف بکتا ہے مصنف نہیں سکتی۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Commentary on al-Tawdih wa... Before starting any knowledge, it is necessary to know many things so that the knowledge can be started with insight. According to the early scholars, it is necessary to know eight things, which are called the eight matters. According to the later scholars, it is necessary to know three things: (1) definition of the science, (2) subject matter, (3) purpose and end. We, in the beginning of this book, departing from the early and later scholars, adopting the middle path, will explain five matters because the noble Prophet (SAW) said: 'The best of affairs is the middle.' They are: (1) definition, (2) subject, (3) purpose and end, (4) founder, (5) author's background. Question: Why is it necessary to know these five matters? Answer: Knowing the definition is necessary so that the evil of seeking the absolutely unknown does not occur. Knowing the subject is necessary so that distinction between sciences can be made. Knowing the purpose and end is necessary so that the student's effort is not wasted. Knowing the founder is necessary so that there is enthusiasm for the discipline. Knowing the author's background is necessary so that there is enthusiasm for the book, as it is famous: 'In the market, the author is sold, not the book.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is part of the book's introduction. It presents the scholarly tradition of defining preliminary matters before studying a science. The author mentions that earlier scholars (mutaqaddimeen) required eight matters, later scholars (muta'akhireen) required three, but he chooses a middle path of five, citing the hadith about the best being the middle. He then lists the five: definition, subject, purpose, founder, and author's background. The question and answer elaborate the rationale for each: definition avoids confusion with unknown subjects, subject distinguishes sciences, purpose ensures effort is not wasted, founder creates interest in the discipline, and author's background creates interest in the book. This shows the pedagogical concern for both understanding and motivation.

Key Terms
امور خمسہ (umur khamsah): The five essential matters: definition, subject, purpose, founder, author's background.
تعريف علم (ta'rif al-'ilm): The definition of the science, which demarcates its boundaries.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of the science, i.e., what it studies.
غرض غایت (gharad ghayah): The purpose and ultimate end of studying the science.
واضع (wadi'): The founder or originator of the science.
حالات مصنف (halat musannif): The background and credentials of the author of the book being studied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) To differentiate it from other sciences
D) To create interest in the book

Key Takeaway
The five introductory matters—definition, subject, purpose, founder, author—provide the necessary foundation for focused and motivated study of Usul al-Fiqh.

The Five Essential Matters Before Studying a Science
Author explains the five matters necessary to know before studying a discipline.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five essential matters (umūr khamsah) and explain the purpose of each in beginning the study of a science.

Core Idea
Before studying any science, know its definition, subject, purpose, founder, and author's life.

In this opening passage, the author sets out a middle path between earlier scholars who required eight preliminary matters and later scholars who reduced them to three. He chooses five matters and explains why each is crucial for a student beginning a science. Understanding these five matters gives you a framework for approaching any Islamic discipline, especially usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
List the five matters
State the five matters: definition (تعريف), subject (موضوع), purpose (غرض/غاية), founder (واضع), and author's circumstances (حالات مصنف).
These are common in Hanafi intro works.
2
Understand the author's choice
Why does the author choose five instead of eight or three? He takes a middle path, citing the principle 'خير الأمور أوساطها' (the best of affairs is their middle course).
The hadith is used as a general maxim.
3
Grasp the benefit of each matter
For each matter, recall the reason given: definition prevents seeking the unknown; subject distinguishes sciences; purpose saves effort; founder creates eagerness for the art; author's life creates eagerness for the book.
The Q&A section explains each rationale.
4
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Imagine beginning the study of usul al-fiqh. What would be its definition, subject, purpose, founder, and key author? This internalizes the framework.
Example: definition = methodology of deriving rulings; subject = proofs (Quran, Sunnah, etc.)

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. Before starting any science, it is necessary to know multiple things so that the science can be begun with insight. According to the earlier scholars, it is necessary to know eight things, which are called the eight heads. According to the later scholars, it is necessary to know three things: (1) definition of the science, (2) subject matter, (3) purpose and goal. We, before the beginning of this book, deviating from the earlier and later scholars and adopting a middle path, will explain five matters because the Holy Prophet ﷺ said: 'The best of affairs is their middle course.' (1) definition, (2) subject matter, (3) purpose and goal, (4) founder, (5) circumstances of the author. Question: Why is knowing these five matters necessary? Answer: Knowing the definition is necessary so that the error of seeking an absolute unknown does not become necessary. Knowing the subject matter is necessary so that distinction between sciences can be made. Knowing the purpose and goal is necessary so that the student's effort is not wasted. Knowing the founder is necessary so that there is eagerness for the art. Knowing the circumstances of the author is necessary so that there is eagerness for the book, as is well-known: in the market, the author is sold, not the book.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This is the opening of the book, where the author sets out his methodology for presenting the science of usul al-fiqh. He acknowledges that earlier scholars (متَقَدِّمِین) required knowledge of eight preliminary matters (رُؤُوس ثَمَانِیَہ) before studying any science, whereas later scholars (مُتَأَخِّرِین) reduced them to three: definition, subject, and purpose. Choosing a middle path, the author will discuss five matters: definition, subject, purpose, founder, and the author's circumstances. He supports this choice with the hadith 'خیر الأمور أوسطها' (the best of affairs is their middle course). Then he explains, in question-answer form, the benefit of each: knowing the definition prevents seeking something totally unknown; knowing the subject distinguishes one science from another; knowing the purpose ensures the student's effort is not in vain; knowing the founder creates enthusiasm for the discipline; and knowing the author's life creates enthusiasm for the book. The saying 'the author is sold, not the book' means that a well-known author makes his work sought after. This passage is introductory and sets the stage for the detailed exposition that follows.

Key Terms
امور خمسہ (umūr khamsah): The five matters: definition, subject, purpose, founder, and author's circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Before studying any science, a student must know its definition, subject, purpose, founder, and the author’s circumstances to study with insight and motivation.

The Dual Meanings of Usul and Furu' in Shari'ah
Explaining the dual meanings of usul and furu' in the opening of al-Tawdih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible meanings of 'usul' and 'furu' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh literature and explain why the preferred interpretation is 'general proofs' and 'rulings'.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'usul' primarily means general proofs, not beliefs; 'furu' means derived rulings.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih opens by defining key terms. The author presents two possible interpretations of 'usul' and 'furu' and argues for the one most appropriate to the discipline of usul al-fiqh. Understanding these layers is essential for grasping the foundational scope of the science.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the dual interpretation
Identify that 'usul' can mean either general proofs (adillah kulliyyah) or beliefs (aqa'id). Similarly, 'furu' can mean either rulings (ahkam) or righteous actions (a'mal salihah).
2
Locate the author's preference
The author states that the first possibility (general proofs) is preferable because the book discusses general proofs, not theology, and because it ensures istihlal (appropriateness).
3
Analyze the objections and answers
Examine the objection that making the Book firm through itself is invalid, and understand the two responses (different aspects of i'jaz and words/meanings). Also examine the objection about beliefs and the responses.
4
Connect to the tree analogy
See how the 'goodly tree' verse is interpreted to illustrate the result: the foundation (faith) becomes firm and the building (righteous actions) becomes elevated.

Misk al-Malih: ... Explanation: For the intended meaning of 'usul' there are two possibilities: (1) general proofs (adillah kulliyyah), (2) beliefs (aqa'id). The first possibility is preferable because it has istihlal (appropriateness). The book discusses general proofs, not beliefs. According to the first possibility, the meaning of the sentence is: Allah, through His Book, made firm the general proofs of the clear Shari'ah. 'Ihkam' means that the general proofs are hujjah and yield certainty and definitiveness. The ihkam of Sunnah is from His saying: 'Whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you, refrain from it.' The ihkam of Ijma' from His saying: 'And whoever follows a path other than that of the believers, We will turn him to what he has chosen.' The ihkam of Qiyas from His saying: 'So take a lesson, O people of insight.' Objection: Among the general proofs is the Book of Allah itself, so the meaning would be that Allah made the Book firm through the Book, which is making a thing firm through itself, and that is invalid. Answer (1): The first resolution is that the Quran has the quality of i'jaz (miraculousness), and through that Allah made His Book firm. So the Book is the object made firm (muhkam) and the quality of i'jaz is the means of making firm (muhkim). They are the same thing but from different aspects, so no problem. Answer (2): The second resolution is that the muhkam (made firm) are the meanings, and the muhkim (making firm) are the words; meaning Allah made the meanings of the Quran firm through words. According to the second possibility, if 'usul' means beliefs, then the purpose is that Allah made beliefs firm through His Book. 'Ihkam' here means supporting and confirming beliefs. Objection: Beliefs are not proven by the Book of Allah, but by rational proofs, because the very proof of the Book of Allah depends on beliefs. Only someone who believes in the existence and attributes of Allah will accept the Book as the Book of Allah. Thus the commentator's statement that Allah made religious beliefs firm through the Book is incorrect. Answer: (1) It is conceded that some beliefs are proven by rational proofs, but some beliefs are proven by transmitted proofs, such as the vision of Allah, bodily resurrection, and punishment of the grave. Here, these beliefs are intended. Answer: (2) All beliefs, whether proven by rational or transmitted proofs, are considered valid and correct only when they conform to the Book of Allah. So, in terms of proof (thubut), beliefs are not dependent on the Book, but in terms of validity and correctness, they are dependent on the Book. In that respect, the Book makes them firm. For this reason, the commentator chose the word 'ahkama' (made firm) and did not mention 'athbata' (established). (See footnote 1, page 2-3). For 'furu'' there are also two possibilities: (1) If 'usul' means general proofs, then 'furu'' means rulings (ahkam). (2) If 'usul' means beliefs, then 'furu'' means righteous actions (a'mal salihah). If the first, the meaning is that Allah, through His address, elevated the rank and status of the rulings of the Hanafi easy millah. 'Raf'' means raising status. If the second probability, the meaning is that Allah, through His address, bestowed the honor of acceptance upon the righteous actions of the easy Hanafi Shari'ah, thereby elevating their rank. 'Raf'' here means acceptance. 'Hatta' is the result and conclusion of what preceded. Benefit: There are three probabilities for 'hatta': (1) coordinating, (2) inceptive, (3) operating as a particle. By 'kalimah baqiyah', the word of tawhid is meant. By 'asas', faith and heart's affirmation are meant. By 'rusukh', tranquility of heart and inner conviction are meant. By 'bina'', righteous action is meant, which is a branch of affirmation. By 'shumukh', the ascent of righteous action to the place of acceptance is meant. The meaning of the phrase is: When Allah made firm the principles of Shari'ah (beliefs or general proofs) through the Book, and elevated the branches of Hanafi millah (actions or rulings) through the address, then the result came about that the foundation (faith) of the remaining word (tawhid) became firm, and its building and construction became elevated, and the example of this word of tawhid became like a goodly tree (the date palm), whose root is firm in the earth and whose branch is in the sky.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the opening lines of al-Tawdih, explaining the dual meanings of 'usul' and 'furu'. The author first defines key terms: 'al-gharra' (clear/splendid), 'khitab' (address), 'furu' (branches), 'al-hanifiyyah' (inclining towards truth), 'al-samhah' (easy/tolerant). Then he provides a translation of the matn, highlighting that 'usul' can mean either 'general proofs' (adillah kulliyyah) or 'beliefs' (aqa'id), and 'furu' can mean either 'rulings' (ahkam) or 'righteous actions' (a'mal salihah). He argues that the first meaning (general proofs) is preferable because the book is about usul al-fiqh, not theology. However, he also defends the second possibility against objections, noting that some beliefs (like the vision of Allah, bodily resurrection) are derived from transmitted proofs, and even rational beliefs must conform to the Quran to be valid. The author concludes with an allegorical interpretation of the 'goodly tree' (shajarah tayyibah) from the Quran, applying it to the kalimah tayyibah (word of tawhid). The commentary is typical of the Hanafi usul tradition, engaging with multiple interpretations and defending the text against potential criticisms.

Key Terms
اصول (usul): This text defines 'usul' as having two possible meanings: (1) general proofs (adillah kulliyyah) of the Shari'ah, (2) beliefs (aqa'id). The first is preferred.
فروع (furu'): This text defines 'furu' as having two possible meanings: (1) rulings (ahkam) derived from the proofs, (2) righteous actions (a'mal salihah) depending on beliefs.
احکام (ihkam): The act of making firm, establishing as authoritative. In this passage, it means confirming proofs as hujjah or confirming beliefs through the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the first interpretation of 'usul' (general proofs) preferred over the second (beliefs)?
A) Because beliefs cannot be proven from the Quran.
B) Because the subject of al-Tawdih is usul al-fiqh, not theology, and the first interpretation is more appropriate (istihlal).
C) Because the second interpretation leads to a contradiction with the tree analogy.
D) Because the commentator only mentions one possible meaning.

Key Takeaway
The term 'usul' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh primarily denotes the general proofs of the Shari'ah, not theology, and this clarifies the scope of the discipline.
