Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Niche and the Lamp: Opening Metaphors of Usul
Author's opening praises and metaphors for Sunnah and Qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rhetorical metaphors used in the opening of a Hanafi usul text and identify how they frame the role of Sunnah and Qiyas.

Core Idea
The Sunnah is the niche; Qiyas extends its light to new cases.

This lesson unpacks the author's opening metaphors, which are not mere decoration but a profound statement of Hanafi usul methodology. Understanding these images helps you grasp how the Hanafi school views the relationship between revealed sources and rational analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metaphors
Locate the two key metaphors: 'mishkat' (niche) and 'siraj' (lamp). Note how they are described in the passage.
The niche is the recess for the lamp; here it symbolizes the Prophet or the Sunnah.
2
Define each component
According to the commentary, 'mishkat' represents the Prophet's person or the Sunnah, and 'siraj' represents his words (alfaz). The 'lights' (anwar) are the rulings and concepts derived.
The metaphor draws on Quran 24:35 (Ayat al-Nur).
3
Connect to Qiyas
The author says God 'made clear analogy (qiyas) to gather opinions on following the traces of the Sunnah.' Qiyas is presented as a tool to unify scholarly thought around the Sunnah's implications.
Qiyas here is the 'clear path' (mahajjah) to extend rulings.
4
Observe the rhetorical structure
The passage has a cause-effect flow: manifestation of the lamp leads to 'seas of knowledge surging with waves,' and then to 'people entering Islam in crowds.'
This reinforces the idea that proper usul methodology leads to widespread guidance.
5
Extract the usul principle
The metaphors embed the Hanafi view: the Sunnah is the primary revealed source, and Qiyas is the rational method to apply it to new cases, forming a complete system for deriving rulings.
This opening sets the stage for a work that balances naql (transmission) and aql (reason).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوقد من مشكوة السنة لاقتباس انوارها سراجا وها جا واوضح لاجماع الاراء على اقتفاء اثارها قياسا ومنها جا حتى صادفت بحار العلوم والهدى تتلاطم امواجا وريت الناس يدخلون في دين الله افواجا. تفسير: مشكوة: الكوة الخير النافذة التي يوضع فيها السراج. السنة: الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين. اقتباس: أخذ النار من شرارة. سراج: المصباح. إجماع: اتفاق المجتهدين على حكم شرعي. قياس: مساواة الفرع بالأصل في علة الحكم. تشريح: المقصد أن الله أظهر من مشكوة السنة (لسان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم) سراجا وها جا (ألفاظه) لاقتباس الأنوار (المفاهيم والأحكام) وأوضح القياس ليجمع الآراء على اتباع آثار السنة. وقوله "حتى صادفت بحار العلوم تتلاطم أمواجا" نتيجة الإظهار، و"ورأيت الناس يدخلون في دين الله أفواجا" نتيجة الإيضاح. والصلوة على من أرسله لساطع الحجة معوانا وظهيرا وجعله لواضح المحجة سلطانا ونصيرا محمد المبعوث هدى للناس مبشرا ونذيرا وداعيا إلى الله باذنه وسراجا منيرا.
He kindled from the niche of the Sunnah, to derive its lights, a blazing lamp, and he made clear, for the consensus of opinions to follow its traces, a clear analogy, until you encountered the seas of knowledge and guidance surging with waves, and you saw people entering the religion of God in crowds. Explanation: Niche: the recess where the lamp is placed. Sunnah: the path followed in religion. Derivation: taking fire from a spark. Lamp: the light. Consensus: agreement of mujtahids on a ruling. Analogy: equating a branch to the root in the cause of the ruling. Elaboration: The purpose is that God manifested from the niche of the Sunnah (the tongue of the Prophet) a blazing lamp (his words) to derive lights (concepts and rulings), and He made clear analogy to gather opinions on following the traces of the Sunnah. His saying "until you encountered the seas of knowledge surging with waves" is the result of manifestation, and "you saw people entering the religion of God in crowds" is the result of clarification. And prayers upon the one He sent as a helper and supporter of the brilliant proof, and made him a sultan and helper of the clear path, Muhammad sent as guidance for people, a bearer of glad tidings and a warner, and a caller to God by His permission, and a luminous lamp.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary, where the author uses rhetorical metaphors to highlight the role of the Sunnah and Qiyas in deriving Islamic rulings. The source text (matn) likely began with praise to God, and the commentator expands it with vivid imagery. The 'niche' (mishkat) symbolizes the Prophet's person or heart, the 'lamp' (siraj) his words, and the 'lights' the meanings and rulings derived. Qiyas is presented as a clear path to unify scholarly opinions on following the Sunna's traces (the 'athar' are the rulings or their causes). The result is a flourishing of sciences and people entering Islam. The commentator then defines key usul terms: Sunnah (the Prophet's way), Ijma (consensus of mujtahids), and Qiyas (analogy based on common 'illa). He also explains the metaphors in detail, noting that the 'seas' represent the vastness of knowledge, and the 'waves' the interconnected issues. This sets the stage for a work that derives fiqh rulings from revealed sources using rational analogy, firmly rooted in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
مشكوة (mishkāt): The niche or recess in a wall where a lamp is placed; here metaphorically referring to the Prophet (peace be upon him) himself or his blessed person.
سنة (sunnah): The path or way followed in religion; technically: what issued from the Prophet (peace be upon him) of speech, action, or tacit approval.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): The agreement of the mujtahids of the Muslim community in any age upon a legal ruling.
قياس (qiyās): Equating a subsidiary case (farʿ) to an original case (aṣl) on the basis of a common effective cause (ʿilla) for the same ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does the 'lamp' (siraj) in the opening metaphor represent?
A) The Holy Quran
B) The words (utterances) of the Prophet (peace be upon him)
C) The consensus of the scholars
D) The analogy of the jurists

Key Takeaway
The opening metaphors establish the Sunnah as the primary revealed source of light and Qiyas as the rational tool to extend that light to new cases, encapsulating the Hanafi usul method.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
12 min
Metaphorical Interpretation: Mishkah and Siraj in Hanafi Usul
Metaphorical analysis of 'mishkah' and 'siraj'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four possible referents of 'mishkah' and classify the types of isti'ara (metaphor) used in the title.

Core Idea
The Prophet's essence is the niche and his words the lamp — metaphor bridges the sensory to the legal.

In this opening passage, the author unpacks the title 'Misk al-Maleeh' by analyzing the metaphors 'mishkah' (niche) and 'siraj' (lamp). He shows how these terms point to the Prophet and his speech, and then classifies each metaphor rhetorically. Understanding this foundational imagery will help you see how Hanafi usul uses figurative language to affirm the clarity and authority of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four possibilities for 'mishkah'
Find in the passage where the author lists four meanings: the Prophet's essence, person, chest, or heart. Write them down in order.
These show the metaphorical range from the outward person to the innermost reality.
2
Determine the relationship between 'mishkah' and 'siraj'
The author says 'anwar' (lights) means concepts and rulings, and 'siraj' means the Prophet's words. Understand that the niche holds the lamp, so the Prophet's person holds his words which illuminate.
This establishes the metaphor: the Prophet is the container, his words are the light.
3
Classify the types of isti'ara
The passage names three types: isti'ara tafrihiyyah (for 'mishkah'), isti'ara tasrihiyyah (for 'siraj'), and isti'ara takhyiliyyah/tarshiihiyyah (for 'bihar al-ulum' and 'amwaj'). Note the key features of each.
Hanafi usul scholars often employ Arabic rhetorical categories to analyze Qur'an and Hadith.
4
Explain the overall purpose of the metaphors
The metaphors show that Allah illuminated the Prophet's statements so that people can derive rulings. Recognize this as a foundational claim about the clarity and accessibility of the Sunna.
This sets the stage for the importance of qiyas and ijtihad.

صلى الله
تعالی یایھا الذین آمنوا صلوا علیہ الایت (۲) واتباعا با الحديث كما قال حیث ما ذكرت ذکرت (۳) نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم ہمارے محسن ہیں آپ کی بدولت ہمارے اوپر افاضتہ الخیر ہوا کیونکہ عبداللہ انتہائی سفل میں ہیں اور ذات باری تعالی انتہائی علو میں ہے تو فیضان بلا واسطہ ناممکن تھا کسی واسطه ورابطہ کی حاجت تھی وہ واسطہ نبی کریم پاتے ہیں اس لیے وہ منعم ہیں اور شکر اعم واجب شکر یہی ہے کہ آپ پر صلوۃ و سلام بھیجا جائے ۔ الصلوۃ لغوی معنی الدعاء جب یہ منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی طلب رحمت ہوگا جب منسوب الی ملیکہ ہو تو استغفار ہوگا اور جب منسوب الی العباد ہو تو دعاء ہوگا اگر منسوب الی الحیوانات والنباتات والطيور ہو تو معنی تسبیح ہوگا۔ سوال ! معنی طلب الرحمت منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ذات باری تعالی طلب سے منزہ ہیں۔ لان الطلب دلیل الاحتیاج - جواب ! جب منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو طلب کو ترک کر کے صرف رحمت مراد لی جائے گی اس کو صنعت تجرید کہا جاتا ہے۔ سوال ! فقط رحمت بھی منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ معنی رحمت رقۃ القلب ہے واللہ منزه عن القلب ورقتہ ۔ جواب ! رحمت کے دو معنی ہیں (۱) معنی حقیقی و صورقۃ القلب (۲) معنی مجازی و هو تفضل والاحسان و افاضته الخير . جب رحمت
Misk al-Maleeh: Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Explanation: 'Mishkah' metaphorically has four possibilities: (1) the essence of the Prophet, (2) the person of the Prophet, (3) his chest, (4) his heart. 'Anwar' means concepts and meanings, and 'Siraj' means the words of the Prophet, peace be upon him. The purpose of the phrase is that Allah Most High illuminated a shining lamp from the blessed mouth of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, so that people could acquire from this perfect luminous lamp the meanings, rulings, and bright concepts. 'Athar' refers to the actions of rulings. The meaning of the phrase is that Allah made the path of qiyas clear so that people's opinions would unite upon following the fruits of the Sunnah of the Messenger, peace be upon him, such that when unstated (ghayr mansus) issues arise, they are resolved by analogy (qiyas) to stated (mansus) issues due to the commonality of action. If qiyas were not legislated, it would be impossible to resolve those unstated issues and people's opinions would not agree. The result meets the oceans of knowledge and the result of [؟]... The intent is that when Allah lit the perfect luminous lamp and people acquired from it the lights of theoretical and practical sciences, the consequence was that the oceans of knowledge began to surge; and 'you see people entering' is the result of 'that which is evident'. The intent is that when Allah made qiyas clear and people's opinions united upon the Sunnah, people began to enter the religion of Islam in crowds and armies. Metaphors: In 'Mishkat al-Sunnah', the person of the Prophet is likened to a niche (mishkah); the mention of the compared-to (mushabbah bihi) is made, intending the compared (mushabbah). This is an isteara tafrihiyyah. Similarly, in 'siraj'an wahhaja', there is an isteara tasrihiyyah: the words of the Prophet are likened to a lamp. In 'bihar al-ulum', there is idafa (annexation) of the compared-to to the compared; waves are from the necessary implications of the compared-to; this is an isteara takhyiliyyah. The surging is from the appropriate concomitants; this is an isteara tarshiihiyyah. And blessings upon the one He sent with a blazing proof, as a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path: Muhammad, sent as a guidance for mankind, a bringer of good news and a warner, and a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp. Commentary: Solution of vocabulary: 'sati' from 'sutu' meaning to rise high; 'mu'an' is an intensive form meaning abundant assistance; 'zahiran' means continuously helpful because it is a descriptive form; 'mahajjah' means the highway, the main road; 'i'tasama' means to hold firmly; 'ightanama' means to consider as a gain; 'karamah' is a noun from 'takrim' meaning greatness; 'istishab' means to make something accompany; 'istihsan' means to consider something good. The construction 'li-sati' al-hujjah' is a genitive phrase related to 'mu'an', and in it there is idafa of the adjective to the described; originally it was 'al-hujjah al-sati'ah'. In 'mu'an', there are two possibilities: (1) as second object of 'arsala' — but 'arsala' is transitive with one object, how can it be second? Answer: 'arsala' carries the meaning of 'ja'ala' (to make); (2) it is a haal (circumstantial) from the pronoun of 'arsala'. 'Sultanan wa nasiran' is the second object of 'ja'ala'. 'Muhammad' is a substitute (badal) from the relative pronoun in 'man arsalahu', or it is a haal from 'arsala' meaning 'hadiyan', or it is a maf'ul li-ajlih. In this case 'al-mab'uth' is passive; similarly for 'mubashshiran' and 'nadhiran'; the 'thumma' is for order. 'Al-dalalata' is mansub as the object of 'iltazama'; 'karamata' in 'al-istishab' is the object of 'ightanama'; 'min al-muhajirin': 'min' is explanatory (bayaniyyah), clarifying 'al-iltizam'. Translation: 'And mercy be upon the one Whom Allah sent with a clear proof, a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path: Muhammad, who was sent, while being a guide to people, a bearer of good news and a warner, a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp. Then blessings and peace be upon the person who undertook to guide, according to the requirement of the Prophet's indication, towards the path of knowing Allah the Glorious, and who firmly held to the proofs that are mutawatir (i.e., the texts that are manifestly clear), and who considered as a gain the honor of companionship in the noble court of the Prophet, and the honor of considering good (i.e., the Muhajirun and Ansar), and blessings and peace be upon those who followed them in goodness.' Explanation: Question: Why mention salawat after the praise (hamd)? Answer: (1) Following the Book as Allah said: 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him...' [Quran 33:56]. (2) Following the hadith as he said: 'Wherever I am mentioned, send blessings upon me.' (3) The Blessed Prophet is our benefactor; through him goodness was bestowed upon us, because 'abd (servant) is in the extreme lowest, and the Essence of Allah is in the extreme highest; so direct emanation is impossible; there was need of an intermediary and link; that intermediary is the Prophet; thus he is a benefactor, and gratitude for blessings is obligatory; this gratitude is to send blessings and peace upon him. 'Salah' lexically means 'supplication'. When attributed to Allah, it means 'requesting mercy'; when attributed to angels, it means 'seeking forgiveness'; when attributed to servants, it means 'supplication'; if attributed to animals, plants, and birds, it means 'glorification'. Question: The meaning of 'requesting mercy' cannot be attributed to Allah because the Divine Essence is above requesting, for request indicates need. Answer: When attributed to Allah, the requesting is dropped and only mercy is intended; this is called the art of abstracting (tajrid). Question: Even mercy alone cannot be attributed to Allah because the meaning of mercy is tenderness of heart, and Allah is free of heart and its tenderness. Answer: Mercy has two meanings: (1) real meaning: tenderness of heart; (2) metaphorical meaning: favor and benevolence and the bestowal of goodness.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary (sharh) on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a key Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author begins by explaining the metaphorical title 'Misk al-Maleeh' and the phrase 'Mishkat al-Sunnah'. He breaks down the four possible meanings of 'Mishkah' as referring to the Prophet's essence, person, chest, or heart, with 'Anwar' (lights) being the meanings and rulings derived from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and 'Siraj' (lamp) being the very words of the Prophet. The purpose of these metaphors is to show how Allah illuminated the Prophet's statements so that people can derive rulings and understandings. The author then explains that the 'athar' (traces) refer to actions and rulings, and that the path of qiyas (analogy) was made clear so that unresolved issues can be analogically derived from established texts, thus uniting opinions. The result is the flourishing of the oceans of knowledge and the mass conversion of people to Islam. The author then analyzes each metaphor as specific types of isti'ara (metaphorical usage) in Arabic rhetoric. Following this, he offers a lengthy salawat (blessings) on the Prophet, with detailed grammatical parsing of the Arabic phrases, explaining the function of words like 'mu'an', 'zahiran', and the construction of the sentence. Then he provides a translation into Urdu. After that, he addresses a common question: why does the author mention salawat after the opening hamd (praise)? He gives three reasons: following the Qur'anic command, following the hadith instruction, and because the Prophet is the intermediary through whom divine grace reaches humanity—thus gratitude requires sending blessings. He then lexically defines 'salah' and addresses theological objections about attributing 'request' or 'mercy' to Allah, explaining the rhetorical device of 'tajrid' (abstraction) and the distinction between real and metaphorical meanings of mercy. This passage is purely introductory and does not yet delve into substantive usul principles.

Key Terms
مشکوۃ (mishkah): A niche or lamp-holder, metaphorically used for the Prophet's person or essence.
سراج (siraj): A lamp, metaphor for the words of the Prophet.
استعارہ تفریحیہ (isti'ara tafrihiyyah): A metaphor where the compared-to (mushabbah bihi) is mentioned and the compared (mushabbah) is intended.
استعارہ تصریحیہ (isti'ara tasrihiyyah): An explicit metaphor where the word for the compared-to is used directly for the compared.
استعارہ تخیلیہ (isti'ara takhyiliyyah): A metaphor where something is attributed to the compared-to that is a necessary concomitant of the compared-from.
استعارہ ترشیحیہ (isti'ara tarshiihiyyah): A metaphor reinforced by mentioning appropriate concomitants (e.g., waves for ocean).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many possible referents does 'mishkah' have?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Metaphorical interpretation in Hanafi usul is a disciplined tool that relies on Arabic rhetorical categories to derive legal implications from texts.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
14 min
The Obligation of Salawat: Reasons and Linguistic Analysis
Reasons for salawat and lexical analysis of 'salah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three reasons for sending salawat after hamd and define 'salah' lexically, distinguishing its meanings when attributed to Allah, angels, believers, and others.

Core Idea
Gratitude for the Prophet's mediation obligates salawat; Allah's 'salah' is mercy, not supplication.

After the hamd, the author questions why he mentions salawat. He gives three compelling reasons: following the Qur'an, following the hadith, and because the Prophet is the intermediary through whom divine grace reaches us—thus gratitude demands it. He then defines 'salah' lexically and addresses theological objections about attributing 'request for mercy' or 'mercy' to Allah. This passage lays the foundation for understanding the obligation of sending blessings upon the Prophet from a Hanafi perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three reasons for mentioning salawat after hamd
Find the author's answer to 'Why mention salawat after hamd?' He gives three reasons: (1) following the Qur'an, (2) following the hadith, (3) the Prophet as benefactor. List them with brief evidence.
The third reason is based on theological necessity: the Prophet is the intermediary for divine emanation.
2
Define 'salah' lexically and by attribution
The author states 'salah' literally means supplication. Then he gives different meanings when attributed to Allah (request for mercy, but dropped to 'mercy'), angels (seeking forgiveness), believers (supplication), and others (glorification). Understand the shift.
This lexical analysis is crucial for interpreting the Qur'anic command 'send blessings upon him'.
3
Address the first theological objection
Objection: 'request for mercy' cannot be attributed to Allah because request implies need. Answer: When attributed to Allah, the 'request' is dropped and only 'mercy' is intended via the device of tajrid (abstraction).
Tajrid is a rhetorical removal of the requesting aspect.
4
Address the second theological objection
Objection: 'mercy' (rahmah) cannot be attributed to Allah because its literal meaning is tenderness of heart, which is impossible for Allah. Answer: Mercy has a metaphorical meaning: favor and bestowal of goodness. This is the intended meaning.
This shows how Hanafis use metaphorical interpretation (majaz) to resolve apparent anthropomorphism.

ارسل جعل کے معنی کو ضمن ہو گا (۲) حال ہے اوسلہ کی ضمیر سے سلطانا و نصیرا جعل کا مفعول ثانی ہے محمد من ارسلہ کے من سے بدل ہے ہدی یا مفعول لہ ہے یا حال ہے ارسلہ سے بمعنی ھادیا یا مفعول یہ ہے اس صورت میں المبعوث بمعنی المجھول ہوگا اسی طرح مبشر او د اغیا میں بھی یہی ترکیبی احتمالات میں مبشر اور داعیاثم ترتیب کیلئے ہے۔ الدلالۃہ منصوب ہو کر التنزم کا مفعول ہے کرامتہ الاستصحاب میں کرامتہ انتم کا مفعول ہے من المہاجرین میں من بیانیہ ہے من التنزم کا بیان ہے:

صلى الله
تعالی یایھا الذین آمنوا صلوا علیہ الایت (۲) واتباعا با الحديث كما قال حیث ما ذكرت ذکرت (۳) نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم ہمارے محسن ہیں آپ کی بدولت ہمارے اوپر افاضتہ الخیر ہوا کیونکہ عبداللہ انتہائی سفل میں ہیں اور ذات باری تعالی انتہائی علو میں ہے تو فیضان بلا واسطہ ناممکن تھا کسی واسطه ورابطہ کی حاجت تھی وہ واسطہ نبی کریم پاتے ہیں اس لیے وہ منعم ہیں اور شکر اعم واجب شکر یہی ہے کہ آپ پر صلوۃ و سلام بھیجا جائے ۔ الصلوۃ لغوی معنی الدعاء جب یہ منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی طلب رحمت ہوگا جب منسوب الی ملیکہ ہو تو استغفار ہوگا اور جب منسوب الی العباد ہو تو دعاء ہوگا اگر منسوب الی الحیوانات والنباتات والطيور ہو تو معنی تسبیح ہوگا۔ سوال ! معنی طلب الرحمت منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ذات باری تعالی طلب سے منزہ ہیں۔ لان الطلب دلیل الاحتیاج - جواب ! جب منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو طلب کو ترک کر کے صرف رحمت مراد لی جائے گی اس کو صنعت تجرید کہا جاتا ہے۔ سوال ! فقط رحمت بھی منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ معنی رحمت رقۃ القلب ہے واللہ منزه عن القلب ورقتہ ۔ جواب ! رحمت کے دو معنی ہیں (۱) معنی حقیقی و صورقۃ القلب (۲) معنی مجازی و هو تفضل والاحسان و افاضته الخير . جب رحمت
Misk al-Maleeh: Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Explanation: 'Mishkah' metaphorically has four possibilities: (1) the essence of the Prophet, (2) the person of the Prophet, (3) his chest, (4) his heart. 'Anwar' means concepts and meanings, and 'Siraj' means the words of the Prophet, peace be upon him. The purpose of the phrase is that Allah Most High illuminated a shining lamp from the blessed mouth of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, so that people could acquire from this perfect luminous lamp the meanings, rulings, and bright concepts. 'Athar' refers to the actions of rulings. The meaning of the phrase is that Allah made the path of qiyas clear so that people's opinions would unite upon following the fruits of the Sunnah of the Messenger, peace be upon him, such that when unstated (ghayr mansus) issues arise, they are resolved by analogy (qiyas) to stated (mansus) issues due to the commonality of action. If qiyas were not legislated, it would be impossible to resolve those unstated issues and people's opinions would not agree. The result meets the oceans of knowledge and the result of [؟]... The intent is that when Allah lit the perfect luminous lamp and people acquired from it the lights of theoretical and practical sciences, the consequence was that the oceans of knowledge began to surge; and 'you see people entering' is the result of 'that which is evident'. The intent is that when Allah made qiyas clear and people's opinions united upon the Sunnah, people began to enter the religion of Islam in crowds and armies. Metaphors: In 'Mishkat al-Sunnah', the person of the Prophet is likened to a niche (mishkah); the mention of the compared-to (mushabbah bihi) is made, intending the compared (mushabbah). This is an isteara tafrihiyyah. Similarly, in 'siraj'an wahhaja', there is an isteara tasrihiyyah: the words of the Prophet are likened to a lamp. In 'bihar al-ulum', there is idafa (annexation) of the compared-to to the compared; waves are from the necessary implications of the compared-to; this is an isteara takhyiliyyah. The surging is from the appropriate concomitants; this is an isteara tarshiihiyyah. And blessings upon the one He sent with a blazing proof, as a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path: Muhammad, sent as a guidance for mankind, a bringer of good news and a warner, and a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp. Commentary: Solution of vocabulary: 'sati' from 'sutu' meaning to rise high; 'mu'an' is an intensive form meaning abundant assistance; 'zahiran' means continuously helpful because it is a descriptive form; 'mahajjah' means the highway, the main road; 'i'tasama' means to hold firmly; 'ightanama' means to consider as a gain; 'karamah' is a noun from 'takrim' meaning greatness; 'istishab' means to make something accompany; 'istihsan' means to consider something good. The construction 'li-sati' al-hujjah' is a genitive phrase related to 'mu'an', and in it there is idafa of the adjective to the described; originally it was 'al-hujjah al-sati'ah'. In 'mu'an', there are two possibilities: (1) as second object of 'arsala' — but 'arsala' is transitive with one object, how can it be second? Answer: 'arsala' carries the meaning of 'ja'ala' (to make); (2) it is a haal (circumstantial) from the pronoun of 'arsala'. 'Sultanan wa nasiran' is the second object of 'ja'ala'. 'Muhammad' is a substitute (badal) from the relative pronoun in 'man arsalahu', or it is a haal from 'arsala' meaning 'hadiyan', or it is a maf'ul li-ajlih. In this case 'al-mab'uth' is passive; similarly for 'mubashshiran' and 'nadhiran'; the 'thumma' is for order. 'Al-dalalata' is mansub as the object of 'iltazama'; 'karamata' in 'al-istishab' is the object of 'ightanama'; 'min al-muhajirin': 'min' is explanatory (bayaniyyah), clarifying 'al-iltizam'. Translation: 'And mercy be upon the one Whom Allah sent with a clear proof, a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path: Muhammad, who was sent, while being a guide to people, a bearer of good news and a warner, a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp. Then blessings and peace be upon the person who undertook to guide, according to the requirement of the Prophet's indication, towards the path of knowing Allah the Glorious, and who firmly held to the proofs that are mutawatir (i.e., the texts that are manifestly clear), and who considered as a gain the honor of companionship in the noble court of the Prophet, and the honor of considering good (i.e., the Muhajirun and Ansar), and blessings and peace be upon those who followed them in goodness.' Explanation: Question: Why mention salawat after the praise (hamd)? Answer: (1) Following the Book as Allah said: 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him...' [Quran 33:56]. (2) Following the hadith as he said: 'Wherever I am mentioned, send blessings upon me.' (3) The Blessed Prophet is our benefactor; through him goodness was bestowed upon us, because 'abd (servant) is in the extreme lowest, and the Essence of Allah is in the extreme highest; so direct emanation is impossible; there was need of an intermediary and link; that intermediary is the Prophet; thus he is a benefactor, and gratitude for blessings is obligatory; this gratitude is to send blessings and peace upon him. 'Salah' lexically means 'supplication'. When attributed to Allah, it means 'requesting mercy'; when attributed to angels, it means 'seeking forgiveness'; when attributed to servants, it means 'supplication'; if attributed to animals, plants, and birds, it means 'glorification'. Question: The meaning of 'requesting mercy' cannot be attributed to Allah because the Divine Essence is above requesting, for request indicates need. Answer: When attributed to Allah, the requesting is dropped and only mercy is intended; this is called the art of abstracting (tajrid). Question: Even mercy alone cannot be attributed to Allah because the meaning of mercy is tenderness of heart, and Allah is free of heart and its tenderness. Answer: Mercy has two meanings: (1) real meaning: tenderness of heart; (2) metaphorical meaning: favor and benevolence and the bestowal of goodness.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary (sharh) on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a key Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author begins by explaining the metaphorical title 'Misk al-Maleeh' and the phrase 'Mishkat al-Sunnah'. He breaks down the four possible meanings of 'Mishkah' as referring to the Prophet's essence, person, chest, or heart, with 'Anwar' (lights) being the meanings and rulings derived from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and 'Siraj' (lamp) being the very words of the Prophet. The purpose of these metaphors is to show how Allah illuminated the Prophet's statements so that people can derive rulings and understandings. The author then explains that the 'athar' (traces) refer to actions and rulings, and that the path of qiyas (analogy) was made clear so that unresolved issues can be analogically derived from established texts, thus uniting opinions. The result is the flourishing of the oceans of knowledge and the mass conversion of people to Islam. The author then analyzes each metaphor as specific types of isti'ara (metaphorical usage) in Arabic rhetoric. Following this, he offers a lengthy salawat (blessings) on the Prophet, with detailed grammatical parsing of the Arabic phrases, explaining the function of words like 'mu'an', 'zahiran', and the construction of the sentence. Then he provides a translation into Urdu. After that, he addresses a common question: why does the author mention salawat after the opening hamd (praise)? He gives three reasons: following the Qur'anic command, following the hadith instruction, and because the Prophet is the intermediary through whom divine grace reaches humanity—thus gratitude requires sending blessings. He then lexically defines 'salah' and addresses theological objections about attributing 'request' or 'mercy' to Allah, explaining the rhetorical device of 'tajrid' (abstraction) and the distinction between real and metaphorical meanings of mercy. This passage is purely introductory and does not yet delve into substantive usul principles.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): Linguistically supplication; when attributed to Allah, it means mercy (rahmah); to angels, seeking forgiveness; to believers, supplication; to others, glorification.
تجرید (tajrid): Abstraction; removing an element that is inappropriate for the context.
رحمة (rahmah): Mercy; has a real meaning (tenderness of heart) and a metaphorical meaning (favor and beneficence).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'salah' when attributed to believers?
A) Mercy
B) Seeking forgiveness
C) Supplication (du'a)
D) Glorification

Key Takeaway
The obligation of salawat is rooted in Qur'anic command, Prophetic instruction, and the logical necessity of gratitude for the Prophet's mediatory role.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Role of Qiyas in Resolving Unstated Issues
Explanation of the necessity of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why qiyas is necessary for resolving unstated (ghayr mansus) issues and how it unites scholarly opinions.

Core Idea
Qiyas connects the stated to the unstated, ensuring legal consistency and preventing disagreement.

The author explains that Allah made the path of qiyas clear so that people's opinions could unite upon the Sunnah. When unstated issues arise, they are resolved by analogy to stated issues based on shared action. Without qiyas, those issues would remain unresolved and opinions would diverge. This passage highlights the foundational importance of qiyas in Hanafi usul as a tool for expanding the law while maintaining coherence with revealed sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of making the path of qiyas clear
The author says: 'Allah made the path of qiyas clear so that people's opinions would unite upon following the fruits of the Sunnah.' Write down this purpose in your own words.
The 'fruits of the Sunnah' (athmar al-sunnah) refer to the rulings and guidance derived from the Sunnah.
2
Describe the process of qiyas as outlined
The passage states: when unstated (ghayr mansus) issues come, they are resolved by qiyas on stated (mansus) issues due to commonality of action (ishtirak al-'amal). Paraphrase this process.
The commonality of action (al-illah) is the key link.
3
Identify the consequence of lacking qiyas
The author warns: 'If qiyas were not legislated, it would be impossible to resolve unstated issues and people's opinions would not agree.' Recognize the dire consequence.
This underscores the necessity of qiyas for the continuity of Islamic law.
4
Connect qiyas to the overall purpose of spreading Islam
The passage then says: 'When Allah made qiyas clear and people's opinions united, people began to enter Islam in crowds.' See the link between legal coherence and da'wah.
Unity of method leads to unity of the community.

تشریح : مشکوہ کے معنی مرادی میں چار احتمال ہیں (۱) ذات النبی من (۲) تم النبی (۳) صدره (۴) قلبہ انوار سے مراد مفہومات و معانی ہیں اور سراج سے مراد الفاظ النبی صلى الله عليه وسلمے ہیں مقصد عبارت یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے منہ مبارک سے الفاظ کا چمکنے والا چراغ روشن کر دیا تا کہ لوگ اس سراج کامل النور سے معانی و احکام و مفہومات والانور اور روشنی حاصل کریں۔ اثار سے احکام کے عمل مراد ہیں مقصد عبارت یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے قیاس والے راستے کو اس لیے واضح فرمایا تا کہ لوگوں کے اراء سنت رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اثمار کے اتباع پر جمع ہو جائیں اس طرح کہ جو مسائل غیر منصوصہ پیش آئیں ان کو مسائل منصوصہ پر بوجہ اشتراک عمل کے قیاس کر کے حل کر لیا جائے اگر قیاس کو مشروع نہ کیا جاتا تو ان مسائل غیر منصوصہ کو حل کرنا ممکن نہ ہوتا اور لوگوں کی آراء متفق نہ ہوتیں جتی. نتیجیہ ہے صادفت بحار العلوم اوقدر کا نتیجہ ہے مقصد یہ ہوگا جب اللہ تعالی نے چراغ کامل النور کو روشن کر دیا اور لوگوں نے اس سے انوار علوم نظریہ وعملیہ کو حاصل کیا تو نتیجہ یہ مرتب ہوا کہ علوم کے سمندر ٹھاٹھیں مارنے لگ گئے ورئیت الناس يدخلون اوضح کا نتیجہ ہے مقصد یہ ہو گا جب اللہ تعالی نے قیاس کو واضح کر دیا اور لوگوں کی آراء سنت پر جمع ہوگئیں تو لوگ جوق در جوق فوج در فوج دین اسلام میں داخل ہونے لگے : استعارات مشکوۃ السنتہ میں تم النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کو مشکوۃ سے تشبیہ دی گئی ذکر مشبہ بہ کا اور ارادہ مشبہ کا ہے یہ استعارہ تفریحیہ ہے اسی طرح سرا جاوھا جا میں استعارہ تصریحیہ ہے الفاظ النبی میلے کو سراج کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی گئی ہے۔ بحار العلوم میں اضافت لمشبہ بہ الی مشبہ ہے امواج لوازمات مشبہ بہ میں سے ہے یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے تلاطم مناسبات میں سے ہے یہ استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے: والصلوة على من ارسله لساطع الحجة معوانا وظهيرا وجعله لواضح المحجه سلطانا ونصيرا محمد المبعوث هدى للناس مبشراو نذيرا و داعيا الى الله باذنه وسراجا منيرا :
عليق
حل مفردات ساطع من سطوع از نصر بلند ہونا معوانا صیغہ مبالغہ کثیر المعونة از نفر ظهيرا مستمر المعو به لكونه صفة مشحة المحجة جادة الطريق عمده راستة اعتصم چنگل مارنا مضبوطی سے پکڑنا اغتنم عداشی قیمت مساحة فتاء الدار من و ميدان والكرامة اسم من التكريم معناه العظمة الاستصحاب جعل الشتی مصاحباحفه الاستحسان عد الشئی حسنا: اچھا سمجھنا ترکیب سامح الحجہ جار مجرور معوانا کے متعلق ہے اسمیں اضافت الصفۃ الی الموصوف ہے اصل میں الحجۃ الساطعہ تھا معوانا میں د و احتمال ہیں (۱) مفعول ثانی ہے ارسلہ کا سوال ارسل متعدی بیک مفعول ہے معو انا اس کا مفعول ثانی کیسے بنے گا؟ جواب:

شرح التوضيح والتلويح
ارسل جعل کے معنی کو ضمن ہو گا (۲) حال ہے اوسلہ کی ضمیر سے سلطانا و نصیرا جعل کا مفعول ثانی ہے محمد من ارسلہ کے من سے بدل ہے ہدی یا مفعول لہ ہے یا حال ہے ارسلہ سے بمعنی ھادیا یا مفعول یہ ہے اس صورت میں المبعوث بمعنی المجھول ہوگا اسی طرح مبشر او د اغیا میں بھی یہی ترکیبی احتمالات میں مبشر اور داعیاثم ترتیب کیلئے ہے۔ الدلالۃہ منصوب ہو کر التنزم کا مفعول ہے کرامتہ الاستصحاب میں کرامتہ انتم کا مفعول ہے من المہاجرین میں من بیانیہ ہے من التنزم کا بیان ہے:
ترجمہ: اور رحمت کا ملہ نازل ہو اس ذات پر جس کو بھیجا اللہ تعالی نے بلند دلیل ( قرآن پاک کیلئے مددگار اور پشت پناہ اور بنایا اس ذات کو عمدہ واضح راستہ کیلئے والی اور مددگار یعنی محمد ملا ہے جو بھیجے گئے ہیں درانحالیکہ ہدایت دینے والے ہیں لوگوں کو درانحالیکہ مبشر اور نذیر ہیں درانحالیکہ بلانے والے ہیں اللہ تعالی کی طرف اس کے حکم سے اور دورانحالیکہ روشن چراغ ہیں پھر اس کے بعد صلاۃ وسلام نازل ہو اس شخص پر جس نے لازم کر لیا اس نبی کر یم ا اللہ کے اشارہ کے تقاضا کے مطابق رہنمائی کرنے واللہ سبحانہ کی معرفت کے راستے کی طرف اور اس نے مضبوطی سے پکڑے رکھا اس دلالت اور رہنمائی کرنے میں ان دلائل کو جو متواتر ہیں یعنی وہ نصوص جو نما ہرۃ البیان ہیں اور اس نے غنیمت سمجھا اس نبی کریم ملانے کے عمدہ دربار میں صحابی ہونے (ساتھی ہونے ) کی کرامت کو اور اچھا سمجھنے کی کرامت کو یعنی مہاجرین و انصار اور صلوٰۃ و سلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے ان مہاجرین و انصار کی اتباع کی احسان کے ساتھ تشریح : سوال - بعد الحمد صلوٰۃ کو کیوں ذکر کیا ؟ جواب: (۱) اقتداء بالكتاب كما قال الله
صلى الله
تعالی یایھا الذین آمنوا صلوا علیہ الایت (۲) واتباعا با الحديث كما قال حیث ما ذكرت ذکرت (۳) نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم ہمارے محسن ہیں آپ کی بدولت ہمارے اوپر افاضتہ الخیر ہوا کیونکہ عبداللہ انتہائی سفل میں ہیں اور ذات باری تعالی انتہائی علو میں ہے تو فیضان بلا واسطہ ناممکن تھا کسی واسطه ورابطہ کی حاجت تھی وہ واسطہ نبی کریم پاتے ہیں اس لیے وہ منعم ہیں اور شکر اعم واجب شکر یہی ہے کہ آپ پر صلوۃ و سلام بھیجا جائے ۔ الصلوۃ لغوی معنی الدعاء جب یہ منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی طلب رحمت ہوگا جب منسوب الی ملیکہ ہو تو استغفار ہوگا اور جب منسوب الی العباد ہو تو دعاء ہوگا اگر منسوب الی الحیوانات والنباتات والطيور ہو تو معنی تسبیح ہوگا۔ سوال ! معنی طلب الرحمت منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ذات باری تعالی طلب سے منزہ ہیں۔ لان الطلب دلیل الاحتیاج - جواب ! جب منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو طلب کو ترک کر کے صرف رحمت مراد لی جائے گی اس کو صنعت تجرید کہا جاتا ہے۔ سوال ! فقط رحمت بھی منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ معنی رحمت رقۃ القلب ہے واللہ منزه عن القلب ورقتہ ۔ جواب ! رحمت کے دو معنی ہیں (۱) معنی حقیقی و صورقۃ القلب (۲) معنی مجازی و هو تفضل والاحسان و افاضته الخير . جب رحمت
Misk al-Maleeh: Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Explanation: 'Mishkah' metaphorically has four possibilities: (1) the essence of the Prophet, (2) the person of the Prophet, (3) his chest, (4) his heart. 'Anwar' means concepts and meanings, and 'Siraj' means the words of the Prophet, peace be upon him. The purpose of the phrase is that Allah Most High illuminated a shining lamp from the blessed mouth of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, so that people could acquire from this perfect luminous lamp the meanings, rulings, and bright concepts. 'Athar' refers to the actions of rulings. The meaning of the phrase is that Allah made the path of qiyas clear so that people's opinions would unite upon following the fruits of the Sunnah of the Messenger, peace be upon him, such that when unstated (ghayr mansus) issues arise, they are resolved by analogy (qiyas) to stated (mansus) issues due to the commonality of action. If qiyas were not legislated, it would be impossible to resolve those unstated issues and people's opinions would not agree. The result meets the oceans of knowledge and the result of [؟]... The intent is that when Allah lit the perfect luminous lamp and people acquired from it the lights of theoretical and practical sciences, the consequence was that the oceans of knowledge began to surge; and 'you see people entering' is the result of 'that which is evident'. The intent is that when Allah made qiyas clear and people's opinions united upon the Sunnah, people began to enter the religion of Islam in crowds and armies. Metaphors: In 'Mishkat al-Sunnah', the person of the Prophet is likened to a niche (mishkah); the mention of the compared-to (mushabbah bihi) is made, intending the compared (mushabbah). This is an isteara tafrihiyyah. Similarly, in 'siraj'an wahhaja', there is an isteara tasrihiyyah: the words of the Prophet are likened to a lamp. In 'bihar al-ulum', there is idafa (annexation) of the compared-to to the compared; waves are from the necessary implications of the compared-to; this is an isteara takhyiliyyah. The surging is from the appropriate concomitants; this is an isteara tarshiihiyyah. And blessings upon the one He sent with a blazing proof, as a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path: Muhammad, sent as a guidance for mankind, a bringer of good news and a warner, and a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp. Commentary: Solution of vocabulary: 'sati' from 'sutu' meaning to rise high; 'mu'an' is an intensive form meaning abundant assistance; 'zahiran' means continuously helpful because it is a descriptive form; 'mahajjah' means the highway, the main road; 'i'tasama' means to hold firmly; 'ightanama' means to consider as a gain; 'karamah' is a noun from 'takrim' meaning greatness; 'istishab' means to make something accompany; 'istihsan' means to consider something good. The construction 'li-sati' al-hujjah' is a genitive phrase related to 'mu'an', and in it there is idafa of the adjective to the described; originally it was 'al-hujjah al-sati'ah'. In 'mu'an', there are two possibilities: (1) as second object of 'arsala' — but 'arsala' is transitive with one object, how can it be second? Answer: 'arsala' carries the meaning of 'ja'ala' (to make); (2) it is a haal (circumstantial) from the pronoun of 'arsala'. 'Sultanan wa nasiran' is the second object of 'ja'ala'. 'Muhammad' is a substitute (badal) from the relative pronoun in 'man arsalahu', or it is a haal from 'arsala' meaning 'hadiyan', or it is a maf'ul li-ajlih. In this case 'al-mab'uth' is passive; similarly for 'mubashshiran' and 'nadhiran'; the 'thumma' is for order. 'Al-dalalata' is mansub as the object of 'iltazama'; 'karamata' in 'al-istishab' is the object of 'ightanama'; 'min al-muhajirin': 'min' is explanatory (bayaniyyah), clarifying 'al-iltizam'. Translation: 'And mercy be upon the one Whom Allah sent with a clear proof, a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path: Muhammad, who was sent, while being a guide to people, a bearer of good news and a warner, a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp. Then blessings and peace be upon the person who undertook to guide, according to the requirement of the Prophet's indication, towards the path of knowing Allah the Glorious, and who firmly held to the proofs that are mutawatir (i.e., the texts that are manifestly clear), and who considered as a gain the honor of companionship in the noble court of the Prophet, and the honor of considering good (i.e., the Muhajirun and Ansar), and blessings and peace be upon those who followed them in goodness.' Explanation: Question: Why mention salawat after the praise (hamd)? Answer: (1) Following the Book as Allah said: 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him...' [Quran 33:56]. (2) Following the hadith as he said: 'Wherever I am mentioned, send blessings upon me.' (3) The Blessed Prophet is our benefactor; through him goodness was bestowed upon us, because 'abd (servant) is in the extreme lowest, and the Essence of Allah is in the extreme highest; so direct emanation is impossible; there was need of an intermediary and link; that intermediary is the Prophet; thus he is a benefactor, and gratitude for blessings is obligatory; this gratitude is to send blessings and peace upon him. 'Salah' lexically means 'supplication'. When attributed to Allah, it means 'requesting mercy'; when attributed to angels, it means 'seeking forgiveness'; when attributed to servants, it means 'supplication'; if attributed to animals, plants, and birds, it means 'glorification'. Question: The meaning of 'requesting mercy' cannot be attributed to Allah because the Divine Essence is above requesting, for request indicates need. Answer: When attributed to Allah, the requesting is dropped and only mercy is intended; this is called the art of abstracting (tajrid). Question: Even mercy alone cannot be attributed to Allah because the meaning of mercy is tenderness of heart, and Allah is free of heart and its tenderness. Answer: Mercy has two meanings: (1) real meaning: tenderness of heart; (2) metaphorical meaning: favor and benevolence and the bestowal of goodness.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary (sharh) on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a key Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author begins by explaining the metaphorical title 'Misk al-Maleeh' and the phrase 'Mishkat al-Sunnah'. He breaks down the four possible meanings of 'Mishkah' as referring to the Prophet's essence, person, chest, or heart, with 'Anwar' (lights) being the meanings and rulings derived from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and 'Siraj' (lamp) being the very words of the Prophet. The purpose of these metaphors is to show how Allah illuminated the Prophet's statements so that people can derive rulings and understandings. The author then explains that the 'athar' (traces) refer to actions and rulings, and that the path of qiyas (analogy) was made clear so that unresolved issues can be analogically derived from established texts, thus uniting opinions. The result is the flourishing of the oceans of knowledge and the mass conversion of people to Islam. The author then analyzes each metaphor as specific types of isti'ara (metaphorical usage) in Arabic rhetoric. Following this, he offers a lengthy salawat (blessings) on the Prophet, with detailed grammatical parsing of the Arabic phrases, explaining the function of words like 'mu'an', 'zahiran', and the construction of the sentence. Then he provides a translation into Urdu. After that, he addresses a common question: why does the author mention salawat after the opening hamd (praise)? He gives three reasons: following the Qur'anic command, following the hadith instruction, and because the Prophet is the intermediary through whom divine grace reaches humanity—thus gratitude requires sending blessings. He then lexically defines 'salah' and addresses theological objections about attributing 'request' or 'mercy' to Allah, explaining the rhetorical device of 'tajrid' (abstraction) and the distinction between real and metaphorical meanings of mercy. This passage is purely introductory and does not yet delve into substantive usul principles.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from a stated (mansus) case to an unstated (ghayr mansus) case due to shared effective cause (illah).
منصوص (mansus): Stated in the texts (Quran or Sunnah).
اشتراک عمل (ishtirak al-'amal): Commonality of action; the shared feature that links the two cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would happen if qiyas were not legislated?
A) People would rely only on the Qur'an.
B) Unstated issues would remain unresolved and opinions would not agree.
C) Only the Prophet could issue rulings.
D) The Sunnah would be abandoned.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is an indispensable tool in Hanafi usul that ensures legal continuity, resolution of new issues, and unity of the community.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Meaning of Salah When Attributed to Allah
Analyzes the word 'salah' and its attributions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of haqiqa and majaz to explain the meaning of 'salah' when attributed to Allah.

Core Idea
When Allah sends salah, it means mercy, not supplication, using majaz (figurative meaning).

In the opening of his Usul work, the author sends blessings upon the Prophet and then analyzes the linguistic and theological dimensions of the word 'salah'. This lesson unpacks that analysis, showing how Hanafi usul principles distinguish between literal and figurative meanings to avoid attributing imperfection to Allah. The discussion also reveals why sending blessings is an act of gratitude.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition of salah
The text states that salah literally means supplication. However, when attributed to different beings, its meaning shifts: to Allah it means mercy, to angels it means forgiveness, to believers it means supplication, to animals and plants it means glorification.
This is based on the principle of majaz (figurative usage).
2
Apply the principle of haqiqa and majaz
The literal meaning of salah (supplication) cannot be applied to Allah because supplication implies need, which Allah is free from. Therefore, the meaning shifts to a figurative one: mercy. This is known as 'tajrid' (dropping the literal meaning).
Hanafi usul teaches that when a literal meaning is impossible, a figurative meaning is adopted.
3
Address the objection regarding mercy
Even the literal meaning of mercy (tenderness of heart) cannot be attributed to Allah. So mercy must be understood figuratively as favor and beneficence. The text distinguishes between haqiqa (literal) and majaz (figurative) for mercy itself.
This shows the precision of Hanafi theological and linguistic analysis.
4
Conclude the theological significance
Sending salah upon the Prophet is an expression of gratitude because the Prophet is the medium through which goodness reaches humanity. The Companions are also included in the blessings due to their adherence and firmness in guiding others.
The author thus combines linguistic, theological, and ethical arguments.

ارسل جعل کے معنی کو ضمن ہو گا (۲) حال ہے اوسلہ کی ضمیر سے سلطانا و نصیرا جعل کا مفعول ثانی ہے محمد من ارسلہ کے من سے بدل ہے ہدی یا مفعول لہ ہے یا حال ہے ارسلہ سے بمعنی ھادیا یا مفعول یہ ہے اس صورت میں المبعوث بمعنی المجھول ہوگا اسی طرح مبشر او د اغیا میں بھی یہی ترکیبی احتمالات میں مبشر اور داعیاثم ترتیب کیلئے ہے۔ الدلالۃہ منصوب ہو کر التنزم کا مفعول ہے کرامتہ الاستصحاب میں کرامتہ انتم کا مفعول ہے من المہاجرین میں من بیانیہ ہے من التنزم کا بیان ہے:
ترجمہ: اور رحمت کا ملہ نازل ہو اس ذات پر جس کو بھیجا اللہ تعالی نے بلند دلیل ( قرآن پاک کیلئے مددگار اور پشت پناہ اور بنایا اس ذات کو عمدہ واضح راستہ کیلئے والی اور مددگار یعنی محمد ملا ہے جو بھیجے گئے ہیں درانحالیکہ ہدایت دینے والے ہیں لوگوں کو در انحالیکہ مبشر اور نذیر ہیں درانحالیکہ بلانے والے ہیں اللہ تعالی کی طرف اس کے حکم سے اور دورانحالیکہ روشن چراغ ہیں پھر اس کے بعد صلاۃ وسلام نازل ہو اس شخص پر جس نے لازم کر لیا اس نبی کر یم ا اللہ کے اشارہ کے تقاضا کے مطابق رہنمائی کرنے واللہ سبحانہ کی معرفت کے راستے کی طرف اور اس نے مضبوطی سے پکڑے رکھا اس دلالت اور رہنمائی کرنے میں ان دلائل کو جو متواتر ہیں یعنی وہ نصوص جو نما ہرۃ البیان ہیں اور اس نے غنیمت سمجھا اس نبی کریم ملانے کے عمدہ دربار میں صحابی ہونے (ساتھی ہونے ) کی کرامت کو اور اچھا سمجھنے کی کرامت کو یعنی مہاجرین و انصار اور صلوٰۃ و سلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے ان مہاجرین و انصار کی اتباع کی احسان کے ساتھ تشریح : سوال - بعد الحمد صلوٰۃ کو کیوں ذکر کیا ؟ جواب: (۱) اقتداء بالكتاب كما قال الله

تعالی یایھا الذین آمنوا صلوا علیہ الایت (۲) واتباعا با الحديث كما قال حیث ما ذكرت ذکرت (۳) نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم ہمارے محسن ہیں آپ کی بدولت ہمارے اوپر افاضتہ الخیر ہوا کیونکہ عبداللہ انتہائی سفل میں ہیں اور ذات باری تعالی انتہائی علو میں ہے تو فیضان بلا واسطہ ناممکن تھا کسی واسطه ورابطہ کی حاجت تھی وہ واسطہ نبی کریم پاتے ہیں اس لیے وہ منعم ہیں اور شکر اعم واجب شکر یہی ہے کہ آپ پر صلوۃ و سلام بھیجا جائے ۔ الصلوۃ لغوی معنی الدعاء جب یہ منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی طلب رحمت ہوگا جب منسوب الی ملیکہ ہو تو استغفار ہوگا اور جب منسوب الی العباد ہو تو دعاء ہوگا اگر منسوب الی الحیوانات والنباتات والطيور ہو تو معنی تسبیح ہوگا۔ سوال ! معنی طلب الرحمت منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ذات باری تعالی طلب سے منزہ ہیں۔ لان الطلب دلیل الاحتیاج - جواب ! جب منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو طلب کو ترک کر کے صرف رحمت مراد لی جائے گی اس کو صنعت تجرید کہا جاتا ہے۔ سوال ! فقط رحمت بھی منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ معنی رحمت رقۃ القلب ہے واللہ منزه عن القلب ورقتہ ۔ جواب ! رحمت کے دو معنی ہیں (۱) معنی حقیقی و صورقۃ القلب (۲) معنی مجازی و هو تفضل والاحسان و افاضته الخير . جب رحمت

منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی مجازی مراد ہو گا نہ حقیقی فلا اشکال مقصد ہوگا کہ صلوۃ و سلام نازل ہو اس ذات پر جس کو اللہ تعالی نے قرآن حکیم کیلئے معین و مددگار بنا کر بھیجا اور عمدہ طریق ( دین اسلام) کیلئے سلطان ونصیر بنادیا وہ ذات محمد رسول صلى الله عليه وسلمے ہیں جن کو لوگوں کی ہدایت کیلئے مبعوث کیا گیا اور مبشر و نذیر اور داعی الی اللہ اور سراج منیر بنایا گیا، ثم تراخی ترتیب کیلئے ہے کیونکہ صلوۃ علی النبی اصالۃ اور صلوۃ علی الصحابہ تبعاً ہے مقصد عبارت ہوگا کہ صلوۃ علی النبی کے بعد صلوۃ وسلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے نبی کریم اللہ کے اشارہ کے مطابق اللہ سبحانہ کی معرفت کے راستے پر لوگوں کی رہنمائی کی اور اس رہنمائی میں نصوص متواترہ ظاہرۃ البیان کو مظبوطی سے پکڑے رکھا اور نبی اکرم میں اللہ نے ان کو ساتھی ہونے اور اچھا سمجھنے کی کرامت اور اعزاز سے نوازا انہوں نے اس کو اپنے لیے غنیمت سمجھا وہ کون لوگ تھے وہ مہاجر و انصار تھے پھر اس کے بعد صلوۃ و سلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے مہاجرین و انصار کی اتباع کی اچھے طریقہ کے ساتھ ﴿ خلاصہ یہ کہ صلوٰۃ وسلام ان لوگوں پر ہو جن میں تین چیزیں پائی جائیں التزام: اعتصام : انتنام ۔ فائدہ ! شارح نے خطبہ میں براعت استہلال کو اختیار فرمایا۔ براعت استبلال یہ ہوتی ہے کہ خطبہ میں ایسے الفاظ استعمال کیے جائیں جو آنے والے مقاصد کی طرف اشارہ کریں ، مثلا کتاب ، اصول فروع سنت ، اجماع، قیاس، اشاره، دلالت نص، ظاہر، استصحاب، استحسان وغیرہ۔۔ حمد یوں ہے
،
وبعد فان علم الالصول الجامع بين المعقول والمنقول النافع في الوصول الى مدارك المحصول اجل ما يتنسم على احكام احكام الشرع قبول القبول واعزما يتخذ لاعلاء اعلام الحق عقول العقول. حل مفردات امدارک جمع ہے مدرک کی بمعنی جائے اور یہاں مراد دلائل تفصیلیہ یا قواعد کلیہ ہیں المحصول ما ينبغي ان يجعل حاصلام یعنی وہ چیز جو حاصل کی جائے یہاں مراد احکام شرعیہ غیر مستنبطہ ہیں ، يتنسم از باب تفعل خوشبو سونگھنا، احکام احکام الشرع - احکام اول مصدر از باب افعال ہے پختہ کرنا احکام دوم جمع ہے حکم کی قبول القبول قبول اول بفتح القاف ہے مصدر از ( نصر ) معنی باد صبا کا چلنا قبول دوم بضم القاف مصدر از سمع معنی مقبول ہونا یا قبول کرنا اعلام جمع علم بمعنی جھنڈا پہاڑ۔ عقول العقول عقول اول جمع عقل ہے جائے پناہ عقول ثانی جمع عقل ہے یمانی قوت اورا کیہ از باب (ضرب) معنی سمجھدار ہونا اور پناہ لینا۔ ترکیب علم الاصول موصوف الجامع صفت اول النافع صفت ثانی ہے موصوف مع الصفتین ان کا اسم ہے اجل ما تقسم خبر ان قبول القبول مفعول ہے تنسم کا عقول العقول تخذ کا مفعول ثانی ہے۔
ترجمہ! بعد الحمد وصلوۃ پس علم اصول فقہ جو کہ جامع بین العقول والمنقول ہے جو کہ احکام کے دلائل تفصیلیہ تک پہنچنے میں مفید
Translation: And mercy descend upon the one whom Allah sent as a support and helper for the clear proof (the Qur'an), and made him a guardian and helper for the good clear path, meaning Muhammad, who is sent as a guide for people, as a bearer of glad tidings and a warner, as a caller to Allah by His command, and as a shining lamp. Then after that, blessings and peace descend upon the one who committed to guiding according to the requirement of the Prophet's indication to the path of knowledge of Allah, and who firmly held onto the mutawatir proofs that are clearly manifest, and who considered as a gain the honor of companionship and approval of the Prophet from among the Muhajirun and Ansar. And blessings and peace be upon those who followed the Muhajirun and Ansar with excellence. Explanation: Question: Why mention salawat after praise? Answer: (1) Following the Book: Allah says 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him...' (2) Following the hadith: 'Wherever I am mentioned, mention me.' (3) The Prophet is our benefactor; through him, goodness flows to us because the slave is in the lowest and Allah in the highest, so direct effusion is impossible; a medium was needed, which is the Prophet, so he is the granter of blessings, and gratitude for blessings is wajib, which is to send blessings and peace upon him. Al-salah linguistically means supplication; when attributed to Allah, it means mercy; when to angels, it means forgiveness; when to people, it means supplication; when to animals, plants, birds, it means glorification. Question: The meaning of 'seeking mercy' cannot be attributed to Allah because He is exalted above seeking. Answer: When attributed to Allah, the meaning of 'seeking' is dropped and only 'mercy' is intended; this is called tajrid. Question: Mere mercy also cannot be attributed to Allah because mercy literally means tenderness of heart, and Allah is free from heart and tenderness. Answer: Mercy has two meanings: (1) literal meaning: tenderness of heart; (2) figurative meaning: favor, beneficence, and bestowal of goodness. When mercy is attributed to Allah, the figurative meaning is intended, not the literal, so no problem. The purpose is that blessings and peace descend upon the one whom Allah sent as a helper and supporter for the Glorious Qur'an and made him a sultan and helper for the good way (religion of Islam). That is Muhammad (peace be upon him), who was sent to guide people and made a bearer of glad tidings, a warner, a caller to Allah, and a luminous lamp. Then 'thumma' is for order because salawat upon the Prophet is primary and upon the Companions is secondary. The meaning is that after salawat on the Prophet, blessings and peace be upon those who guided people to the path of knowledge of Allah according to the Prophet's indication, and firmly held onto the mutawatir clear nusus, and were honored by Allah with the grace of companionship and approval—they were the Muhajirun and Ansar. Then after that, blessings and peace be upon those who followed them in excellence. Summary: Blessings and peace be upon those who possess three things: adherence, firmness, and connection. Benefit: The author adopted the rhetorical device of 'barā'at al-istihlāl' in the introduction, which is that the introduction uses words that hint at the upcoming topics, e.g., Book, principles, branches, Sunnah, consensus, analogy, indication, textual implication, apparent meaning, istishab, istihsan, etc. Then the praise is as follows: 'After praise and salawat, verily the science of principles (usul al-fiqh), which combines the rational and transmitted, useful for reaching the foundational sources of the product, is the most noble science that one can breathe in the rulings of the Sharia with acceptance, and the most honoring that one can adopt for elevating the flags of truth with the intellect of intellects.' Parsing of individual words: 'madarik' plural of 'madrak' meaning place; here intended as detailed proofs or universal principles. 'Al-mahswl' means that which should be obtained; here intended as non-derived Sharia rulings. 'Yatanassamu' from tafa''ul meaning to smell a good scent. 'Ahkam' first is masdar from if'al meaning to strengthen; second is plural of hukm. 'Qabul al-qabul': first qabul (with fatha) masdar from nasr meaning blowing of east wind; second qabul (with damma) masdar from sami' meaning being accepted or accepting. 'A'lam' plural of 'alam' meaning flag or mountain. 'Uqul al-uqul': first 'uqul' plural of 'aql' meaning place of refuge; second 'uqul' plural of 'aql' meaning intellectual power. Composition: 'ilm al-usul' is mawsuf, 'al-jami' is first adjective, 'al-nafi' is second adjective; the mawsuf with two adjectives is the subject, 'ajallu ma tataqassam' is the khabar, 'qabul al-qabul' is maf'ul of 'tatanassamu', 'uqul al-uqul' is second maf'ul of 'tattakhidhu'. Translation: After praise and salawat, the science of usul al-fiqh, which combines the rational and transmitted, beneficial for reaching the detailed proofs of rulings, is the most noble science that is breathed upon the rulings of the Sharia with acceptance, and the most exalted science that is taken for elevating the flags of truth with the intellect of intellects.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is the author's khutbah and the beginning of the definition of usul al-fiqh. The text first explains the blessings upon the Prophet and his Companions, providing linguistic and theological reasoning for sending salawat. The commentator clarifies that al-salah when attributed to Allah means mercy, not supplication, addressing potential doubts. Then the author defines usul al-fiqh as the science that combines rational (al-ma'qul) and transmitted (al-manqul) proofs, useful for reaching the detailed evidences (madarik) that yield the rulings (al-mahsul). The commentator parses each word to emphasize the precision: 'madarik' refers to detailed proofs or universal principles; 'mahsul' refers to non-derived Sharia rulings. The definition highlights the Hanafi usul methodology that integrates both reason and revelation. Then the commentator notes that the author used barā'at al-istihlāl, a rhetorical device where the introduction hints at the topics to come (e.g., book, principles, branches, etc.). This passage sets the stage for the entire usul work.

Key Terms
الصلاۃ (al-ṣalāh): Linguistically supplication; when attributed to Allah, it figuratively means mercy.
تجرید (tajrīd): A rhetorical device where the literal meaning is dropped and only the figurative sense is intended.
حقیقت و مجاز (ḥaqīqa wa majāz): Literal and figurative meanings; a key usul distinction for understanding texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does 'al-salah' mean when attributed to Allah?
A) Supplication
B) Mercy
C) Forgiveness
D) Glorification

Key Takeaway
When Allah sends salah, it means mercy (majaz), not supplication, based on the Hanafi usul principle that literal meaning is abandoned when it implies imperfection.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: A Science Combining Reason and Revelation
Defines usul al-fiqh and praises it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh as the science that combines rational and transmitted proofs and identify its noble status and utility.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the noblest science, combining aql and naql to derive Sharia rulings.

After the khutbah, the author formally defines usul al-fiqh, describing it as the science that unites rational and transmitted sources, useful for reaching the detailed proofs (madarik) that yield Sharia rulings. This lesson unpacks that definition, highlighting the Hanafi emphasis on integrating reason with revelation. The author also employs the rhetorical device barā'at al-istihlāl, hinting at the topics to come.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definitional phrase
The definition says: 'usul al-fiqh is the science that combines the rational and transmitted, beneficial for reaching the foundational sources of the product (al-mahsul).' The commentator explains key words: madarik (detailed proofs or universal principles) and mahsul (non-derived Sharia rulings).
The phrase 'ajallu ma tataqassam' declares it the most noble science.
2
Understand 'jami' bayn al-ma'qul wal-manqul'
This phrase emphasizes that Hanafi usul integrates both rational reasoning (qiyas, istihsan) and scriptural evidence (Quran, Sunnah). This distinguishes Hanafi methodology from pure literalists or pure rationalists.
The Hanafi school is known for its balance between aql and naql.
3
Identify the utility: 'nafi' fi al-wusul ila madarik al-mahsul'
Usul al-fiqh is not merely theoretical; it is a practical tool to reach the detailed proofs (madarik) that then yield the rulings (mahsul). The commentator notes that mahsul refers to rulings that are not yet derived.
This highlights the applied nature of usul al-fiqh.
4
Recognize the rhetorical device: barā'at al-istihlāl
The author uses words in the introduction that hint at the coming topics: book, principles, branches, Sunnah, consensus, analogy, etc. This is a deliberate literary device to orient the reader.
This shows the author's scholarly sophistication.
5
Apply the definition to appreciate the nobility of usul
The text calls usul al-fiqh 'ajallu ma tataqassam' (the most noble science that one can engage in). This is due to its subject matter (proofs) and its outcome (deriving rulings).
This motivates the student to study it with seriousness.

ترجمہ: اور رحمت کا ملہ نازل ہو اس ذات پر جس کو بھیجا اللہ تعالی نے بلند دلیل ( قرآن پاک کیلئے مددگار اور پشت پناہ اور بنایا اس ذات کو عمدہ واضح راستہ کیلئے والی اور مددگار یعنی محمد ملا ہے جو بھیجے گئے ہیں درانحالیکہ ہدایت دینے والے ہیں لوگوں کو در انحالیکہ مبشر اور نذیر ہیں درانحالیکہ بلانے والے ہیں اللہ تعالی کی طرف اس کے حکم سے اور دورانحالیکہ روشن چراغ ہیں پھر اس کے بعد صلاۃ وسلام نازل ہو اس شخص پر جس نے لازم کر لیا اس نبی کر یم ا اللہ کے اشارہ کے تقاضا کے مطابق رہنمائی کرنے واللہ سبحانہ کی معرفت کے راستے کی طرف اور اس نے مضبوطی سے پکڑے رکھا اس دلالت اور رہنمائی کرنے میں ان دلائل کو جو متواتر ہیں یعنی وہ نصوص جو نما ہرۃ البیان ہیں اور اس نے غنیمت سمجھا اس نبی کریم ملانے کے عمدہ دربار میں صحابی ہونے (ساتھی ہونے ) کی کرامت کو اور اچھا سمجھنے کی کرامت کو یعنی مہاجرین و انصار اور صلوٰۃ و سلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے ان مہاجرین و انصار کی اتباع کی احسان کے ساتھ تشریح : سوال - بعد الحمد صلوٰۃ کو کیوں ذکر کیا ؟ جواب: (۱) اقتداء بالكتاب كما قال الله

تعالی یایھا الذین آمنوا صلوا علیہ الایت (۲) واتباعا با الحديث كما قال حیث ما ذكرت ذکرت (۳) نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم ہمارے محسن ہیں آپ کی بدولت ہمارے اوپر افاضتہ الخیر ہوا کیونکہ عبداللہ انتہائی سفل میں ہیں اور ذات باری تعالی انتہائی علو میں ہے تو فیضان بلا واسطہ ناممکن تھا کسی واسطه ورابطہ کی حاجت تھی وہ واسطہ نبی کریم پاتے ہیں اس لیے وہ منعم ہیں اور شکر اعم واجب شکر یہی ہے کہ آپ پر صلوۃ و سلام بھیجا جائے ۔ الصلوۃ لغوی معنی الدعاء جب یہ منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی طلب رحمت ہوگا جب منسوب الی ملیکہ ہو تو استغفار ہوگا اور جب منسوب الی العباد ہو تو دعاء ہوگا اگر منسوب الی الحیوانات والنباتات والطيور ہو تو معنی تسبیح ہوگا۔ سوال ! معنی طلب الرحمت منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ذات باری تعالی طلب سے منزہ ہیں۔ لان الطلب دلیل الاحتیاج - جواب ! جب منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو طلب کو ترک کر کے صرف رحمت مراد لی جائے گی اس کو صنعت تجرید کہا جاتا ہے۔ سوال ! فقط رحمت بھی منسوب الی اللہ نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ معنی رحمت رقۃ القلب ہے واللہ منزه عن القلب ورقتہ ۔ جواب ! رحمت کے دو معنی ہیں (۱) معنی حقیقی و صورقۃ القلب (۲) معنی مجازی و هو تفضل والاحسان و افاضته الخير . جب رحمت

منسوب الی اللہ ہو تو معنی مجازی مراد ہو گا نہ حقیقی فلا اشکال مقصد ہوگا کہ صلوۃ و سلام نازل ہو اس ذات پر جس کو اللہ تعالی نے قرآن حکیم کیلئے معین و مددگار بنا کر بھیجا اور عمدہ طریق ( دین اسلام) کیلئے سلطان ونصیر بنادیا وہ ذات محمد رسول صلى الله عليه وسلمے ہیں جن کو لوگوں کی ہدایت کیلئے مبعوث کیا گیا اور مبشر و نذیر اور داعی الی اللہ اور سراج منیر بنایا گیا، ثم تراخی ترتیب کیلئے ہے کیونکہ صلوۃ علی النبی اصالۃ اور صلوۃ علی الصحابہ تبعاً ہے مقصد عبارت ہوگا کہ صلوۃ علی النبی کے بعد صلوۃ وسلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے نبی کریم اللہ کے اشارہ کے مطابق اللہ سبحانہ کی معرفت کے راستے پر لوگوں کی رہنمائی کی اور اس رہنمائی میں نصوص متواترہ ظاہرۃ البیان کو مظبوطی سے پکڑے رکھا اور نبی اکرم میں اللہ نے ان کو ساتھی ہونے اور اچھا سمجھنے کی کرامت اور اعزاز سے نوازا انہوں نے اس کو اپنے لیے غنیمت سمجھا وہ کون لوگ تھے وہ مہاجر و انصار تھے پھر اس کے بعد صلوۃ و سلام ہو ان لوگوں پر جنہوں نے مہاجرین و انصار کی اتباع کی اچھے طریقہ کے ساتھ ﴿ خلاصہ یہ کہ صلوٰۃ وسلام ان لوگوں پر ہو جن میں تین چیزیں پائی جائیں التزام: اعتصام : انتنام ۔ فائدہ ! شارح نے خطبہ میں براعت استہلال کو اختیار فرمایا۔ براعت استبلال یہ ہوتی ہے کہ خطبہ میں ایسے الفاظ استعمال کیے جائیں جو آنے والے مقاصد کی طرف اشارہ کریں ، مثلا کتاب ، اصول فروع سنت ، اجماع، قیاس، اشاره، دلالت نص، ظاہر، استصحاب، استحسان وغیرہ۔۔ حمد یوں ہے
،
وبعد فان علم الالصول الجامع بين المعقول والمنقول النافع في الوصول الى مدارك المحصول اجل ما يتنسم على احكام احكام الشرع قبول القبول واعزما يتخذ لاعلاء اعلام الحق عقول العقول. حل مفردات امدارک جمع ہے مدرک کی بمعنی جائے اور یہاں مراد دلائل تفصیلیہ یا قواعد کلیہ ہیں المحصول ما ينبغي ان يجعل حاصلام یعنی وہ چیز جو حاصل کی جائے یہاں مراد احکام شرعیہ غیر مستنبطہ ہیں ، يتنسم از باب تفعل خوشبو سونگھنا، احکام احکام الشرع - احکام اول مصدر از باب افعال ہے پختہ کرنا احکام دوم جمع ہے حکم کی قبول القبول قبول اول بفتح القاف ہے مصدر از ( نصر ) معنی باد صبا کا چلنا قبول دوم بضم القاف مصدر از سمع معنی مقبول ہونا یا قبول کرنا اعلام جمع علم بمعنی جھنڈا پہاڑ۔ عقول العقول عقول اول جمع عقل ہے جائے پناہ عقول ثانی جمع عقل ہے یمانی قوت اورا کیہ از باب (ضرب) معنی سمجھدار ہونا اور پناہ لینا۔ ترکیب علم الاصول موصوف الجامع صفت اول النافع صفت ثانی ہے موصوف مع الصفتین ان کا اسم ہے اجل ما تقسم خبر ان قبول القبول مفعول ہے تنسم کا عقول العقول تخذ کا مفعول ثانی ہے۔
ترجمہ! بعد الحمد وصلوۃ پس علم اصول فقہ جو کہ جامع بین العقول والمنقول ہے جو کہ احکام کے دلائل تفصیلیہ تک پہنچنے میں مفید
Translation: And mercy descend upon the one whom Allah sent as a support and helper for the clear proof (the Qur'an), and made him a guardian and helper for the good clear path, meaning Muhammad, who is sent as a guide for people, as a bearer of glad tidings and a warner, as a caller to Allah by His command, and as a shining lamp. Then after that, blessings and peace descend upon the one who committed to guiding according to the requirement of the Prophet's indication to the path of knowledge of Allah, and who firmly held onto the mutawatir proofs that are clearly manifest, and who considered as a gain the honor of companionship and approval of the Prophet from among the Muhajirun and Ansar. And blessings and peace be upon those who followed the Muhajirun and Ansar with excellence. Explanation: Question: Why mention salawat after praise? Answer: (1) Following the Book: Allah says 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him...' (2) Following the hadith: 'Wherever I am mentioned, mention me.' (3) The Prophet is our benefactor; through him, goodness flows to us because the slave is in the lowest and Allah in the highest, so direct effusion is impossible; a medium was needed, which is the Prophet, so he is the granter of blessings, and gratitude for blessings is wajib, which is to send blessings and peace upon him. Al-salah linguistically means supplication; when attributed to Allah, it means mercy; when to angels, it means forgiveness; when to people, it means supplication; when to animals, plants, birds, it means glorification. Question: The meaning of 'seeking mercy' cannot be attributed to Allah because He is exalted above seeking. Answer: When attributed to Allah, the meaning of 'seeking' is dropped and only 'mercy' is intended; this is called tajrid. Question: Mere mercy also cannot be attributed to Allah because mercy literally means tenderness of heart, and Allah is free from heart and tenderness. Answer: Mercy has two meanings: (1) literal meaning: tenderness of heart; (2) figurative meaning: favor, beneficence, and bestowal of goodness. When mercy is attributed to Allah, the figurative meaning is intended, not the literal, so no problem. The purpose is that blessings and peace descend upon the one whom Allah sent as a helper and supporter for the Glorious Qur'an and made him a sultan and helper for the good way (religion of Islam). That is Muhammad (peace be upon him), who was sent to guide people and made a bearer of glad tidings, a warner, a caller to Allah, and a luminous lamp. Then 'thumma' is for order because salawat upon the Prophet is primary and upon the Companions is secondary. The meaning is that after salawat on the Prophet, blessings and peace be upon those who guided people to the path of knowledge of Allah according to the Prophet's indication, and firmly held onto the mutawatir clear nusus, and were honored by Allah with the grace of companionship and approval—they were the Muhajirun and Ansar. Then after that, blessings and peace be upon those who followed them in excellence. Summary: Blessings and peace be upon those who possess three things: adherence, firmness, and connection. Benefit: The author adopted the rhetorical device of 'barā'at al-istihlāl' in the introduction, which is that the introduction uses words that hint at the upcoming topics, e.g., Book, principles, branches, Sunnah, consensus, analogy, indication, textual implication, apparent meaning, istishab, istihsan, etc. Then the praise is as follows: 'After praise and salawat, verily the science of principles (usul al-fiqh), which combines the rational and transmitted, useful for reaching the foundational sources of the product, is the most noble science that one can breathe in the rulings of the Sharia with acceptance, and the most honoring that one can adopt for elevating the flags of truth with the intellect of intellects.' Parsing of individual words: 'madarik' plural of 'madrak' meaning place; here intended as detailed proofs or universal principles. 'Al-mahswl' means that which should be obtained; here intended as non-derived Sharia rulings. 'Yatanassamu' from tafa''ul meaning to smell a good scent. 'Ahkam' first is masdar from if'al meaning to strengthen; second is plural of hukm. 'Qabul al-qabul': first qabul (with fatha) masdar from nasr meaning blowing of east wind; second qabul (with damma) masdar from sami' meaning being accepted or accepting. 'A'lam' plural of 'alam' meaning flag or mountain. 'Uqul al-uqul': first 'uqul' plural of 'aql' meaning place of refuge; second 'uqul' plural of 'aql' meaning intellectual power. Composition: 'ilm al-usul' is mawsuf, 'al-jami' is first adjective, 'al-nafi' is second adjective; the mawsuf with two adjectives is the subject, 'ajallu ma tataqassam' is the khabar, 'qabul al-qabul' is maf'ul of 'tatanassamu', 'uqul al-uqul' is second maf'ul of 'tattakhidhu'. Translation: After praise and salawat, the science of usul al-fiqh, which combines the rational and transmitted, beneficial for reaching the detailed proofs of rulings, is the most noble science that is breathed upon the rulings of the Sharia with acceptance, and the most exalted science that is taken for elevating the flags of truth with the intellect of intellects.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is the author's khutbah and the beginning of the definition of usul al-fiqh. The text first explains the blessings upon the Prophet and his Companions, providing linguistic and theological reasoning for sending salawat. The commentator clarifies that al-salah when attributed to Allah means mercy, not supplication, addressing potential doubts. Then the author defines usul al-fiqh as the science that combines rational (al-ma'qul) and transmitted (al-manqul) proofs, useful for reaching the detailed evidences (madarik) that yield the rulings (al-mahsul). The commentator parses each word to emphasize the precision: 'madarik' refers to detailed proofs or universal principles; 'mahsul' refers to non-derived Sharia rulings. The definition highlights the Hanafi usul methodology that integrates both reason and revelation. Then the commentator notes that the author used barā'at al-istihlāl, a rhetorical device where the introduction hints at the topics to come (e.g., book, principles, branches, etc.). This passage sets the stage for the entire usul work.

Key Terms
براعت استہلال (barā'at al-istihlāl): A rhetorical device where the introduction hints at the upcoming topics (e.g., book, principles, branches, etc.).
مدارک (madārik): Plural of madrak; literally 'places' or 'sources'. Here means detailed proofs or universal principles from which rulings are derived.
المحصول (al-maḥṣūl): That which is obtained; here, non-derived Sharia rulings (the product of usul).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this lesson, usul al-fiqh is the science that combines what two types of proofs?
A) Quran and Hadith only
B) Rational (ma'qul) and transmitted (manqul)
C) Consensus and analogy
D) Arabic grammar and theology

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the noble science combining rational and transmitted proofs to derive Sharia rulings, and its definition highlights its comprehensive and practical nature.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Virtue and Definition of Usul al-Fiqh
Author praises usul al-fiqh as the noblest science combining reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of usul al-fiqh as 'al-jāmi' bayn al-ma'qūl wa al-manqūl' and explain why it is considered the noblest science.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh integrates reason and revelation to enable ijtihad.

In this opening passage, the author sets the stage by praising usul al-fiqh as the most magnificent science, one that bridges rational inquiry and transmitted texts. Understanding this definition is the first step toward appreciating the discipline's unique role in deriving Shari'ah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical device
Notice the use of barā'at al-istihlāl (براعت استہلال) in the introduction, where the author hints at the topics to be covered—Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas, etc. This sets the reader's expectation.
Rhetorical introductions are common in classical Islamic works to outline the scope.
2
Extract the definition of usul al-fiqh
From the sentence beginning with 'فان علم الالصول...', isolate the core definition: 'الجامع بين المعقول والمنقول' (the science that combines the rational and the transmitted). Write it down in Arabic.
The full definition includes the benefit: 'النافع في الوصول الى مدارك المحصول' (beneficial for reaching the detailed proofs).
3
Unpack the two components
Analyze what 'al-ma'qūl' (rational) and 'al-manqūl' (transmitted) mean. The commentary gives two reasons: some topics are rational (like qiyas) and some are transmitted (like Quran and Sunnah); similarly, some proofs are rational and some are transmitted.
This dual nature is what makes usul al-fiqh unique among Islamic sciences.
4
Understand the benefit and superiority
The author claims it is 'اجل ما يتنسم' (the greatest that inhales the fragrance of acceptance) and 'اعز ما يتخذ' (the most honorable taken). Associate this with the power of ijtihad—the ability to derive rulings for new issues—as highlighted in the commentary.
The mastery of usul al-fiqh is essential for a mujtahid.
