مسک الملیح معنی اور نکات غامضہ عبارات میں مخفی تھے یعنی اس کی عبارت بھی چٹانوں اور سخت پتھروں کی طرح مشکل تھی اسی وجہ سے میں نے اس کی تنقیح تنظیم کا ارادہ کیا مودافیہ سے کیفیت مصنف کا ذکر ہے کہ میری کتاب میں، المحصول، اور ، الاصول، کے مباحث کا خلاصہ ہوگا نیز تحقیقات بدیعہ وتدقیقات عامضہ ہوں گی میں اس میں ضبط و اختصار کروں گا میری کتاب فصاحت و بلاغت کے اعتبار سے ایسی انواع پر مشتمل ہوگی گویادہ انواع سحر ہیں اور میں اعجاز کے کڑے کو مضبوطی سے پکڑے رکھوں گا۔ اختار فی پرسش ہوگی الاعجاز ! ایک شبہ کا ازالہ کیا جارہا ہے کہ سحر کے ساتھ لفظ احداب کا ذکر کیا گیا اور اعجاز کے ساتھ لفظ عروہ کا برعکس کیوں نہ کیا گیا جواب ! اعجاز اقوی من السحر ہے اسی طرح عروہ اقوی من احد اب ہے تو اقوی کا ذکر مع الاقوی اور ضعیف کا مع الضعیف کیا گیا۔ واختار فی العروۃ سے بھی شبہ کا ازالہ ہے اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ احد اب کو جمع ذکر کیا گیا اور عروہ کو مفرد اس میں کیا حکمت ہے؟۔ جواب! اعجاز فی الکلام مفرد ہے اس کا صرف ایک طریق ہے کیونکہ اعجاز فی الکلام کا معنی یہ ہے کہ معنی کلام اس طور پر ادا کیا جائے جو جمیع طرق سے اہلغ ہو اور وہ صرف ایک ہی طریق ہو گا تو جب اعجاز مفرد ہے تو عروہ کو بھی مفروذ کر کیا گیا اور سحر کے انواع و طرق متعدد ہیں تو وہ بمنزلہ جمع ہو گیا اس کیلئے لفظ احد اب کو جمع ذکر کیا۔ وسمیتہ میں نے اپنی کتاب کا نام تنقیح الاصول تجویز کیا اور اللہ تعالی کی ذات سے سوال ہے کہ اس کتاب کے ذریعہ نے مولف و کاتب وقاری، وطالب سب کو نفع. دے اور اس کو خالص اپنی ذات مہربان کیلئے بنا لے وہ نیکو کارو مہربان ہے۔
(Untranslated Urdu preface) Meaning and subtle points were hidden in difficult expressions; i.e., its expression was as difficult as rocks and hard stones. For this reason I intended to revise and organize it. In it, from Mudaafiyya, the condition of the author is mentioned that my book will contain a summary of the topics of al-Mahsool and al-Usool, and also unique investigations and precise subtleties. I will exercise restraint and brevity. My book will contain such types of eloquence and rhetoric that are like types of magic, and I will hold firmly to the handle of i'jaaz. ... And I have named my book Tanqih al-Usool. I ask Allah Almighty to benefit through this book the author, writer, reader, and student, and to make it purely for His gracious sake. He is the Most Kind and Merciful.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This is a front_matter passage from the author's preface. The author explains that the original work (the matn being commented upon) had extremely difficult phrasing, like rocks and stones. Therefore, he resolved to revise and rearrange it. He states that his book will summarize the discussions from al-Mahsool and al-Usool, and will include novel investigations and precise subtleties. He emphasizes conciseness. The author then discusses the relationship between 'sihr' (magic) and 'i'jaaz' (miracle) in the style of his book, justifying the use of collective vs. singular terms. Finally, he names his work 'Tanqih al-Usool' (Refinement of Principles) and prays for its benefit for all and for it to be purely for Allah's sake.

Key Terms
تنقیح الاصول (Tanqih al-Usul): The title of the author's book, meaning 'Refinement of the Principles' of Islamic jurisprudence.
المحصول (al-Mahsool): A foundational work in usul al-fiqh by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, widely used in Hanafi and Shafi'i circles.
الاصول (al-Usool): Probably refers to Usul al-Bazdawi by Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi, a key Hanafi usul text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preface, what is the title of his book?
A) المحصول
B) الاصول
C) تنقیح الاصول
D) مسک الملیح

Key Takeaway
Tanqih al-Usul is a refined summary of al-Mahsool and al-Usool, written to clarify difficult expressions and include novel investigations.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Expanding Matn Phrases and Critiquing Usul al-Bazdawi
Commentator expands matn phrases and critiques Usul al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyse how a Hanafi commentator defines key terms like 'raf‘', 'i‘lām', and 'nukta', and identify the implicit criticism of Usul al-Bazdawi's methodology.

Core Idea
The commentator's expansion reveals that nuanced definitions and implicit critique are essential tools in Hanafi usul scholarship.

This lesson delves into the commentary on the opening of Al-Tawdih. The commentator carefully glosses the matn's terms, distinguishing literal from technical meanings, and subtly critiques the methodology of Usul al-Bazdawi. Understanding this expansion helps us appreciate how Hanafi scholars refined usul texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn phrase being expanded
Locate the base text phrases such as 'ma rufi'a', 'jalil al-shan', 'bahir al-burhan', etc. that the commentator expands upon.
These are short statements from the original matn of Al-Tawdih.
2
Analyze the commentator's gloss
Examine how the commentator explains each term: e.g., 'raf‘' can mean elevation or negation, 'i‘lām' means banner not mountain. Note his use of linguistic analysis.
The commentator uses other hadith to illustrate meaning.
3
Detect the implicit criticism
Identify the four faults the commentator attributes to Usul al-Bazdawi: excess verbiage, lack of organization, unresolved difficulties, and failure to follow rational rules of definition.
This criticism is presented within praise (ta‘rīḍ).
4
Evaluate the excuse given
The commentator excuses early scholars by stating they prioritized conveying meaning over formal perfection. Consider how this softens the critique.
This reflects a methodological stance in Hanafi usul.
5
Connect to usul methodology
Understand how this expansion probe demonstrates tafsir (explanation) and ta‘rīḍ (implicit critique) as tools for refining usul works.
This approach is common in later Hanafi commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسک الملیح
شرح التوضيح والتع
ہے اور فصل خطاب سے خود قرآن کا بیان ہے کیونکہ بعض آیات قرآنیہ بعض آخر کیلئے مبین ہوتی ہیں کما یقال القرآن مفسر بعضه بعضا
ما رفع ای مادام رايات الدين مرفوعة عالية باجماع المجتهدين الباذلين وسعهم في اعلاء كلمة الله تعالى واحياء مراسم الدين فان الحكم الجمع عليه مرفوع لا يوضع و منصوب لا يخفض. ترجمہ ایعنی جب تک دین کے جھنڈے بلند و عالی ہیں مجتہدین کے اجتہاد کے ساتھ جو خرچ کرن والے ہیں اپنی ہمت کو اللہ تعالی کے کلمہ کو بلند کرنے میں اور دین کے مٹے ہوئے نشانات کے زندہ کرنے میں کیونکہ مجمع علیہ حکم بلند ہوتا ہے رکھا نہیں جا سکتا اور نصب شدہ ہوتا ہے پست نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
قوله ما رفع إعلام الخ ۔ غرض شارح توضیح متن ! ما دام سے اشارہ کیا کہ مارفع میں مامصدر یہ حیہ ہے جو مادام کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے رایات سے اشارہ کیا کہ اعلام بمعنی رایہ ہے نہ بمعنی جبل ہے نہ بمعنی علامت ہے عالیہ سے اشارہ کیا رفع بمعنی علو ہے بھنی منع نفی نہیں ہے، حدیث رفع القلم عن الثلاث عن امى حتى تختلم عن المجون حتى افاق وعن النائم حتى استيقظ ، اس میں رفع نفی کے معنی میں ہے اس کے بعد وضاحت کی کہ اعلام دین مجتہدین کے اجماع کے ساتھ اس لیے بلند رہتے ہیں
کہ وہ ہمیشہ اعلاء کلمۃ اللہ کیلئے کوشاں رہتے ہیں اور حکم مجمع علیہ ہمیشہ مرفوع رہتا ہے اس میں کبھی وضع وخفض نہیں آتا۔ قوله جلیل الشان عرض شارح متن کے الفاظ مختلفہ کی تشریح جلیل الشان عظیم سے جلیل کی تغییر کی الامر سے شان کی تغییر کی لیکن یہ تفسیر المشہور بلفظ غیر مشہور ہے، باھر البرھان ،باہر کا معنی غالب و فائق اور برہان کا معنی دلیل و حجت مرکوز مدفون سے معنی بیان کیا ، ركزت الرمح سے ماخوذ ہے جب نیزے کو زمین میں گاڑ دیا جائے الكنوز اموال مدفونہ کو کہا جاتا ہے جمع ہے کنز کی الصخور جمع صخر بڑے پتھر ( چٹان) کو کہا جاتا ہے شبہ سے بیان تشبیہ ہے مصنف نے اصول بزدوی کی عبارات مشکلہ جزیلہ (کثیر الافادہ ) کو صخور اور چٹانوں کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی وجہ تشبیہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح چٹانوں میں جو اشیاء پوشیدہ ہوتی ہیں ان تک وصول مشکل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح ان عبارات میں جو معانی پوشیدہ تھے ان تک پہنچنا بھی متعد رتھا اور جو معانی مستورہ فی عبارات اصول بزدوی تھے ان کو ان جواہر نفیسہ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی جو چٹانوں میں پوشیدہ ہوتے ہیں مرموز رمز سے ماخوذ ہے معنی اشار و بالشفتين ( ہونٹ ) یا بالحاجب (ابرو) بعدی بالی سے بیان فائدہ ہے کر فعل رمز متعدی بالی ہوتا ہے یہاں الحذف والا یصال کے طور پر حرف جر کو حذف کر کے رمز کو براہ راست متغدی کر دیا گیا اور غوامض جو کہ مجرور تھا کو مرفوع کر کے مرموز کا نائب فاعل بنا دیا گیا اصل عبارت یوں تھی مرموز الی غوامض یک جینا ہے جمع نکنند ہے شارح نکتہ کا معنی بیان کر رہے ہیں نکتہ ایسی لطیف و بار یک کلام کو کہا جاتا ہے جو ملح وصاف ستھری ہو

مسک الملیح
شرح التوضيح وا
زوائد سے خالی ہو یہ نکت فی الارض بالقضیب سے ماخوذ ہے۔ بمعنی زمین میں لکڑی سے کھود کرید کرنا عموما انسان جب گہری سوچ میں ہوتا ہے تو لکڑی کے ساتھ زمین کو کرید تارہتا ہے، تو نکتہ بھی گہری سوچ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی لئے اس کا نام نکتہ رکھا گيا قد او می مقصد بیان کیا یعنی مصنف بزدوئی نے اشارات دقیقہ کے ضمن میں نکات خفیہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا النظر سے معنی بیان کیا نظر کہا جاتا ہے کسی چیز کو آنکھ کے ساتھ دیکھنا اور پورے تامل اور گہری نگاہ کے ساتھ دیکھنا، واللحوظ ، متوفر عین گوشه چشم کے ساتھ کسی شئی کی طرف دیکھنا لحاظ خود مؤخرمعین کو کہا جاتا ہے جس طرح موق مقدم عین کو کہا جاتا ہے۔ فصیح التہذیب یعنی کسی شئی کے زوائد وشتائت کو کاٹ کر کے صاف ستھرا کرنا مقولہ پیش کیا تحت الجذع جب کھجور کی زائد انفصان کو کاٹ کر اس کو صاف کر لیا جائے بشر طیکہ اس کے لب و دماغ کی شہنی نہ کائی جائے ۔ وعظیم الدرر کا معنی بیان کیا موتیوں کو لڑی میں ترتیب کے
ساتھ پرونا۔ والكلام لا يخلو عن تعريض ما غرض شارح عبارت مصنف کا مقصد بیان کرنا ! شارح فرماتے ہیں مصنف کی کلام کا مقصد علامہ فخر الاسلام پر قدرے تعریض کرنا گویا مدح کے ضمن میں کچھ نہ کچھ تعریض ہے اور بعض عیوب کا ذکر ہے مثلا (۱) اصول بزدوی میں کچھ زوائد تھے جن کا حذف کرنا ضروری تھا (۲) کچھ شائت و متفرقات تھے جن کا نظم ضروری تھا (۳) کچھ مشکلات و مغلقات تھے جن کا حل کرنا واجب تھا (۴) اصول بزدوی قواعد معقول پر مبنی نہیں تھی جن شرائط کا لحاظ کرنا في التعريفات وائج ضروری ہوتا ہے فی علم المیز ان فخر الاسلام نے انکی رعایت نہیں کی اور تقسیمات میں عدم تداخل اقسام کا خیال نہیں رکھا۔ مما يلفتقت سے خود عذر بیان کیا کہ مشائخ متقدمیں ان چیزوں کا لحاظ نہیں کرتے ان کا مطمح نظر بیان مقصود و مطلوب ہوتا ہے۔ قوله موردا فيه ای فی ذالک المتفح غرض شارح فیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع بیان کرنا بہ ضمیر کا رجع المست ہے جو کہ سنتیجہ سے ضمنا مفہوم ہے اس کا مرجع اصول بزدوی نہیں ہے اسی طرح ضمائر مابعد سالکافیه رسمیت مولفہ کا تبه رسب راجح الى مفتح
ہیں۔
قوله لان الاعجاز في الكلام ان يؤدى المعنى الخ ليس تقيسرا لمفهوم اعجاز الكلام لانه لا يلزم ان يكون بالبلاغة بل هو عبارة عن كون الكلام بحيث لا يمكن معارضته والاتيان بمثله من اعجزته اذا جعلته عاجزا ولهذا اختلفو افى جهة اعجاز القرآن مع الاتفاق على كونه معجزا فقيل انه لبلاغة و قيل باخباره عن المغيبات و قیل باسلوبه الغريب و قيل بصرف الله تعالى العقول عن المعارضة بل المرادان اعجاز كلام الله تعالى انما هو بهذا الطريق وهو كونه في غاية البلاغة و نهاية الفصاحة على ما هوا الرأى
Misk al-Malih: Commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. And it is about the chapter of address from the Quran itself because some Quranic verses explain others, as it is said: The Quran explains some of its parts by others. 'Ma rufi'a' means as long as the banners of religion are raised high by the consensus of the mujtahids who exert their effort in elevating the word of Allah and reviving the rituals of religion. For a ruling agreed upon by consensus is raised, cannot be lowered, and is set up, cannot be brought down. Translation: As long as the flags of religion are high and lofty with the ijtihad of the mujtahids who spend their efforts in elevating the word of Allah and reviving the erased signs of religion, because a consensus ruling is elevated, cannot be placed down, and is installed, cannot be degraded. His saying: 'Ma rufi'a i'lam' etc. The purpose of the commentator of al-Tawdih: he indicated by 'ma dama' that 'ma' in 'ma rufi'a' is a masdariyyah meaning 'as long as'; by 'rayat' he indicated that 'i'lam' means banner, not mountain nor sign; by 'aliyah' he indicated that 'raf' means elevation, not negation. The hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the child until he reaches puberty, from the insane until he recovers, and from the sleeping until he awakens.' In this, 'raf' is in the sense of negation. Then he clarified that the signs of religion remain elevated through the consensus of the mujtahids because they constantly strive to elevate the word of Allah, and a consensus ruling always remains raised; it never undergoes lowering or degradation. His saying: 'Jalil al-shan' – the commentator explained the various phrases of the matn: 'Jalil' is derived from 'azim', 'shan' is derived from 'amr', but this is explaining a well-known term by an unfamiliar one. 'Bahir al-burhan': 'bahir' means dominant and superior, 'burhan' means proof and evidence. 'Markuz madfun' – he explained its meaning, derived from 'rakaztu al-rumh' when a spear is planted in the ground. 'Al-kunuz' are buried wealth, plural of 'kanz'. 'Al-sukhur' plural of 'sakhr' meaning large rocks. He used similitude; the author likened the difficult and beneficial expressions of Usul al-Bazdawi to rocks and boulders. The reason for the similitude is that just as objects hidden in rocks are difficult to access, similarly the meanings hidden in those expressions were difficult to reach. And the meanings concealed in the expressions of Usul al-Bazdawi were likened to precious jewels hidden in rocks. 'Marmuz' is derived from 'ramz', meaning indication by lips or eyebrow; 'ba'di bali' expresses benefit; the verb 'ramaza' is transitive with 'ba', but here the preposition is dropped and 'ramaza' is made directly transitive, and 'ghawamid' which was in the genitive is raised to nominative as the subject of 'marmuz' (deputy agent). The original phrase was 'marmuz ilayhi ghawamid'. The commentator is explaining the meaning of 'nuktah': a subtle, fine speech that is pure and free of defects, derived from 'nakata fi al-ard bi al-qadib' meaning to dig and poke the ground with a stick. Generally, when a person is in deep thought, he pokes the ground with a stick; thus 'nuktah' is obtained from deep thought, hence its name. The author of al-Bazdawi indicated subtle points and hidden nuances. 'Nazar' means to look at something with the eye and with full contemplation and deep gaze; 'luhaz' means to look at something with the corner of the eye; 'lahaz' is the corner of the eye, just as 'muq' is the front of the eye. 'Fasih al-tahdhib' means to cut off the excesses and irregularities of something and make it clean; he presented the saying 'tahta al-jidh' when the excess branches of a date palm are cut off and cleaned, provided its core and mind are not damaged. 'Wa 'azim al-durar' – he explained its meaning as stringing pearls in order. And the speech is not free from some criticism. The commentator explains the author's purpose: the author's speech is somewhat critical of Allamah Fakhr al-Islam, as if there is some criticism within praise, and he mentions some faults, e.g., (1) Usul al-Bazdawi had some excesses that needed removal, (2) some scattered parts that needed organization, (3) some difficulties and complexities that needed solution, (4) Usul al-Bazdawi was not based on rational principles whose consideration is necessary in definitions for the science of logic; Fakhr al-Islam did not observe these, and in divisions he did not consider non-overlap of categories. From 'mimma yaltafitu' he himself gave an excuse that the early scholars did not observe these things; their focus was on expressing the intended meaning. His saying: 'muwridan fihi' i.e., in that discussed matter; the commentator explains the referent of the pronoun 'fihi': the pronoun refers to 'al-mustanbit' which is implicitly understood from 'sanatiju', not to Usul al-Bazdawi; similarly for subsequent pronouns. His saying: 'Because the inimitability of speech is that it conveys the meaning...' is not a restriction of the concept of inimitability, because it does not have to be by eloquence; rather it is that the speech cannot be opposed and something like it cannot be produced; from 'a'jiztuhu' when you make him unable. Hence they differed on the aspect of inimitability of the Quran while agreeing that it is inimitable: some said it is due to eloquence, some said due to its reports of the unseen, some said due to its unique style, some said due to Allah turning minds away from opposing it. Rather the intended meaning is that the inimitability of the speech of Allah is but this path: that it is at the utmost eloquence and ultimate fluency, as is the view.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the opening phrases of the matn of al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The commentator begins by explaining the term 'ma rufi'a' (what is raised), clarifying that it means 'as long as' (ma dama) and that 'i'lam' refers to banners, not mountains or signs. The raising is one of elevation, not negation, except in the hadith of lifting the pen where 'raf' has a negative sense. The commentator emphasizes that the signs of religion remain elevated through the consensus of mujtahids who strive to exalt Allah's word. He then glosses the author's phrases 'Jalil al-shan', 'Bahir al-burhan', 'Markuz madfun', and 'al-sukhur', explaining that the author of Usul al-Bazdawi likened his difficult expressions to rocks containing precious jewels, indicating the effort needed to extract their meanings. The term 'marmuz' is analyzed as derived from 'ramz' (gesture), and the grammatical change from 'marmuz ilayhi' to 'marmuz' directly transitive is noted. 'Nuktah' is defined as a subtle point obtained through deep contemplation, from the act of poking the ground. 'Nazar' and 'luhaz' are distinguished as types of looking. 'Fasih al-tahdhib' means to prune excess, from date palm trimming. 'Azim al-durar' means stringing pearls. The commentator then reveals that the author's speech contains implicit criticism of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, listing four shortcomings: excess verbiage, lack of organization, unresolved difficulties, and failure to observe rational rules of definition and classification. However, the commentator excuses this by noting that early scholars prioritized conveying meaning over formal perfection. Finally, he discusses the inimitability (i'jaz) of the Quran, stating that it is not restricted to eloquence but is the inability to produce similar speech, with various opinions on its aspect, concluding that the correct view is that it lies in extreme eloquence and fluency.

Key Terms
رفع (raf‘): Elevation or lifting; in the hadith, it means negation (of accountability).
اعلام (a‘lām): Banners or signs of religion, not mountains or symbols.
نکتہ (nukta): A subtle point or fine meaning obtained through deep contemplation, derived from poking the ground.
تعریض (ta‘rīḍ): Indirect criticism or allusion, often within praise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three', what does 'raf‘' (lifting) mean according to the commentator?
A) Literal physical lifting
B) Elevation of status
C) Negation (removal of accountability)
D) Exemption from punishment

Key Takeaway
Commentary on usul texts often involves subtle linguistic distinctions and implicit critique, revealing the depth of Hanafi scholastic method.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Structure of Al-Tawdih: Introduction and Two Sections
Explaining the overall structure of the book Al-Tawdih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the overall structure of Al-Tawdih and resolve the apparent contradiction between the author and commentator regarding the number of sections.

Core Idea
Al-Tawdih: introduction (preliminaries) + two main sections (evidences and rulings). The contradiction is resolved by context.

This passage from Misk al-Malih introduces the structure of Al-Tawdih, a foundational Hanafi usul text. The commentator al-Taftazani outlines the book's components and addresses a seeming discrepancy: the author Sadr al-Shari'a says 'the book is arranged into two sections,' while al-Taftazani includes an introduction. Understanding this structure helps you navigate any Hanafi usul text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components
Al-Taftazani states that Al-Tawdih consists of an introduction (muqaddimah), a first section (al-qism al-awwal), and a second section (al-qism al-thani). The introduction covers definitions and subject matter of usul al-fiqh.
The introduction is considered preliminary (mabadi'), not part of the core subject matter.
2
Understand the apparent contradiction
Sadr al-Shari'a, the author, writes 'we arrange the book into two sections,' which seems to omit the introduction. Al-Taftazani's summary includes the introduction, creating an apparent conflict.
The objection is based on a literal reading of the author's statement.
3
Follow the harmonization
Al-Taftazani gives two answers: (1) The author's statement refers only to the subject matter (maqasid al-fann), while the commentator includes both subject matter and preliminaries. (2) The author's statement comes after completing the introduction, so from that point on, the book is arranged into two sections; the introduction is already passed. Both statements are correct in their context.
This shows the importance of context in interpreting texts.
4
Note the justification for the section division
Everything in the book is either preliminary (introduction) or substantive. Substantive content deals either with evidences (adilla) or rulings (ahkam). Hence two sections: first on evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas, plus appendices on tarjih and ijtihad), second on rulings (hukm, mahkum bih, mahkum alayh).
The appendices are not independent but subsidiary to Qiyas.

Misk al-Malih Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: Sharh al-Talwih. His saying: 'Usul al-Fiqh: the book is arranged on an introduction and two sections.' The aim of the commentator al-Taftazani is to summarize the book al-Tawdih. Thus he said: The entire book al-Tawdih consists of an introduction and two sections. Objection: The commentator's statement contradicts the author's statement, because later the author himself will say 'We arrange the book into two sections.' So from the author's words it is understood that al-Tawdih is arranged into only two sections, while the commentator says it has two sections and an introduction. There is conflict. Answer (1): There is no contradiction between the author and commentator because the commentator's intention is to summarize the entire book al-Tawdih, including both the subject matter (maqasid al-fann) and preliminaries (mabadi'), while the author's statement 'we arrange the book into two sections' refers only to the subject matter, which is arranged into two sections; the introduction is excluded. Answer (2): The author's statement comes after completing the introduction, so from that point the book is arranged into two sections, since the introduction has already passed. The commentator's statement includes the introduction. Thus both statements are correct in their respective contexts. Because 'what is mentioned in it' (lan al-madhkūr fīh): al-Taftazani explains the reason for the division. The summary of the division: Whatever is mentioned in this book either pertains to the subject matter of the science or not. If not, it is called the introduction. If it is from the subject matter, then it is either a discussion of evidences (adilla) or rulings (ahkam). If it is discussion of evidences, that is the first section. If it is discussion of rulings, that is the second section, because in this science only these two things are discussed. The first section is built on four pillars: (1) the Book (Qur'an), (2) the Sunnah, (3) Consensus (Ijma'), (4) Analogy (Qiyas). It is appended with two chapters: tarjih (preponderation) and ijtihad. The commentator aims to answer a presumed objection: It is said that your statement that the first section consists of four pillars is incorrect; it includes a chapter on tarjih between evidences and reasons and a chapter on ijtihad, so these are six pillars, not four. The commentator answers: These two chapters are subsidiary (mudhayyal); they are attached. The lexical meaning of 'dhayl' is 'hem'; the intended meaning is to mention something secondarily. The point is that these two chapters are not independent but subsidiary and subordinate to Qiyas; they are part of its completion and supplement, so no problem. The second section consists of three chapters: (1) Hukm (ruling), (2) Mahkum bih (the thing ruled upon), (3) Mahkum 'alayh (the person ruled upon). The reason for the limitation will come soon. And the introduction is dedicated to... The commentator al-Taftazani wants to explain what matters are mentioned in the introduction. He says that in the introduction two things will be mentioned: (1) the definition of the science of usul al-fiqh, (2) its subject matter. Because it is the right of the student...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a structural overview of al-Tawdih, one of the foundational Hanafi usul texts. The commentator, al-Taftazani, clarifies that the entire work consists of an introduction (muqaddimah) and two main sections (qismayn). A potential contradiction is raised: the author Sadr al-Shari'a says 'we arrange the book into two sections,' seemingly omitting the introduction. The harmonization is that the author's statement is made after completing the introduction, so he refers only to the two sections of substantive content. The commentator's summary includes the introduction as a preliminary. Thus no real conflict. The division is justified: everything in the book is either preliminary (introduction) or substantive; the substantive part deals either with evidences (adilla) or rulings (ahkam). Evidences are four: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas. Additional chapters on tarjih and ijtihad are not separate pillars but appendices to Qiyas. The second section has three chapters on the ruling (hukm), the object of ruling (mahkum bih), and the subject of ruling (mahkum alayh). The introduction defines the science and its subject matter. This structure is typical of Hanafi usul works; it shows the rational organization of the science.

Key Terms
المقدمة (al-muqaddimah): The introduction of the book that deals with the definition and subject matter of usul al-fiqh, i.e., the preliminaries (mabadi') of the science.
القسم الأول (al-qism al-awwal): The first section of al-Tawdih, covering the four evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) plus appendices on tarjih and ijtihad.
القسم الثاني (al-qism al-thānī): The second section of al-Tawdih, covering the ruling (hukm), the object of ruling (mahkum bih), and the subject of ruling (mahkum 'alayh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does al-Taftazani reconcile the apparent contradiction that Sadr al-Shari'a says the book has two sections while he says it has an introduction plus two sections?
A) He admits it is a contradiction and prefers the author's view
B) He says the author's statement refers only to the substantive content after the introduction is finished
C) He says the introduction is actually one of the two sections
D) He says the book has three sections

Key Takeaway
Al-Tawdih is organized into an introduction (preliminaries) and two substantive sections: one on the four evidences (with appendices on tarjih and ijtihad) and one on rulings (hukm, mahkum bih, mahkum alayh).

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Structure of Al-Tawdih: Muqaddimah and Two Sections
Explaining the book's structure and resolving a seeming contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the division of Al-Tawdih into a muqaddimah and two sections, identify the four pillars of the first section, and explain why the chapters on tarjih and ijtihad are appended rather than independent pillars.

Core Idea
Al-Tawdih is arranged as a muqaddimah and two sections: the first on proofs (four pillars) and the second on rulings (three chapters).

This lesson examines the overall structure of Al-Tawdih as explained by its commentator, Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The book is divided into a preface (muqaddimah) and two main sections. The first section deals with the sources of law (four pillars), while the second covers rulings and their subjects. We will also see how an apparent contradiction between the author and commentator is resolved, and why additional chapters on tarjih and ijtihad do not increase the number of pillars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about the book's structure
Find where Taftazani states that Al-Tawdih is arranged into a muqaddimah and two sections. Recognize that this is a summary of the entire book.
2
Recognize the objection
The author of the matn says 'we divide the book into two sections,' which seems to contradict the inclusion of a preface. Understand why this creates a potential conflict.
The objection arises if one reads the author's statement as excluding the preface.
3
Analyze the two answers that resolve the contradiction
Both answers show that the author's 'two sections' refers only to the core content after the preface, while the commentator includes the preface in his description. Both are correct from their respective contexts.
Answer 1: Author deals with purposes of the discipline; Answer 2: Author's statement comes after the preface.
4
Examine the first section's four pillars
The first section (on proofs) is built upon four arkan: the Book, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. Note that chapters on Tarjih and Ijtihad are appended (mudhayyal) to this section.
These two chapters are subsidiary to Qiyas, not independent pillars.
5
Examine the second section's three chapters
The second section (on rulings) consists of three chapters: Hukm (ruling), Mahkum bih (object of ruling), and Mahkum alayh (subject of ruling). The reason for this division will be explained later in the book.

موضوع ہے لہذا طالب علم کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ ہر علم کے مسائل کثیرہ معلوم کرنے سے پہلے اس کی تعریف اور اس کا موضوع جان لے اس طرح وہ مقصود کے فوت ہونے اور غیر مقصود میں اشتعال سے مامون و محفوظ ہو جائے گا تعریف علم کے معلوم کرنے سے وہ علم مطلوب ممتاز عن سائر العلوم ہو جاتا ہے عند (الطالب ) لا فی نفسہ وفی حد ذاتہ اور موضہ ع کے ذریعہ سے وہ ممتاز ہو جائے گافی حد ذاتہ وفی نفسہ باقی علوم سے لہذا مقاصد سے پہلے علم کی تعریف اور موضوع کا جاننا ضروری ہے ورنہ طلب مجہول لازم آئے گا اور مقصود و غیر مقصود میں امتیاز نہ ہو سکے گا۔ سوال ! مقدمہ میں تو تین اشیاء کو بیان کیا جاتا ہے (۱) تعریف (۲) موضوع (۳) غرض و غایت شارح کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے تعریف اور موضوع کو ذکر کیا ہے غرض و غایت کو بیان نہیں کیا اس کی کیا وجہ ہے۔ جواب اغانیہ کی عموماً تعریف سے ہی معلوم ہو جاتی ہے یا موضوع سے یہاں پر بھی ایسا ہی ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کی تعریف ہے هو علم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه اى سے معلوم ہوا کہ غایت هذا العلم التوصل الی الفقہ ہے اسی بناء پر مصنف نے اس کو علیحدہ و مستقل ذکر نہیں فرمایا۔ فحين تشوقت نفس السامع غرض شارح تفتازانی توضیح متن ہے مصنف نے متن میں اصول الفقہ میں دوتر کیبی احتمال
The statement: 'The book of Usul al-Fiqh is arranged into a preface and two sections.' The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to explain the summary of the book Al-Tawdih, so he said that the entire book Al-Tawdih consists of one preface and two sections. Objection: The commentator's statement is against the author's statement because later the author himself will say 'and we divide the book into two sections.' So from the author's phrase it is understood that Al-Tawdih is arranged only into two sections, while the commentator's statement says Al-Tawdih is arranged into two sections and one preface, so there is conflict and contradiction. Answer (1): There is no contradiction between the author and commentator's statements because the commentator's intent is to explain the summary of the entire book of Al-Tawdih, whether it is from the purposes of the discipline or from the preliminaries of the discipline; while the author's intent in 'we divide the book into two sections' is only the purposes of the discipline, and that is arranged only into two sections, the preface is excluded. Answer (2): The author's statement is after the completion of the preface, and from here the book is arranged into two sections because the preface has already passed; and the commentator's statement includes the preface. From this perspective, the book Al-Tawdih includes the preface in addition to the two sections. Therefore, the statements of both great scholars are correct according to their respective contexts. Because 'that which is mentioned in it', the commentator Taftazani explains the reason for the limitation. The summary of the limitation is that whatever is mentioned in this book is either related to the purposes of the discipline or not (rather from the preliminaries). If it is not from the purposes, it is called the preface. If it is from the purposes of the discipline, then it is either discussing proofs or rulings. If it is about proofs, it is the first section; if about rulings, it is the second section, because in this discipline only these two things are discussed. And the first section is based on four pillars. The first section consists of four pillars: (1) the Book, (2) Sunnah, (3) Ijma', (4) Qiyas. And it is appended with two chapters: the chapter of Tarjih and Ijtihad. The commentator's purpose is to answer a presumed objection. Objection: It is said that your statement that the first section consists of four pillars is not correct; rather, in it there is a chapter on Tarjih between proofs and causes, and another chapter on Ijtihad, so these total six pillars, not four. Answer: The commentator replies that these two chapters are subsidiary; 'mudhayyal' is from 'dhayl', literal meaning skirt, intended meaning: to mention something by following. The purpose is that these two chapters are not independent but are subsidiary and dependent on Qiyas, and are part of its completion and introduction, so no problem. And the second section consists of three chapters: (1) Hukm, (2) Mahkum bih, (3) Mahkum alayh. The reason for their limitation will come soon. And the preface is delivered. The commentator Taftazani wants to show what matters will be explained in the preface. He says that in the preface two things will be mentioned: (1) the definition of the science of Usul al-Fiqh, (2) its subject matter. Because it is the right of the seeker of multiplicity that is regulated by one aspect... From here, the commentator Taftazani wants to explain why it is necessary to state the definition and subject in the preface and why it is necessary to know these two before the purposes. He says that the rule is: A person who is a seeker of multiplicity, i.e., wants to seek many things, and those many things are such that all of them are regulated by a single aspect, i.e., all things have a connection and relationship with one thing, and that thing is common among them all, then it is necessary for such a seeker of multiplicity that when he seeks those many things, at the time of seeking he must consider that aspect, and know that aspect before seeking the many things and acquire knowledge of it; otherwise there is a risk that he will miss the intended goal and become occupied with what is not intended, and he will not distinguish between intended and unintended. For example, a person is a seeker of religious students; religious students are many, but they are regulated by one aspect. Then it is necessary for that person to acquire knowledge of that single aspect. That single aspect would be the definition of those students: that a student is one who studies religion and is bearded, turbaned, and wears a cap, etc. After knowing this single aspect, that seeker of multiplicity will achieve his sought and intended, and will distinguish intended from unintended. If this aspect were not known, he could not distinguish intended from unintended, sought from unsought; instead of religious students, the seeker of multiplicity might think traders are religious students and become occupied in serving them, and thus miss the intended. When it is established that for a seeker of multiplicity it is necessary to acquire knowledge of the single aspect first, then it should also be known that every science consists of many issues, and those many issues are connected, regulated, and common in a single aspect, and that single aspect is the definition and subject of each science. Therefore, it is necessary for a student of knowledge to know its definition and subject before knowing the many issues of each science. In this way, he will be safe and secure from missing the intended and becoming occupied with what is not intended. By knowing the definition of the science, that desired science becomes distinguished from other sciences in the mind of the student (not in itself and in its essence); and by means of the subject, it will be distinguished in itself and in its essence from other sciences. Therefore, it is necessary to know the definition and subject of the science before the purposes, otherwise 'seeking the unknown' would be necessary, and there would be no distinction between intended and unintended. Objection: In the preface, three things are usually mentioned: (1) definition, (2) subject, (3) purpose and end. From the commentator's phrase, it appears that the author mentioned definition and subject, but did not state the purpose and end. What is the reason for this? Answer: The purpose and end are generally known from the definition or from the subject, and the same applies here because the definition of Usul al-Fiqh is 'it is knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at Fiqh', i.e., from this it is known that the end of this science is arriving at Fiqh. Based on this, the author did not mention it separately and independently. 'Then when the soul of the listener becomes eager' - the purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to explain the text of Al-Tawdih. The author in the text explained the two possibilities in Usul al-Fiqh.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an explanation (sharh) of the introductory section of Al-Tawdih. The commentator, Taftazani, begins by clarifying the overall structure of the book: it comprises a preface (muqaddimah) and two main sections (qismain). He notes an apparent contradiction: the author of the matn states 'we divide the book into two sections,' while Taftazani says it has a preface plus two sections. The commentator resolves this by explaining that the author's statement refers only to the core content after the preface, whereas Taftazani includes the preface in his description. Thus both are correct from their respective perspectives. 

The first section (Qism al-Awwal) is built upon four pillars (arkan): the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, Ijma' (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy). Additionally, it is appended (mudhayyal) with two chapters: one on Tarjih (preference between proofs) and one on Ijtihad. An objection is raised: why are these not considered additional pillars? The commentator responds that these chapters are subsidiary to Qiyas and not independent, hence they do not increase the number of pillars. The second section (Qism al-Thani) consists of three chapters: Hukm (ruling), Mahkum bih (that which is ruled upon), and Mahkum alayh (the subject of the ruling). 

The remainder of the passage explains why the preface includes the definition (ta'rif) and subject (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh. The commentator lays down a principle (dabitah): anyone who seeks to study a collection of items that share a common aspect must first understand that aspect, otherwise they risk confusing the target with unrelated items. For example, one seeking to identify students of religious knowledge must know their defining characteristics (e.g., studying religion, wearing a beard, turban, etc.). Similarly, every science has a definition and subject that distinguish it from other sciences; the definition distinguishes it in the mind of the student, while the subject distinguishes it objectively. Therefore, it is necessary to learn the definition and subject before delving into the detailed issues of the science. The commentator also addresses why the author did not separately mention the purpose (gharad/ghayah) of the science: because the purpose is inherent in the definition—Usul al-Fiqh is defined as 'knowledge of principles leading to Fiqh,' so the end goal is implicit. Thus, the preface adequately covers what is needed.

Key Terms
اصول الفقہ (usul al-fiqh): Knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at Fiqh.
مقدمہ (muqaddimah): The introductory part of the book covering definition and subject of the science.
قسم (qism): A major division of the book; first section on proofs, second section on rulings.
رکن (rukn): A fundamental pillar; the first section has four arkan: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas.
ذیل (dhayl): Something appended or subsidiary; in this context, the chapters on Tarjih and Ijtihad are dhayl to Qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many pillars does the first section of Al-Tawdih have?
A) 4
B) 6
C) 2
D) 3

Key Takeaway
Al-Tawdih is structured with a muqaddimah (definition and subject) and two sections: the first on proofs (four pillars plus appendices) and the second on rulings (three chapters).

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Necessity of Ta'rif and Mawdu' in Usul al-Fiqh Prefaces
Justifying the inclusion of definition and subject in the preface through a general principle and example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the principle that a seeker of multiplicity must know the common aspect first, and apply it to the inclusion of definition (ta'rif) and subject (mawdu') in a usul preface.

Core Idea
To avoid confusion, every science must begin with its definition and subject to distinguish it from other sciences.

This lesson uncovers the methodological justification for including the definition (ta'rif) and subject (mawdu') in the preface of a usul al-fiqh work. The commentator Taftazani articulates a general principle: a person seeking to learn a collection of items that share a single common aspect must first understand that aspect, otherwise they risk confusing the intended with the unintended. He illustrates this with the example of seeking religious students. This principle underscores why every science begins with a definition and subject, ensuring the student's focus and clarity. The lesson also addresses why the purpose (ghayah) of the science may be omitted if implied in the definition.

Guided Path
1
State the principle (dabitah) articulated by Taftazani
The commentator says: 'A seeker of multiplicity that is regulated by a single aspect must know that aspect first.' Understand what 'multiplicity' and 'single aspect' refer to in the context of studying a science.
The 'multiplicity' is the many issues of a science; the 'single aspect' is its definition and subject.
2
Understand the analogy with seeking religious students
Taftazani gives an example: one who seeks to identify religious students must first know their defining characteristics (studying religion, wearing a beard/turban). Without this, one might confuse students with traders.
This analogy makes the abstract principle concrete.
3
Apply the principle to the study of any science
Every science consists of many issues, but they are all unified by a common aspect: the definition of that science and its subject matter. A student must learn these first to correctly identify what belongs to the science.
Definition distinguishes the science in the mind of the student; subject distinguishes it objectively.
4
Differentiate the roles of definition and subject
Definition (ta'rif) makes the science distinct from other sciences in the student's mind (subjective distinction). Subject (mawdu') makes it distinct in itself (objective distinction). Both are necessary before studying the details.
Without both, the student may not know what falls under the science.
5
Address the omission of ghayah (purpose/end)
An objection is raised: why is ghayah not separately mentioned in the preface? The answer is that ghayah is implied in the definition. For Usul al-Fiqh, the definition 'knowledge of principles leading to Fiqh' already indicates the end is arriving at Fiqh.
This is an example of the Hanafi principle of conciseness (ikhtisar).

موضوع ہے لہذا طالب علم کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ ہر علم کے مسائل کثیرہ معلوم کرنے سے پہلے اس کی تعریف اور اس کا موضوع جان لے اس طرح وہ مقصود کے فوت ہونے اور غیر مقصود میں اشتعال سے مامون و محفوظ ہو جائے گا تعریف علم کے معلوم کرنے سے وہ علم مطلوب ممتاز عن سائر العلوم ہو جاتا ہے عند (الطالب ) لا فی نفسہ وفی حد ذاتہ اور موضہ ع کے ذریعہ سے وہ ممتاز ہو جائے گافی حد ذاتہ وفی نفسہ باقی علوم سے لہذا مقاصد سے پہلے علم کی تعریف اور موضوع کا جاننا ضروری ہے ورنہ طلب مجہول لازم آئے گا اور مقصود و غیر مقصود میں امتیاز نہ ہو سکے گا۔ سوال ! مقدمہ میں تو تین اشیاء کو بیان کیا جاتا ہے (۱) تعریف (۲) موضوع (۳) غرض و غایت شارح کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے تعریف اور موضوع کو ذکر کیا ہے غرض و غایت کو بیان نہیں کیا اس کی کیا وجہ ہے۔ جواب اغانیہ کی عموماً تعریف سے ہی معلوم ہو جاتی ہے یا موضوع سے یہاں پر بھی ایسا ہی ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کی تعریف ہے هو علم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه اى سے معلوم ہوا کہ غایت هذا العلم التوصل الی الفقہ ہے اسی بناء پر مصنف نے اس کو علیحدہ و مستقل ذکر نہیں فرمایا۔ فحين تشوقت نفس السامع غرض شارح تفتازانی توضیح متن ہے مصنف نے متن میں اصول الفقہ میں دوتر کیبی احتمال
The statement: 'The book of Usul al-Fiqh is arranged into a preface and two sections.' The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to explain the summary of the book Al-Tawdih, so he said that the entire book Al-Tawdih consists of one preface and two sections. Objection: The commentator's statement is against the author's statement because later the author himself will say 'and we divide the book into two sections.' So from the author's phrase it is understood that Al-Tawdih is arranged only into two sections, while the commentator's statement says Al-Tawdih is arranged into two sections and one preface, so there is conflict and contradiction. Answer (1): There is no contradiction between the author and commentator's statements because the commentator's intent is to explain the summary of the entire book of Al-Tawdih, whether it is from the purposes of the discipline or from the preliminaries of the discipline; while the author's intent in 'we divide the book into two sections' is only the purposes of the discipline, and that is arranged only into two sections, the preface is excluded. Answer (2): The author's statement is after the completion of the preface, and from here the book is arranged into two sections because the preface has already passed; and the commentator's statement includes the preface. From this perspective, the book Al-Tawdih includes the preface in addition to the two sections. Therefore, the statements of both great scholars are correct according to their respective contexts. Because 'that which is mentioned in it', the commentator Taftazani explains the reason for the limitation. The summary of the limitation is that whatever is mentioned in this book is either related to the purposes of the discipline or not (rather from the preliminaries). If it is not from the purposes, it is called the preface. If it is from the purposes of the discipline, then it is either discussing proofs or rulings. If it is about proofs, it is the first section; if about rulings, it is the second section, because in this discipline only these two things are discussed. And the first section is based on four pillars. The first section consists of four pillars: (1) the Book, (2) Sunnah, (3) Ijma', (4) Qiyas. And it is appended with two chapters: the chapter of Tarjih and Ijtihad. The commentator's purpose is to answer a presumed objection. Objection: It is said that your statement that the first section consists of four pillars is not correct; rather, in it there is a chapter on Tarjih between proofs and causes, and another chapter on Ijtihad, so these total six pillars, not four. Answer: The commentator replies that these two chapters are subsidiary; 'mudhayyal' is from 'dhayl', literal meaning skirt, intended meaning: to mention something by following. The purpose is that these two chapters are not independent but are subsidiary and dependent on Qiyas, and are part of its completion and introduction, so no problem. And the second section consists of three chapters: (1) Hukm, (2) Mahkum bih, (3) Mahkum alayh. The reason for their limitation will come soon. And the preface is delivered. The commentator Taftazani wants to show what matters will be explained in the preface. He says that in the preface two things will be mentioned: (1) the definition of the science of Usul al-Fiqh, (2) its subject matter. Because it is the right of the seeker of multiplicity that is regulated by one aspect... From here, the commentator Taftazani wants to explain why it is necessary to state the definition and subject in the preface and why it is necessary to know these two before the purposes. He says that the rule is: A person who is a seeker of multiplicity, i.e., wants to seek many things, and those many things are such that all of them are regulated by a single aspect, i.e., all things have a connection and relationship with one thing, and that thing is common among them all, then it is necessary for such a seeker of multiplicity that when he seeks those many things, at the time of seeking he must consider that aspect, and know that aspect before seeking the many things and acquire knowledge of it; otherwise there is a risk that he will miss the intended goal and become occupied with what is not intended, and he will not distinguish between intended and unintended. For example, a person is a seeker of religious students; religious students are many, but they are regulated by one aspect. Then it is necessary for that person to acquire knowledge of that single aspect. That single aspect would be the definition of those students: that a student is one who studies religion and is bearded, turbaned, and wears a cap, etc. After knowing this single aspect, that seeker of multiplicity will achieve his sought and intended, and will distinguish intended from unintended. If this aspect were not known, he could not distinguish intended from unintended, sought from unsought; instead of religious students, the seeker of multiplicity might think traders are religious students and become occupied in serving them, and thus miss the intended. When it is established that for a seeker of multiplicity it is necessary to acquire knowledge of the single aspect first, then it should also be known that every science consists of many issues, and those many issues are connected, regulated, and common in a single aspect, and that single aspect is the definition and subject of each science. Therefore, it is necessary for a student of knowledge to know its definition and subject before knowing the many issues of each science. In this way, he will be safe and secure from missing the intended and becoming occupied with what is not intended. By knowing the definition of the science, that desired science becomes distinguished from other sciences in the mind of the student (not in itself and in its essence); and by means of the subject, it will be distinguished in itself and in its essence from other sciences. Therefore, it is necessary to know the definition and subject of the science before the purposes, otherwise 'seeking the unknown' would be necessary, and there would be no distinction between intended and unintended. Objection: In the preface, three things are usually mentioned: (1) definition, (2) subject, (3) purpose and end. From the commentator's phrase, it appears that the author mentioned definition and subject, but did not state the purpose and end. What is the reason for this? Answer: The purpose and end are generally known from the definition or from the subject, and the same applies here because the definition of Usul al-Fiqh is 'it is knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at Fiqh', i.e., from this it is known that the end of this science is arriving at Fiqh. Based on this, the author did not mention it separately and independently. 'Then when the soul of the listener becomes eager' - the purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to explain the text of Al-Tawdih. The author in the text explained the two possibilities in Usul al-Fiqh.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an explanation (sharh) of the introductory section of Al-Tawdih. The commentator, Taftazani, begins by clarifying the overall structure of the book: it comprises a preface (muqaddimah) and two main sections (qismain). He notes an apparent contradiction: the author of the matn states 'we divide the book into two sections,' while Taftazani says it has a preface plus two sections. The commentator resolves this by explaining that the author's statement refers only to the core content after the preface, whereas Taftazani includes the preface in his description. Thus both are correct from their respective perspectives. 

The first section (Qism al-Awwal) is built upon four pillars (arkan): the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, Ijma' (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy). Additionally, it is appended (mudhayyal) with two chapters: one on Tarjih (preference between proofs) and one on Ijtihad. An objection is raised: why are these not considered additional pillars? The commentator responds that these chapters are subsidiary to Qiyas and not independent, hence they do not increase the number of pillars. The second section (Qism al-Thani) consists of three chapters: Hukm (ruling), Mahkum bih (that which is ruled upon), and Mahkum alayh (the subject of the ruling). 

The remainder of the passage explains why the preface includes the definition (ta'rif) and subject (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh. The commentator lays down a principle (dabitah): anyone who seeks to study a collection of items that share a common aspect must first understand that aspect, otherwise they risk confusing the target with unrelated items. For example, one seeking to identify students of religious knowledge must know their defining characteristics (e.g., studying religion, wearing a beard, turban, etc.). Similarly, every science has a definition and subject that distinguish it from other sciences; the definition distinguishes it in the mind of the student, while the subject distinguishes it objectively. Therefore, it is necessary to learn the definition and subject before delving into the detailed issues of the science. The commentator also addresses why the author did not separately mention the purpose (gharad/ghayah) of the science: because the purpose is inherent in the definition—Usul al-Fiqh is defined as 'knowledge of principles leading to Fiqh,' so the end goal is implicit. Thus, the preface adequately covers what is needed.

Key Terms
تعریف (ta'rif): The definition of a science that distinguishes it from other sciences in the mind of the student.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science that distinguishes it objectively from other sciences.
غرض/غایت (gharad / ghayah): The purpose or end goal of studying a science; in Usul al-Fiqh, it is to derive Fiqh rulings.
ضابطہ (dabitah): A rule or principle; here, the principle that a seeker of multiplicity must first know the common aspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it necessary to know the definition and subject of a science before studying its issues?
A) To memorize them easily
B) To avoid wasting time
C) To distinguish the science from others and avoid confusion
D) To impress one's teachers

Key Takeaway
Every science's muqaddimah must state its definition and subject to guide the seeker of knowledge and prevent confusion; the purpose can be inferred from the definition.
